Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Catching One Rak'ah of Zuhr with Congregation: Legal Reality vs. Reward
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the effect of catching one rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the legal reality of congregational prayer from the reward (fadl) when catching only one rak'ah, and apply this distinction to oath rulings.

Core Idea
Catching one rak'ah gives reward but not the legal status of congregational prayer.

When you join the congregation late and catch only the last rak'ah, have you prayed with the congregation? The Hanafi school makes a subtle but crucial distinction: you have not performed the prayer in congregation in a legal sense, but you have attained the virtue and reward. This distinction has practical consequences, especially in matters of oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person joins the Zuhr congregation after the imam has already prayed three rak'ahs, so he catches only the fourth rak'ah with the imam.
This is a specific case of idrak al-jama'ah with one rak'ah.
2
State the majority Hanafi ruling
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that he has not prayed Zuhr with congregation (lam yusalli al-zuhr bi-jama'ah). The prayer is not considered congregational; he must complete the missed rak'ahs alone.
This is the default ruling from the matn.
3
Analyze Imam Muhammad's view
Imam Muhammad adds that he has attained the virtue of congregation (fadl al-jama'ah) because 'whoever catches the last part of something has caught it.' This is a qiyas (analogy) based on a general principle.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. Imam Muhammad does not contradict the legal reality but supplements it regarding reward.
4
Apply the dispute to oaths
If someone swears 'I will not catch the congregation' (la udrik al-jama'ah), catching one rak'ah breaks the oath because he attained the virtue. If he swears 'I will not pray Zuhr with the congregation' (la usalli al-zuhr bi-jama'ah), catching one rak'ah does not break the oath because he did not actually pray the full prayer with them.
This thamarah (practical consequence) shows the legal difference between idrak (catching) and salat bi-jama'ah (praying with congregation).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ادرك من الظهر ركعة ولم يدرك الثلاث، فانه لم يصل الظهر بجماعة. وقال محمد: قد ادرك فضل الجماعة، لان من ادرك آخر الشيء فقد ادر كه فصار محرزا ثواب الجماعة، لكنه لم يصلها بالجماعة حقيقة، ولهذا يحنث به في يمينه لايدرك الجماعة، ولا يحنث في يمينه لا يصلي الظهر بالجماعة
رجمہ اور جس نے ظہر کی ایک رکعت پائی اور تین کو نہیں پایا تو اس نے ظہر کو جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھا۔ اور امام محمد نے کہا کہ اس نے جماعت کی فضیلت کو پالیا۔ کیونکہ جس نے کسی چیز کو آکر کو پالیا اس نے اس چیز کو پالیا۔ پس وہ جماعت کے ثواب کو حاصل کرنے والا ہو گیا لیکن ظہر کو حقیقتہ جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھا ہے۔ اور اسی وجہ سے اتنی مقدار سے اپنی قسم (لا یدرک الجماعت ، جماعت کو نہیں پائے گا میں حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور اپنی قسم لا يصلى الظهر بالجماعة (ظہر کو جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھے گا ) میں حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے رباعی نماز کی ایک رکعت کو امام کے ساتھ پایا اور تین رکعات کو نہیں پایا تو یہ کہا جائے گا کہ اس نے جماعت کے ساتھ نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے۔ امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ فضیلت جماعت کو پالیا۔ متن میں امام محمد کی تخصیص یو نہی کر دی گئی ہے۔ ورنہ یہ حکم احناف کا متفق علیہ ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس نے کسی چیز کا آخری جز پالیا تو اس نے اس چیز ہی کو پالیا۔ لہذا یہ شخص فضیلت جماعت کو حاصل کرنے والا ہو گیا۔ البتہ حقیقتہ اس نماز کو جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ بخدا میں جماعت کو نہیں پاؤں گا۔ پھر ایک رکعت جماعت کے ساتھ مل گئی تو یہ شخص حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے فضیلت جماعت کو پالیا ہے اور اگر یہ تم مانی که والله لا يصلى الظهر بالجماعة بخدا میں ظہر کو جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھوں گا۔ پھر اس کو ایک رکعت اما کے ساتھ یل
And if someone catches one rak'ah of Zuhr but does not catch the three, he has not prayed Zuhr with congregation. Muhammad said: He has attained the virtue of congregation, because whoever catches the last part of a thing has caught that thing. So he becomes one who has obtained the reward of congregation, but he has not actually prayed it with congregation. For this reason, he would be guilty of breaking his oath if he swore 'I will not catch the congregation', but he would not be guilty if he swore 'I will not pray Zuhr with congregation'.
Translation: And if someone catches one rak'ah of Zuhr and does not catch the three, it is said that he has not prayed Zuhr with congregation. Imam Muhammad said that he has attained the virtue of congregation. Because whoever catches the end part of something has caught that something. So this person becomes one who obtains the reward of congregation. However, in reality he has not prayed this prayer with congregation. This is why if someone takes an oath: 'By Allah, I will not catch the congregation', then if he catches one rak'ah with the congregation, he becomes an oath-breaker because he has obtained the virtue of congregation. But if he swears 'By Allah, I will not pray Zuhr with congregation', and he catches one rak'ah with the imam, he does not become an oath-breaker.
Explanation: The issue is that if someone catches one rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer with the imam and does not catch the remaining three, it will be said that he has not prayed with the congregation. Imam Muhammad said that he has attained the virtue of congregation. In the text, this is specified as Imam Muhammad's view, but otherwise the ruling is agreed upon by the Hanafis. The proof is: whoever catches the last part of something has caught that thing. So this person becomes one who obtains the virtue of congregation. However, in reality he has not prayed that prayer with congregation. This is why if someone takes an oath: 'By Allah, I will not catch the congregation', then if he joins for one rak'ah, he becomes an oath-breaker because he attained the virtue of congregation. And if he takes an oath: 'By Allah, I will not pray Zuhr with congregation', then if he catches one rak'ah with the imam, he does not become an oath-breaker.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific situation: a person joins the Zuhr congregation after the imam has already prayed three rak'ahs, so he catches only the fourth rak'ah with the imam. The ruling is that he has not actually prayed Zuhr with the congregation because he missed most of the prayer with them. However, Imam Muhammad adds that he has attained the virtue (fadl) of congregation because he caught the last part of the prayer with them. The proof is a qiyas (analogy): whoever catches the last part of something has caught the whole thing for certain purposes. This has practical implications for oaths. If someone swears that he will not 'catch' (idrak) the congregation, and then he catches just one rak'ah, he breaks his oath because he has caught the virtue. But if he swears that he will not 'pray Zuhr with the congregation', and he catches one rak'ah, he does not break his oath because he did not actually pray the full prayer with them. The passage highlights the distinction between actual congregational prayer (hukman haqiqi) and attaining the virtue (fadl).

Key Terms
ادراك الجماعة (idrak al-jama'ah): Catching the congregation means joining the imam at any point during the prayer such that one prays at least one rak'ah with him.
فضل الجماعة (fadl al-jama'ah): The virtue or reward of praying in congregation, as opposed to the legal ruling of having performed the prayer with the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person swears, 'By Allah, I will not pray Zuhr with the congregation,' and then catches only the fourth rak'ah with the imam, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) He breaks his oath because he caught one rak'ah
B) He does not break his oath because he did not pray the full Zuhr with the congregation
C) He breaks his oath if he completes the prayer with the imam
D) oaths about prayer are not taken seriously

Key Takeaway
Catching one rak'ah with the congregation gives the reward but not the legal status of congregational prayer; this distinction is critical for oaths and other rulings.

Ruling on Making Up the Sunnah of Fajr and Other Sunnahs
Ruling on qada of sunnah prayers in subordination to fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the sunnah of Fajr and other sunnah prayers, and distinguish between the preferred view and differing opinions within the school.

Core Idea
Only the Sunnah of Fajr is made up, and only before noon (zawal) in subordination to its fard.

This lesson addresses a common practical scenario: what to do when you miss both the fard and sunnah of Fajr. The Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's practice, allows making up the Fajr sunnah only in subordination to its fard and only before zawal. For other sunnah prayers, qada is generally not performed. We will examine the evidence, the time limit, and the scholarly differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon – here, qada (make-up) of sunnah prayers. State the general ruling: only the Fajr sunnah is made up, and only in subordination to its fard.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's action (peace be upon him): he made up the sunnah of Fajr after its time in subordination to the fard. This is a sunnah ahad proof.
The passage does not quote a specific hadith text but refers to the known practice.
3
Note the time limit (zawal)
The passage states that qada of the Fajr sunnah is only allowed before zawal (noon). After zawal, there is disagreement.
Zawal is when the sun passes its zenith.
4
Identify the ikhtilaf after zawal
Some scholars allow making up the Fajr sunnah after zawal in subordination; the preferred view (mufta bihi) is not to do so, as the Prophet did not do it.
The tarjih authority is Al-Hidayah.
5
Evaluate the ruling for other sunnahs
For sunnahs other than Fajr, qada is not performed alone after the time. Whether they can be made up in subordination to fard is disputed; the correct view (al-sahih) is no, because qada is specific to wajib.
Some mashayikh argued implicit establishment (ضمناً ثابت) but the majority rejected it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ادراك الفريضة مینی چونکہ فجر کی فرض نماز بھی فوت ہوگی تھی اس لئے جب آپ نے فرض کی قضاء کی تو اس کی تبعیت میں سنت کی بھی قضاء فرمائی۔ لہذا اس کے علاوہ اصل پر باقی رہے گا یعنی اس صورت کے علاوہ میں قضاء نہیں کی جائے گی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ سنت فجر کی قضاء فرض کے تابع ہو کر کی جائے گی یعنی اگر صبح کی فرض نماز کی قضاء کرتا ہے تو سنت فجر کی قضاء بھی کرے صبح کی فرض نماز خواہ جماعت کے ساتھ قضاء کرے یا تنہا قضاء کرے۔ یہ بات یادر ہے کہ سنت فجر کی قضاء فرض کے تابع ہو کر فقط زوال تک کی جاسکتی ہے لیکن اگر سورج ڈھل گیا اور ابھی تک قضاء کی نہیں تو اس میں اختلاف ہے بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ زوال کے بعد سنت فجر کی قضاء نہیں کی جائے گی اگر چہ فرض کے تابع ہو کر ہی ہو ۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے زوال سے پہلے پہلے تابع فرض ہو کر سنت فجر کی قضاء کی ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ زوال کے بعد بھی تبع للفرض سنت فجر کی قضاء کر سکتا ہے۔ رہی دوسری سنتیں ، سنت فجر کے علاوہ تو ان کے بارے میں حکم یہ ہے کہ وقت کے بعد تنہاسنتوں کی قضاء نہیں کی جائے گی لیکن فرض کے تابع ہو کر قضاء کی جاسکتی ہے یا نہیں تو اس بارے میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے بعض نے کہا ہے کہ قضاء کرے کیونکہ بہت سی چیزیں ضمنا ثابت ہو جاتی ہیں اگر چہ قصد آثابت نہیں ہوتیں۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ قضاء نہ کرے کیونکہ قضاء واجب کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ یہی صحیح قول ہے۔
Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer. Because the Fajr fard prayer was also missed, when he made up the fard, he also made up the sunnah in its subordination. Therefore, other than this, it remains on the original principle, i.e., qada is not performed except in this case. The author of Al-Hidayah said: The qada of the sunnah of Fajr is performed in subordination to the fard, meaning if one makes up the fajr fard prayer, he should also make up the sunnah of Fajr, whether he makes up the fard with congregation or alone. It is remembered that the qada of the sunnah of Fajr in subordination to the fard can only be done until zawal (noon). But if the sun has declined and qada has not yet been performed, there is disagreement: Some scholars said that after zawal, the qada of the sunnah of Fajr is not performed even in subordination to the fard, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made up the sunnah of Fajr in subordination to the fard before zawal. And some scholars said that after zawal as well, one can make up the sunnah of Fajr in subordination to the fard. As for other sunnahs besides the sunnah of Fajr, the ruling is that after the time, the qada of sunnahs alone is not performed. But can they be performed in subordination to the fard? Regarding this, the mashayikh differ: Some said to perform qada because many things become established implicitly even if not intended explicitly. Others said not to perform qada because qada is specific to obligatory (wajib). This is the correct saying.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the qada (make-up) of sunnah prayers, particularly the sunnah of Fajr, in relation to the fard prayer. The discussion follows the Hanafi school as expounded in Al-Hidayah. The passage clarifies that the sunnah of Fajr is made up only in subordination to its fard, based on the Prophet's action. There is a disagreement among scholars about whether this can be done after zawal. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that qada of the Fajr sunnah after zawal is not performed, even in subordination to the fard, because the Prophet did not do so. For other sunnah prayers, the ruling is that they are not made up alone after their time; but whether they can be made up in subordination to the fard is a point of ikhtilaf among the mashayikh. The text concludes that the correct view (al-sahih) is not to make them up, because qada is specifically for wajib acts, not sunnah.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah prayed before the Fajr fard prayer.
زوال (zawal): The time when the sun passes its zenith, i.e., noon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Hidayah, when can the sunnah of Fajr be made up?
A) At any time before the next obligatory prayer
B) Only before zawal (noon), in subordination to its fard
C) Only during the same day after zawal
D) It is never made up

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: the sunnah of Fajr is made up only before noon and only in subordination to its fard; other sunnahs are not made up at all.

Performing Nafl Before Fard When Time is Limited
Ruling on performing voluntary prayers before fard when time is limited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on whether to perform sunnah prayers before fard when time is limited, and state the preferred view from Al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
Fard takes precedence; sunnah can be performed if time allows, but stressed sunnahs of Fajr and Zuhr are highly recommended.

You enter a mosque where the congregation has already finished. You intend to pray the fard alone. Should you pray the sunnah first? The answer depends on remaining time and which sunnahs are involved. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling based on the principle of muwazabah (the Prophet's consistent practice) and the hadiths emphasizing the sunnahs of Fajr and Zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage addresses a person who enters a mosque where the fard prayer has already been performed, or who intends to pray at home alone. Determine whether time is ample or tight.
2
Distinguish between ample and tight time
The general ruling: if there is ample time (sa'at al-waqt), one may perform sunnah/nafl before the fard. If time is tight (dhiq), one should leave the nafl and pray fard first to avoid missing it.
The fard is the primary obligation; time constraint triggers prioritization.
3
Recognize the dispute over stressed sunnahs
Two opinions are presented: one exempts the sunnahs of Fajr and Zuhr from the general ruling due to strong hadiths; the other applies the ruling to all sunnahs based on muwazabah (the Prophet's consistent practice when praying with congregation).
4
Understand the concept of muwazabah
Muwazabah is the Prophet's consistent practice of an act. According to the second opinion, since the Prophet only performed these sunnahs when praying fard with congregation, for a person praying alone they become nafl (optional) and may be omitted when time is tight.
5
Apply the preferred view (al-ula)
Al-Hidayah states that the better course (al-ula) is not to leave these sunnahs in any situation because they complete the fard, except when one fears the fard time will expire.
The mufta bihi is to preserve the sunnahs unless absolutely necessary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اتي مسجدا قد صلى فيه، فلا بأس بان يتطوع قبل المكتوبة ما بدأ له مادام في الوقت، ومراده إذا كان في الوقت سعة، وان كان فيه ضيق تركه قيل هذا فى غير سنة الظهر والفجر ، لان لهما زيادة مزية، قال عيله السلام فى سنة الفجر: صلوها ولوطردتكم الخيل، وقال فى الاخرى من ترك الاربع قبل الظهر لم تنله شفاعتی، وقيل هذا فى الجميع ، لانه عليه السلام واظب عليها عند أداء المكتوبات بالجماعة، ولا سنة دون المواظبة، والأولى ان لا يتركها فى الاحوال كلها، لكونها مكملات للفرائض الا اذا خاف فوت الوقت ترجمہ جو شخص ایسی مسجد میں آیا کہ اس میں نماز ہو چکی تھی تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ فرض سے پہلے وہ نفل پڑھے۔ جس قدر جی چاہے جب تک وقت میں گنجائش ہے اور مراد نام محمد کی یہ ہے کہ جب تک وقت میں گنجائش ہے اور اگر وقت میں تنگی ہو تو فل چھوڑ دے۔ کہا گیا یہ حکم سنت ظہر اور سنت فجر کے علاوہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ سنت ظہر اور فجر کے واسطے زیادتی فضیلت ہے۔ فجر کی سنت کے بارے میں حضور نے فرمایا کہ اس کو پڑھوا گر چہ گھوڑے تم کو روند ڈالیں۔ اور سنت ظہر کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ جس نے ظہر سے پہلے کی چار رکعت چھوڑ دی اس کو میری شفاعت نصیب نہیں ہوگی۔ اور کہا گیا کہ یہ حکم سب سنتوں میں ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جماعت کے ساتھ فرائض ادا کرے کے وقت ان سنتوں پر مواظبت فرمائی ہے۔ اور بغیر مواظبت کے سنت ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ اور اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ان سنتوں کو تمام احوال میں نہ چھوڑے کیونکہ یہ منتیں فرائض کی تکمیل کرنے والی ہیں ،مگر جبکہ وقت کے فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کی جماعت فوت ہوگئی اور وہ ایسی مسجد میں آیا جس میں جماعت ہو چکی ہے یا گھر میں فرض نماز پڑھنے کا ارادہ کیا ہو تو اس بارے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے کہ وہ فرض ادا کرنے سے پہلے جس قدر چاہے سفن اور نوافل ادا کرے بشر طیکہ وقت میں گنجائش ہو۔ اور اگر وقت تنگ ہو تو پہلے فرض نماز پڑھے تا کہ فرض اپنے وقت سے فوت نہ ہو جائے ۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ تنگی وقت کی صورت میں سنن اور نوافل کے ترک کرنے کا حکم ظہر اور فجر کی سنتوں کے علاوہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ ظہر اور فجر کی سنتوں کو دیگر سنتوں کے مقابلے میں زیادہ فضیلت ہے۔ اس لئے تنگی وقت کے باوجود ان کو ضرور پڑھے۔ ہاں اگر وقت بالکل تنگ ہو گیا اور فرض کے علاوہ کی قطعاً گنجائش نہیں رہی تو ایسی نازک صورت میں ظہر اور فجر کی سنتوں کو بھی چھوڑا جا سکتا ہے۔ سنت فجر کی تاکید میں قال النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم صلوها ولو طردتكم الخیل ہے اور ظہر کی سنت کی تاکید میں من تركب الاربع قبل الظهر لم تنله شفاعتی ہے۔ بعض نے کہا کہ تنگی وقت کی صورت میں سنن کو ترک کرنے کا حکم تمام سنتوں میں ہے خواہ ظہر اور فجر کی ہوں خواہ اس کے علاوہ ہوں ۔ کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سنتوں پر مواظبت اس وقت فرمائی جبکہ آپ فرائض جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کرتے تھے اور جب فرائض کو تنہا پڑھاتو آپ نے ان سنتوں پر مواظبت نہیں فرمائی اور بغیر مواظبت کے سنت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ہے لہذا منفرد کے حق میں یہ نمازیں سنت نہ ہوں گی بلکا نیل ہوں گی اور نفل میں اختیار ہے کہ پڑھے یا نہ پڑھے اس لئے کہا گیا کہ نہ پڑھنے کا حکم تمام سنتوں میں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ان سنتوں کو کسی حال میں نہ چھوڑے وقت میں تنگی ہو یا وسعت ہو فرض نماز جماعت کے
Whoever comes to a mosque in which the prayer has already been performed, there is no harm that he performs voluntary prayers before the obligatory as much as he wishes as long as there is ample time. His intent is when there is ample time; if there is constriction, he leaves it. It is said this is except for the sunnahs of Zuhr and Fajr, because they have additional merit. He (peace be upon him) said regarding the sunnah of Fajr: 'Pray them even if horses trample you.' And regarding the other (Zuhr sunnah): 'Whoever leaves the four before Zuhr, my intercession will not reach him.' And it is said this applies to all, because he (peace be upon him) persisted upon them when performing obligatory prayers with congregation, and there is no sunnah without persistence. The preferred view is not to leave them in any situation because they complete the obligatory prayers, except when one fears the time will expire. (Urdu translation and explanation follow.)
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for a person who enters a mosque where the fard prayer has already been performed, or who intends to pray at home. The general ruling is that it is permissible to perform sunnah and nafl prayers before the fard as long as there is ample time. If time is limited, one should first perform the fard. There is a difference of opinion regarding the stressed sunnahs of Fajr and Zuhr. Some scholars hold that these sunnahs should be performed even when time is tight, because of the strong hadiths encouraging them. Others hold that the ruling applies to all sunnahs because the Prophet persisted on them only when praying fard with congregation; when praying alone, he did not persist, so for a person praying alone, these prayers become nafl (optional) and can be omitted. The author of Al-Hidayah prefers the view that one should not leave these sunnahs in any situation, as they complete the fard, unless one fears the time for fard will expire.

Key Terms
مواظبة (muwazabah): Consistent and regular practice of an act by the Prophet, which makes it a sunnah.
سعة الوقت (sa'at al-waqt): Ample time within the prayer time to perform both sunnah and fard without fear of missing the fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in Al-Hidayah, what should a person do if he enters a mosque where fard has been prayed and the remaining time is sufficient for both sunnah and fard?
A) Perform only the fard and leave the sunnah
B) Perform the sunnah before the fard
C) Perform the fard before the sunnah
D) Leave the mosque

Key Takeaway
When time is ample, sunnah can precede fard; when time is tight, fard takes precedence, but the stressed sunnahs of Fajr and Zuhr are only omitted if absolutely necessary.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Performing Sunan Before Fard When Time is Short
Ruling and preference on sunan before fard when time is short

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing sunan before fard when time is short, and apply the preferred (awla) view in different scenarios of time availability.

Core Idea
Sunnah prayers before fard are not abandoned unless time is extremely tight.

Imagine you arrive at the mosque just after the congregation has finished. You have time for the sunan prayer before fard, but you are not sure if you should pray them or skip to catch the fard on time. This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses that exact scenario: it is permissible to pray nawafil before fard when time permits, but if time is narrow, you should leave them. However, there is a significant difference of opinion regarding the emphasized sunan of Zuhr and Fajr, backed by strong hadith. The preferred view is to maintain these sunan in all situations unless you fear losing the fard time entirely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The ruling applies when a person misses the congregational prayer and either goes to a mosque where prayer has already been performed, or intends to pray alone at home. The basic ruling is that one may pray nawafil before fard as long as there is time.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Two positions are presented: one excludes the sunan of Zuhr and Fajr from the ruling of leaving them in narrow time due to their special merit; the other includes all sunan, arguing that the Prophet's consistency (muwazabah) was only during congregation.
The second position reduces these prayers to nafl when alone.
3
Examine the proofs
For Zuhr and Fajr, strong hadith emphasize their value: 'Pray the Fajr sunnah even if horses trample you' and 'Whoever leaves four rak'ahs before Zuhr will not attain my intercession.' These indicate that these sunan should not be easily abandoned.
The hadith are quoted in the matn.
4
Understand the role of muwazabah
The second position argues that sunnah status depends on the Prophet's consistency. Since he performed these prayers consistently only when praying fard in congregation, they are not sunnah for the individual praying alone, only nafl.
This is a key point: muwazabah is a condition for sunnah in Hanafi usul.
5
Apply the preferred view (awla)
The author of Hidayah states that the best is not to leave these sunan in any situation, because they complete the fard prayers and the righteous predecessors acted accordingly. The only exception is when one fears the fard time will expire.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ادراك الفريضة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
گئی ہے تو شخص حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حقیقتہ اس نے جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ظہر نہیں پڑھی ہے۔ جس مسجد میں فرض نماز ہو چکی پھر کوئی آیا وہ نوافل فرائض سے پہلے پڑھ سکتا ہے یا نہیں
ومن اتي مسجدا قد صلى فيه، فلا بأس بان يتطوع قبل المكتوبة ما بدأ له مادام في الوقت، ومراده إذا كان في الوقت سعة، وان كان فيه ضيق تركه قيل هذا فى غير سنة الظهر والفجر ، لان لهما زيادة مزية، قال عيله السلام فى سنة الفجر: صلوها ولوطردتكم الخيل، وقال فى الاخرى من ترك الاربع قبل الظهر لم تنله شفاعتی، وقيل هذا فى الجميع ، لانه عليه السلام واظب عليها عند أداء المكتوبات بالجماعة، ولا سنة دون المواظبة، والأولى ان لا يتركها فى الاحوال كلها، لكونها مكملات للفرائض الا اذا خاف فوت الوقت
ترجمہ جو شخص ایسی مسجد میں آیا کہ اس میں نماز ہو چکی تھی تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں کہ فرض سے پہلے وہ نفل پڑھے۔ جس قدر جی چاہے جب تک وقت میں گنجائش ہے اور مراد نام محمد کی یہ ہے کہ جب تک وقت میں گنجائش ہے اور اگر وقت میں تنگی ہو تو فل چھوڑ دے۔ کہا گیا یہ حکم سنت ظہر اور سنت فجر کے علاوہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ سنت ظہر اور فجر کے واسطے زیادتی فضیلت ہے۔ فجر کی سنت کے بارے میں حضور نے فرمایا کہ اس کو پڑھوا گر چہ گھوڑے تم کو روند ڈالیں۔ اور سنت ظہر کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ جس نے ظہر سے پہلے کی چار رکعت چھوڑ دی اس کو میری شفاعت نصیب نہیں ہوگی۔ اور کہا گیا کہ یہ حکم سب سنتوں میں ہے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے جماعت کے ساتھ فرائض ادا کرے کے وقت ان سنتوں پر مواظبت فرمائی ہے۔ اور بغیر مواظبت کے سنت ثابت نہیں ہوتی۔ اور اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ان سنتوں کو تمام احوال میں نہ چھوڑے کیونکہ یہ منتیں فرائض کی تکمیل کرنے والی ہیں ،مگر جبکہ وقت کے فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص کی جماعت فوت ہوگئی اور وہ ایسی مسجد میں آیا جس میں جماعت ہو چکی ہے یا گھر میں فرض نماز پڑھنے کا ارادہ کیا ہو تو اس بارے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے کہ وہ فرض ادا کرنے سے پہلے جس قدر چاہے سفن اور نوافل ادا کرے بشر طیکہ وقت میں گنجائش ہو۔ اور اگر وقت تنگ ہو تو پہلے فرض نماز پڑھے تا کہ فرض اپنے وقت سے فوت نہ ہو جائے ۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ تنگی وقت کی صورت میں سنن اور نوافل کے ترک کرنے کا حکم ظہر اور فجر کی سنتوں کے علاوہ میں ہے۔ کیونکہ ظہر اور فجر کی سنتوں کو دیگر سنتوں کے مقابلے میں زیادہ فضیلت ہے۔ اس لئے تنگی وقت کے باوجود ان کو ضرور پڑھے۔ ہاں اگر وقت بالکل تنگ ہو گیا اور فرض کے علاوہ کی قطعاً گنجائش نہیں رہی تو ایسی نازک صورت میں ظہر اور فجر کی سنتوں کو بھی چھوڑا جا سکتا ہے۔ سنت فجر کی تاکید میں قال النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم
صلوها ولو طردتكم الخیل ہے اور ظہر کی سنت کی تاکید میں من تركب الاربع قبل الظهر لم تنله شفاعتی ہے۔ بعض نے کہا کہ تنگی وقت کی صورت میں سنن کو ترک کرنے کا حکم تمام سنتوں میں ہے خواہ ظہر اور فجر کی ہوں خواہ اس کے علاوہ ہوں ۔ کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سنتوں پر مواظبت اس وقت فرمائی جبکہ آپ فرائض جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کرتے تھے اور جب فرائض کو تنہا پڑھاتو آپ نے ان سنتوں پر مواظبت نہیں فرمائی اور بغیر مواظبت کے سنت ثابت نہیں ہوتی ہے لہذا منفرد کے حق میں یہ نمازیں سنت نہ ہوں گی بلکا نیل ہوں گی اور نفل میں اختیار ہے کہ پڑھے یا نہ پڑھے اس لئے کہا گیا کہ نہ پڑھنے کا حکم تمام سنتوں میں ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ان سنتوں کو کسی حال میں نہ چھوڑے وقت میں تنگی ہو یا وسعت ہو فرض نماز جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھے یا تنہا پڑھے خواہ مقیم ہو یا مسافر ہو کیونکہ سفن فرائض کی تکمیل کرنے والی ہیں لہذا فرائض کا ثواب مکمل کرنے کی خاطر ان کو کسی حال میں ترک نہ کرے۔ نیز خلفاء راشدین، کبار صحابہ اور تابعین نے بھی اسی پر عمل کیا ہے کہ سنتوں کو کسی حال میں ترک نہیں فرمایا۔ ہاں البتہ اگر وقت کے فوت ہونے کا خوف ہو تو سنتوں کو ترک کر دے اور فرائض ادا کرے۔ (عنایه)
Whoever comes to a mosque in which the prayer has already been performed, there is no harm if he performs voluntary prayers before the obligatory prayer as much as he wishes, as long as there is slack in the time. If the time is narrow, he should leave them. It is said this applies to other than the sunnah of Zuhr and Fajr, because they have additional merit. The Prophet ﷺ said regarding the sunnah of Fajr: 'Pray them even if horses trample you.' And regarding the other: 'Whoever leaves the four rak'ahs before Zuhr, my intercession will not reach him.' And it is said this applies to all sunnah, because the Prophet ﷺ consistently performed them when performing the obligatory prayers in congregation, and there is no sunnah without consistency. The best is not to leave them in any situation, because they complete the obligatory prayers, unless one fears that the time will expire. [Then Urdu commentary elaborates that it is permissible to pray nawafil before fard as long as there is time; if time is narrow, one should prioritize fard. There is a difference of opinion: some say the ruling applies to all sunan except Zuhr and Fajr due to their virtue; others say it applies to all because the Prophet only maintained consistency in congregation, not alone. The author of Hidayah states that the best is not to leave them in any case, following the practice of the righteous predecessors, except when fearing loss of time.]
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on performing voluntary prayers (sunan/nawafil) before the obligatory prayer when one arrives in a mosque where the congregation has already prayed. The Arabic matn from the Hidayah states that it is permissible to pray nawafil before the fard as long as there is ample time. If time is short, one should leave them. There is a difference of opinion about the sunnah prayers of Zuhr and Fajr: some exclude them, citing their additional merit as shown by hadiths emphasizing them, while others include them, arguing that the Prophet's consistency (muwazabah) on these sunnah was only when performing fard in congregation, so they are not sunnah for the individual praying alone. The preferred view (awla) according to the author of Hidayah is not to leave these sunan in any situation, because they complete the fard prayers and the righteous predecessors maintained them. However, if one fears the time for fard will expire, one may leave the sunan. The commentary explains the scenario and concludes with the emphasis on following the practice of the khulafa' rashidin and companions.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): In this passage, sunnah refers to the recommended voluntary prayers that are consistently performed by the Prophet and are associated with the obligatory prayers.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer that is not obligatory and can be performed optionally.
مواظبت (muwazabah): Consistency in performing an act; considered a criterion for an act to be classified as sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred (awla) view in this passage, what should a person do if he arrives in a mosque after the congregation has prayed and has only enough time for the fard prayer before the time expires?
A) He should skip the sunnah and pray the fard only.
B) He should pray the sunnah first even if it causes the fard to be missed.
C) He should pray both sunnah and fard with a slight delay.
D) He should combine the sunnah with the fard in any order.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position is to maintain the emphasized sunan (especially Zuhr and Fajr) even when missing congregation, unless time is so limited that the fard may be lost.

Catching a Rak'ah by Joining Imam in Ruku' Without Bowing
Ruling and dispute on catching rak'ah when joining imam in ruku' without bowing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for catching a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku', and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the Hanafi position and Imam Zufar's position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school requires actual participation in ruku' to catch the rak'ah; finding the imam in ruku' is not enough.

A common scenario in congregational prayer is arriving late while the imam is already in ruku'. What if you say the opening takbir but then stand frozen until the imam rises — do you still catch that rak'ah? The Hanafi school answers no, while Imam Zufar and others say yes. This lesson examines the evidence and the practical consequences, sharpening your understanding of what it means to truly follow the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act: a person joins the imam in ruku', says takbir, but does not bow; he remains standing until the imam raises his head. The dispute: does he catch that rak'ah?
The three Hanafi imams say no; Zufar, Thawri, Ibn Abi Layla, Ibn Mubarak say yes.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi position requires actual participation (musharakat) in the actions of prayer. The person participated neither in qiyam (he missed it) nor in ruku' (he did not bow). The hadith of Ibn Umar is cited: bowing before the imam raises his head is a condition for catching the rak'ah.
Musharakat is the key principle: following means physically doing the actions.
3
State Zufar's position and its proof
Zufar argues that finding the imam in ruku' has the ruling of qiyam, so it is as if the follower caught the imam in qiyam, which would be sufficient to catch the rak'ah. This is an analogy (qiyas).
The analogy treats ruku' as equivalent to qiyam for the purpose of counting the rak'ah.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis reject the analogy because the hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly requires bowing. The condition is actual participation, not a legal fiction. The hadith is a direct textual proof (dalil naqli) that overrides qiyas.
The hadith is clear: 'if you bow before he raises his head...' — no bow, no rak'ah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Practical consequence: If one does not bow, according to Hanafis, he must add an extra rak'ah after the imam finishes. According to Zufar, he does not need to add an extra rak'ah. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the Hanafi position.
This difference affects how latecomers complete their salah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن انتهى الى الإمام فى ركوعه، فكبر وقف حتى رفع الامام رأسه، لا يصير مدركا لتلك الركعة خلافا لزفر هو يقول : ادرك الامام فيما له حكم القيام، ولنا ان الشرط هو المشاركة فى افعال الصلاة، ولم يوجد لا في القيام ولا في الركوع
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے امام کو اس کے رکوع میں پایا پھر اس شخص نے تکبیر تحریمہ کہی اور توقف کیا یہاں تک کہ امام نے اپنا سر اٹھالیا تو ی شخص اس رکعت کو پانے والا نہیں ہوگا امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس نے امام کو ایسی حالت میں پا لیا جس کو قیام کا حکم حاصل ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شرط افعال صلوۃ میں مشارکت ہے اور وہ پائی نہیں گئی نہ قیام میں اور نہ رکوع میں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص امام تک اس وقت پہنچا جبکہ امام رکوع میں تھا اور یہ شخص تکبیر تحریمہ کہہ کر کھڑا ہو گیا مگر امام کے ساتھ رکوع نہیں کیا یہاں تک کہ امام نے رکوع سے اپنا سر اٹھالیا۔ تو ائمہ ثلثہ کے نزدیک یہ شخص اس رکعت کو پانے والا شما نہیں ہوگا۔ امام زفر نے کہا کہ یہ شخص اس رکعت کا پانے والا شمار ہوگا۔ یہی قول ہے سفیان ثوری، ابن ابی لیلی اور عبداللہ بن مبارک کا ۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے امام کو رکوع کی حالت میں پایا ہے اگر چہ خود کوع نہیں کیا۔ اور رکوع کو قیام کا حکم حاصل ہے۔ پس رکوع کی حالت میں پانا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ حقیقتہ قیام کی حالت میں پانا اور حقیقت قیام کے اندر پانے سے رکعت کا پانے والا ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے رکوع کی حالت میں امام کو پانے سے بھی اس رکعت کو پانے والا شمارہ ہو گا۔ علماء ثلاثہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقتداء نام ہے نماز کے افعال میں شرکت کرنے کا اور شرکت یہاں پائی نہیں گئی نہ قیام کے اندر اور نہ رکوع کے اندر۔ پس جب اس رکعت کے نہ قیام میں شرکت ہو اور نہ رکوع میں تو یہ شخص اس رکعت کو پانے والا بھی نہیں ہوا۔ اور ہا امام زفر کا یہ کہنا کہ رکوع کو قیام کا حکم حاصل ہے تو یہ بھی تسلیم نہیں کیونکہ عبداللہ بن عمر کی حدیث ہے اذا ادرکت الامام راكعا فركعت قبل ان يرفع رأسه فقد ادركت تلك الركعة و ان رفع رأسه قبل ان يركع فاتتک تلک الرکعۃ یعنی جب تو نے امام کورکوع کی حالت میں پایا پھر تو نے امام کے سر اٹھانے سے پہلے رکوع کر لیا تو تو نے اس رکعت کو پالیا اور اگر امام نے اپنا سر اٹھایا کون کرنے سے پہلے تو یہ رکعت تجھ سے فوت ہو گئی۔
Whoever reaches the imam in his ruku', and he says the takbir and stands still until the imam raises his head, he does not become a participant in that rak'ah, contrary to Zufar. He says: He caught the imam in a state that has the ruling of standing. Our proof is that the condition is participation in the actions of prayer, and it is not found in standing nor in ruku'. [Urdu commentary: The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold he does not catch the rak'ah. Zufar and others hold he does. Zufar's proof: finding the imam in ruku' has the ruling of qiyam. The Hanafi proof: participation is necessary; the hadith of Ibn Umar states: 'If you catch the imam in ruku' and you bow before he raises his head, you have caught that rak'ah; if he raises his head before you bow, you have missed it.']
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning a person who joins the imam while the imam is already in ruku'. The person says the takbir (tahrimah) but does not bow; he simply stands until the imam raises his head. According to the three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), this person does not catch that rak'ah. Imam Zufar, along with Sufyan al-Thawri, Ibn Abi Layla, and Abdullah ibn Mubarak, holds that he does catch the rak'ah, arguing that finding the imam in ruku' is equivalent to finding him in qiyam regarding the ruling. The Hanafis respond that the condition for valid following (iqtida) is actual participation in the actions of prayer, and here the person participated neither in qiyam nor in ruku'. Furthermore, the hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly conditions catching the rak'ah upon bowing before the imam raises his head. The hadith says: 'If you catch the imam in ruku' and you bow before he raises his head, you have caught that rak'ah; if he raises his head before you bow, you have missed it.' This clearly refutes Zufar's position. The relied-upon view is the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
مدرک (mudrik): One who catches a rak'ah by joining the imam before the imam rises from ruku' of that rak'ah.
مشارکت (musharakat): Participation in the actions of prayer, which is required for valid following (iqtida).
ائتمام (i'timam): Following the imam in congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the hadith of Abdullah ibn 'Umar state about catching a rak'ah when finding the imam in ruku'?
A) One catches the rak'ah simply by finding the imam in ruku'.
B) One catches the rak'ah only if one bows before the imam raises his head.
C) One catches the rak'ah if one says the takbir before the imam rises.
D) One catches the rak'ah only if one recites al-Fatiha in that rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
To catch a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku', one must actually perform ruku' before the imam raises his head; merely finding him in ruku' is insufficient.

Ruling on Performing Sunnah Prayers Along with Fard
States ruling that sunnah prayers should not be abandoned unless fear of missing fard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing sunnah prayers with fard, identify the exception when sunnah may be abandoned, and explain the reasoning.

Core Idea
Sunnah prayers complete the fard; abandon them only if you fear missing the fard time.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling regarding the sunnah prayers that accompany the five daily fard prayers. The text emphasizes that these sunnahs are integral to perfecting the fard and should never be neglected under normal circumstances. However, a critical exception is provided: if there is a genuine fear that the fard time will expire, the sunnah may be abandoned to ensure the fard is performed within its prescribed window. Understanding this hierarchy—fard takes priority over sunnah—is essential for proper daily prayer practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is performing the sunnah prayers that accompany the fard prayers. The default ruling in the Hanafi school is that these are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized) and should be performed.
Sunnah muakkadah are akin to wajib in terms of emphasis, though not obligatory.
2
Recognize the general obligation to perform them
The text states that these sunnahs should be performed in all situations: whether one is praying alone or in congregation, whether resident or traveler. They should not be abandoned under any normal circumstance.
This contradicts a common misconception that traveling exempts one from sunnah prayers.
3
Note the exception
The only exception is when there is fear that the prescribed time for the fard prayer will expire. In that case, the sunnah may be abandoned to ensure the fard is performed within its time.
This exception is based on the priority of fard over sunnah.
4
Understand the reasoning
The sunnah prayers are described as 'completers' of the fard, meaning they make up for any deficiencies in the fard and increase its reward. Therefore, abandoning them would result in a loss of perfection of the fard.
The practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and senior Companions is cited as evidence.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
In daily life, one should always attempt to pray the sunnah prayers before/after the fard, unless there is a genuine time constraint. For example, if the congregation is about to start and praying sunnah would cause missing the fard, the sunnah should be skipped.
This ruling applies equally to residents and travelers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ساتھ پڑھے یا تنہا پڑھے خواہ مقیم ہو یا مسافر ہو کیونکہ سنن فرائض کی تکمیل کرنے والی ہیں لہذا فرائض کا ثواب مکمل کرنے کی خاطر ان کو کسی حال میں ترک نہ کرے۔ نیز خلفاء راشدین، کبار صحابہ اور تابعین نے بھی اسی پر عمل کیا ہے کہ سنتوں کو کسی حال میں ترک نہیں فرمایا۔ ہاں البتہ اگر وقت کے فوت ہونے کا خوف ہو تو سنتوں کو ترک کر دے اور فرائض ادا کرے۔ (عنایه)
He should recite along or alone, whether he is a resident or a traveler, because the sunnahs are completers of the fard. Therefore, for the sake of completing the reward of the fard, he should not abandon them in any circumstance. Also, the Rightly Guided Caliphs, senior Companions, and the Successors practiced thus: they never abandoned the sunnahs under any circumstance. However, if there is fear of the time passing, then he should abandon the sunnahs and perform the fard. (from 'Inaya)
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning the sunnah prayers (sunan) that accompany the fard prayers. The author instructs that whether one is praying individually or in congregation, as a resident or a traveler, the sunnah prayers should not be abandoned. The reason given is that the sunnah prayers complete the fard prayers, meaning they compensate for any shortcomings and increase reward. Therefore, abandoning them would result in a deficiency in the fard's reward. The author then cites the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, senior Companions, and the Successors to reinforce that the sunnah prayers were never abandoned. However, an exception is made if one fears that the prescribed time for the fard will expire; then the sunnah may be left to ensure the fard is performed within its time. This exception is based on priority: the fard is the primary obligation.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): The recommended prayers that accompany the fard prayers, specifically the sunnah muakkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When he is traveling
B) When he is a resident
C) When he fears the time for the fard will pass
D) When he is praying alone

Key Takeaway
Sunnah prayers should be performed in all situations unless there is a genuine fear that the fard time will expire.

Catching the Rak'ah When Follower Does Not Bow in Time
Intra-Hanafi dispute on catching rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on catching a rak'ah when a latecomer finds the imam in ruku' but does not bow before the imam raises his head, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar and the evidence from the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar.

Core Idea
Catching a rak'ah requires actual participation in ruku' with the imam, not merely finding him in ruku'.

In congregational prayer, latecomers often face the question: did I catch that rak'ah? The Hanafi school holds that catching a rak'ah depends on actual participation in either the standing (qiyam) or bowing (ruku') with the imam. This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about a scenario where a follower finds the imam in ruku' but fails to bow before the imam rises. The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule that the follower does not catch the rak'ah, while Imam Zufar disagrees. We will explore the evidence, especially the hadith of Ibn 'Umar, and understand why the majority view is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) regarding the latecomer who finds the imam in ruku' but does not bow. According to them, the follower does not catch that rak'ah.
The follower's prayer is valid overall, but he missed that specific rak'ah and must add another after the imam's salaam.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Zufar (and some other early scholars) hold that the follower does catch the rak'ah, because finding the imam in ruku' is equivalent to finding him in qiyam. Understand the reasoning behind this analogy.
Imam Zufar's logic: ruku' has the ruling of qiyam for the purpose of catching the rak'ah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine Imam Zufar's evidence: he argues that since ruku' has the ruling of qiyam, finding the imam in ruku' should suffice, just as finding him in qiyam would.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Study the response of the three imams: the condition is actual participation (musharaka) in the actions of prayer, not a legal fiction. The hadith of Ibn 'Umar is cited to show that bowing before the imam raises his head is explicitly required. Mere finding does not substitute.
The hadith states: 'If you catch the imam in ruku' and bow before he raises his head, you have caught that rak'ah; if he raises his head before you bow, that rak'ah is lost.'
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical difference: under Imam Zufar's view, the follower counts that rak'ah without bowing; under the three imams, he must perform an additional rak'ah after the imam's salaam.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the three imams, based on the explicit hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جو امام کو رکوع میں نہ پاسکا اس نے رکعت کو نہیں پایا
ومن انتهى الى الإمام فى ركوعه، فكبر وقف حتى رفع الامام رأسه، لا يصير مدركا لتلك الركعة خلافا لزفر هو يقول : ادرك الامام فيما له حكم القيام، ولنا ان الشرط هو المشاركة فى افعال الصلاة، ولم يوجد لا في القيام ولا في الركوع
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے امام کو اس کے رکوع میں پایا پھر اس شخص نے تکبیر تحریمہ کہی اور توقف کیا یہاں تک کہ امام نے اپنا سر اٹھالیا تو ی شخص اس رکعت کو پانے والا نہیں ہوگا امام زفر کا اختلاف ہے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس نے امام کو ایسی حالت میں پا لیا جس کو قیام کا حکم حاصل ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ شرط افعال صلوۃ میں مشارکت ہے اور وہ پائی نہیں گئی نہ قیام میں اور نہ رکوع میں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص امام تک اس وقت پہنچا جبکہ امام رکوع میں تھا اور یہ شخص تکبیر تحریمہ کہہ کر کھڑا ہو گیا مگر امام کے ساتھ رکوع نہیں کیا یہاں تک کہ امام نے رکوع سے اپنا سر اٹھالیا۔ تو ائمہ ثلثہ کے نزدیک یہ شخص اس رکعت کو پانے والے شما نہیں ہوگا۔ امام زفر نے کہا کہ یہ شخص اس رکعت کا پانے والا شمار ہوگا۔ یہی قول ہے سفیان ثوری، ابن ابی لیلی اور عبداللہ بن مبارک کا ۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے امام کو رکوع کی حالت میں پایا ہے اگر چہ خود کوع نہیں کیا۔ اور رکوع کو قیام کا حکم حاصل ہے۔ پس رکوع کی حالت میں پانا ایسا ہے جیسا کہ حقیقتہ قیام کی حالت میں پانا اور حقیقت قیام کے اندر پانے سے رکعت کا پانے والا ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے رکوع کی حالت میں امام کو پانے سے بھی اس رکعت کو پانے والا شمار ہوگا۔ علماء ثلاثہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقتداء نام ہے نماز کے افعال میں شرکت کرنے کا اور شرکت یہاں پائی نہیں گئی نہ قیام کے اندر اور نہ رکوع کے اندر۔ پس جب اس رکعت کے نہ قیام میں شرکت ہو اور نہ رکوع میں تو یہ شخص اس رکعت کو پانے والا بھی نہیں ہوا۔ اور ہاں امام زفر کا یہ کہنا کہ رکوع کو قیام کا حکم حاصل ہے تو یہ بھی تسلیم نہیں کیونکہ عبداللہ بن عمر کی حدیث ہے اذا ادرکت الامام راكعا فركعت قبل ان يرفع رأسه فقد ادركت تلك الركعة و ان رفع رأسه قبل ان يركع فاتتک تلک الرکعۃ یعنی جب تو نے امام کورکوع کی حالت میں پایا پھر تو نے امام کے سر اٹھانے سے پہلے رکوع کر لیا تو تو نے اس رکعت کو پالیا اور اگر امام نے اپنا سر اٹھایا رکوع کرنے سے پہلے تو یہ رکعت تجھ سے فوت ہو گئی۔
Whoever did not catch the imam in ruku' did not catch the rak'ah. And whoever reaches the imam in his ruku', says takbir, and waits until the imam raises his head, he does not become a catcher of that rak'ah, contrary to Zufar. He says: He caught the imam in a state that has the ruling of standing. For us, the condition is participation in the actions of the prayer, and it did not exist, neither in standing nor in ruku'. Translation: And whichever person found the imam in his ruku', then that person said the takbir tahrimah and waited until the imam raised his head, then that person will not be a finder of that rak'ah. Imam Zufar has a difference; he says that he found the imam in a state that has the ruling of standing. And our proof is that the condition is participation in the actions of prayer, and it was not found, neither in standing nor in ruku'. Elaboration of the issue: A person reached the imam when the imam was in ruku', and this person said takbir tahrimah and stood but did not bow with the imam until the imam raised his head from ruku'. Then according to the three imams, this person will not be considered a finder of that rak'ah. Imam Zufar said that this person will be counted as having found that rak'ah. This is also the saying of Sufyan Thawri, Ibn Abi Layla, and Abdullah ibn Mubarak. Imam Zufar's proof is that this person found the imam in the state of ruku' even if he did not himself bow. And ruku' has the ruling of standing. So finding him in ruku' is like finding him in standing in reality, and finding him in standing makes one a finder of the rak'ah. Therefore, finding the imam in ruku' also makes him counted as a finder of that rak'ah. The proof of the three imams is that iqtida' (following) is participation in the actions of the prayer, and participation was not found here, neither in standing nor in ruku'. So when there is no participation in the rak'ah either in standing or in ruku', then this person did not become a finder of that rak'ah. And as for Imam Zufar's statement that ruku' has the ruling of standing, that is also not accepted because of the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar: 'When you catch the imam in ruku' and you bow before he raises his head, then you have caught that rak'ah; and if he raises his head before you bow, then that rak'ah is lost for you.'
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding catching a rak'ah when a latecomer finds the imam in ruku' but does not actually join the ruku' before the imam raises his head. The ruling of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that the follower does not catch that rak'ah because he did not participate in any part of the prayer with the imam. He neither stood (qiyam) with the imam nor bowed (ruku') with him. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing that finding the imam in ruku' is equivalent to finding him in standing (qiyam), because ruku' has the ruling of standing for the purpose of catching the rak'ah. The Hanafi response is that the condition for catching a rak'ah is actual participation (musharaka) in an action of the prayer, not a legal fiction. They support their position with the hadith of Ibn 'Umar, which explicitly states that catching the rak'ah requires bowing (ruku') before the imam raises his head. If the follower does not bow in time, the rak'ah is lost. Thus, mere finding the imam in ruku' without joining is insufficient. This hadith directly refutes Zufar's analogy.

Key Terms
إدراك الركعة (idrak al-rak'ah): Catching a rak'ah in congregational prayer by participating in at least one part (juz') with the imam.
مشاركة (musharaka): Participation in an action of the prayer simultaneously with the imam.
ركوع (ruku'): The bowing posture in prayer. Here, the key action for catching a rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), when does a latecomer catch the rak'ah if he finds the imam in ruku'?
A) As soon as he says the takbir tahrimah
B) If he bows (ruku') before the imam raises his head
C) If he stands with the imam before ruku'
D) He never catches it

Key Takeaway
Catching a rak'ah in the Hanafi school requires actual participation in either qiyam or ruku' with the imam; merely finding the imam in ruku' is insufficient, as per the hadith of Ibn 'Umar.

Follower Bows Before Imam: Validity When Imam Joins in Ruku'
Ruling on follower's prayer when he precedes imam in ruku' but imam joins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the validity of a follower's prayer when he precedes the imam in ruku' but the imam joins him, and explain the proof using the concept of juz' participation.

Core Idea
Participation in any part (juz') of an action with the imam saves the prayer even if the follower initially preceded.

In congregational prayer, the follower must follow the imam. But what if the follower accidentally bows before the imam, yet the imam later bows and they share the ruku'? This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the ruling of the three imams (valid but makruh) and the dissenting view of Imam Zufar (invalid). Understanding the concept of 'juz' (part)' is key to resolving this intra-Hanafi dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the three imams' ruling
Identify the ruling from the passage: the follower's prayer is valid (jā'iz) but makruh (disliked) because he preceded the imam. Validity is based on eventual participation in one part.
The three imams are Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
2
Identify Imam Zufar's ruling and proof
Imam Zufar holds the prayer invalid. His proof: the part of ruku' performed before the imam is not credited, and what is built on the invalid is invalid. He cites the hadith 'Do not differ from your imam.'
Zufar's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: condition of juz' participation
The three imams argue that the condition for valid following is participation in any one part (juz') of the act. Here, they shared the latter part of ruku', satisfying the condition.
The concept of juz' is key: any part, not necessarily the entire action.
4
Distinguish from the case of no participation
Zufar analogized to the case where the follower raises his head before the imam bows. The Hanafi response: in that case, there is no participation at all. Here, there is eventual participation.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Zufar, follower must repeat ruku'; under the three, prayer is valid albeit makruh.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text favors the three imams by presenting their proof and concluding with 'Allah knows best'. The mufta bihi position is validity with karahah.
The majority view is relied upon for fatwa.

And if the follower bowed before his imam, and the imam caught him in it (ruku'), it is permissible. And Zufar said: It does not suffice for him, because what he performed before the imam is not considered, and so what is built upon it is not considered. For us, the condition is participation in one part (juz'), just as in the first side (i.e., the case where the follower bows after the imam but raises before the imam). And Allah knows best. Translation: And if the follower performed ruku' before his imam, then the imam caught him in ruku', then this is permissible. And Imam Zufar said that it will not be sufficient for the follower because the ruku' that the follower brought before the imam is not credited, therefore what is based on it will also be uncredited. And our proof is that the condition is participation in one part, just as in the first side, and Allah knows best. Elaboration: If the follower went into ruku' before the imam, then the imam also went into ruku' so that both shared in ruku', then in this case the follower's prayer is not invalid. The same ruling applies if this situation occurs in sajdah (prostration). However, the follower's prayer will be makruh (disliked). The reason for karahah is the Prophet's statement: 'Do not precede me in ruku' and sujud.' Also the Prophet said: 'Whoever bows before the imam, should fear that his head will be turned into the head of a donkey.' Imam Zufar said that the follower's prayer will not be valid. Consequently, the follower must repeat that ruku'; if he does not repeat, his prayer will not be correct. Imam Zufar's proof is that the part of ruku' which the follower performed before the imam is not credited because the Prophet said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him.' So when that part is uncredited, what is built upon it is also invalid, because building upon the invalid is invalid. Thus it is as if the follower raised his head from ruku' before the imam bowed. Our proof is that the condition for validity is participation in one part. So participation in one part has been found, meaning even if participation was not found in the first part, it was found in the last part, and for validity of the prayer this much participation is sufficient, just as in the first part: when the follower bowed with the imam but raised his head before the imam, it is valid because participation in one part was found. But if he went into ruku' before the imam and raised his head before the imam bowed, then the prayer is not valid because in that case no participation was found in any part, whereas participation in one part was necessary.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage addresses another scenario: the follower bows (ruku') before the imam, but then the imam also goes into ruku' so that both are simultaneously in ruku' for at least one moment. The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rule that the follower's prayer is valid (jā'iz) in this case, though it is makruh because the follower preceded the imam. The reason it is valid is that they shared a part of ruku' together. Imam Zufar, however, holds that the prayer is invalid because the initial part of the follower's ruku' was done independently of the imam and thus is not creditworthy; if a part is invalid, then what is built on it is also invalid. The Hanafi response is that the requirement for validity is participation in at least one part (juz') of an action. In this case, they shared the latter part of ruku', which is sufficient. Zufar's analogy to the case where the follower raises his head before the imam bows is false, because in that case there is no participation at all. The hadiths cited (don't precede the imam) warn against such precedence but do not nullify the prayer if eventual participation occurs.

Key Terms
جزء (juz'): A part of an action, e.g., part of ruku'. Participation in any part suffices for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), what is the ruling if a follower bows before the imam, but the imam joins him in ruku' so they share part of it?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but makruh.
C) The prayer is valid and recommended.
D) The follower must repeat the ruku' separately.

Key Takeaway
The condition for valid following is participation in any part of an action; precedence alone does not invalidate if eventual participation occurs.

Follower's Ruku' Before Imam: Validity and Dispute with Imam Zufar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of preceding Imam in ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a follower precedes the Imam in ruku' and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
Participation in one part suffices for validity — preceding the Imam makes it makruh, not invalid.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement: what happens if a follower goes into ruku' before the Imam but the Imam catches up so they share at least part of the ruku'? The majority holds the prayer valid but disliked, while Imam Zufar deems it invalid. Understanding the principle of 'musharakat fi juz'' is key to resolving this.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad rule: the follower's prayer is valid (sahih) but makruh (disliked) because participation in one part (musharakat fi juz') occurred.
2
Identify Imam Zufar's opposing view
Imam Zufar rules the prayer invalid (fasid) and requires the follower to repeat the ruku' because any part performed before the Imam is invalid, and building upon invalid is invalid.
3
Trace the dalil for each side
Majority uses hadith 'Do not precede me in ruku' and sujud' (indicating karahah) and the principle that participation in one part suffices. Zufar uses hadith 'The Imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him' and qiyas.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The majority rebuts Zufar by clarifying that the condition for validity is participation in one part, not full compliance from start. Even missing the first part, participation in the latter part suffices.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
According to majority, the follower completes prayer without repeating ruku'. According to Zufar, follower must repeat ruku' or prayer is invalid. The mufta bihi is the majority view.

It will not be sufficient because the follower brought ruku' before the Imam, so it is not considered, and what is based on it is also not considered. Our proof is that the condition is participation in one part, as in the first side. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The issue is that if the follower goes into ruku' before the Imam, then the Imam also goes into ruku' until both are together in ruku', then the follower's prayer is not invalid. The same ruling applies if this occurs in prostration. However, the follower's prayer is makruh, due to the Prophet's saying: 'Do not precede me in ruku' and sujud.' Also the Prophet said: 'Does not he who bows before the Imam fear that Allah will turn his head into a donkey's head?' Imam Zufar said that the follower's prayer is not valid, so it is obligatory for him to repeat that ruku', and if he does not repeat, his prayer is not correct. Imam Zufar's proof: The part of ruku' that the follower performed before the Imam is not valid because the Prophet said: 'The Imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him.' Since that part is not valid, what is built upon it is also invalid, because building upon invalid is invalid. So it is as if he raised his head from ruku' before the Imam did. Our proof: The condition for validity is participation in one part. So participation has occurred in one part, i.e., in the latter part even if not in the first part, and this much participation is sufficient for validity, just as in the first part: if the follower went into ruku' with the Imam but raised his head before the Imam, it is valid because participation in one part occurred. And if he went into ruku' before the Imam and raised his head before the Imam's ruku', then his prayer is not valid, because no participation occurred in any part, although participation in one part was necessary.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of a follower's prayer when he goes into ruku' before the Imam but then the Imam joins him. The majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) hold that the prayer is valid but makruh (disliked). The reason is that the condition for validity of following the Imam is participation in at least one part of the action. Even if the follower started ruku' before the Imam, as long as they are together in some portion of the ruku', the requirement is met. The karahah is due to the prohibition of preceding the Imam. Imam Zufar, known for strict qiyas, argues that any part performed before the Imam is invalid because it contradicts the command to follow, and building upon invalid (bina' ala al-fasid) is invalid. Therefore, he requires the follower to repeat the ruku'. The majority responds that the requirement is only participation, not full compliance from the start. This shows the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas in matters of worship.

Key Terms
مشارکت (musharakat): Participation of the follower with the Imam in at least one component of an action (like ruku' or sujud) is the condition for validity of the follower's prayer.
مقتدی (muqtadi): One who prays behind an Imam in congregation.
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a Hanafi scholar known for strict qiyas, often differing from the majority.
جزء (juz'): Part or component; here, a part of an action like ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, if a follower goes into ruku' before the Imam and then the Imam joins him in ruku', what is the ruling of the follower's prayer?
A) Invalid and must be repeated
B) Valid but makruh
C) Valid and recommended
D) Invalid and the follower must repeat the ruku'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that participation in one part of an action suffices for validity, making the follower's prayer valid but makruh if he preceded the Imam.

The Obligation of Order (Tartib) Between Missed and Current Prayers
Inter-madhhab dispute on tartib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that tartib is wajib, state the Shafi'i counterargument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the hadith and usul principles.

Core Idea
Order between missed and current prayers is wajib in Hanafi, not merely recommended.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: when one remembers a missed prayer, must it be performed before the current prayer? The Hanafi school rules this order is wajib, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers it only mustahabb. We will trace the proofs from hadith and usul principles to understand why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling according to the Hanafi school: performing the missed prayer before the current prayer is wajib (obligatory), not fard or sunnah.
Wajib means the order is required, and omitting it without excuse incurs sin, but the current prayer remains valid.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the order is mustahabb (recommended) only. Understand his reasoning: each fard prayer is independent, so one cannot be a condition for another.
Al-Shafi'i's view hinges on the principle that obligations are independent unless a clear condition is proven.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i argues that making a missed prayer a condition for the current prayer contradicts the independent nature of each fard. He also claims the hadith cited by Hanafis is a solitary report (khabar wahid) which cannot establish wujub.
The opponent's dalil is aqli (rational) and naqli (textual critique).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the hadith is mashhur (well-known), not khabar wahid. Even if considered khabar wahid, it explains the mujmal (general) Quranic command 'aqimu al-salah', thus acquiring Quranic authority. The hadith's command to repeat the current prayer confirms that precedence of the missed prayer is required.
This uses the usul principle: al-khabar al-wahid yubayyin al-mujmal.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi: if one prays current prayer first intentionally without excuse, he is sinful but the prayer is valid; he must still make up the missed prayer. Shafi'i: no sin, and order is not required.
The conflict is in the legal category (wajib vs mustahabb) affecting sin but not validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت
ترجمہ ( یہ ) باب فائنہ نمازوں کی قضاء کرنے (کے بیان ) میں ہے
تشریح گذشتہ باب میں ادا اور اس کے متعلقات کے احکام کا بیان تھا اب اس باب میں قضاء کے احکام ذکر کریں گے۔ چونکہ ادا اصل اور قضاء اس کا خلیفہ ہے اس لئے ادا کو پہلے اور قضاء کو بعد میں ذکر کیا گیا ہے۔ ادا کہتے ہیں ، عین واجب کو اس کے مستحق کے سپر د کر دینا ہو قضاء کہتے ہیں مثل واجب کو سپر د کرنا۔
فوت شدہ نماز کو قضاء کرنے کا وقت
من فاتته صلوة قضاها اذا ذكرها، وقدمها على فرض الوقت والاصل فيه ان الترتيب بين الفوائت وفرض الوقت عندنا مستحق، وعند الشافعى مستحب لان كل فرض اصل بنفسه، فلا يكون شرطا لغيره، ولنا قوله عليه السلام من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فلم يذكرها الا وهو مع الامام فليصل التي هو فيها، ثم ليصل التي ذكرها بعد التي صلى مع الامام
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
التي ذكرها بعد التي صلى مع الامام
۲۲۱
باب قضاء الفوائت
زرجمہ جس شخص کی نماز فوت ہو گئی وہ اس کو قضاء کرے جب یاد کرے اور اس کو وقتی فرض پر مقدم کرے اور اصل اس میں یہ ہے کہ فوائت اور وقتی فرض کے درمیان ہمارے نزیک ترتیب واجب ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ ہر فرض بذات خود اصل ہے تو وہ دوسرے کے لئے شرط نہ ہو گا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جو شخص سوگیا نماز سے یا اس کو بھول گیا پھر وہ یاد نہ آئی مگر یہ کہ وہ امام کے ساتھ ہے تو یہ پڑھ لے جس میں موجود ہے پھر وہ پڑھے جس کو یاد کیا پھر اس کا اعادہ کرے جو امام کے ساتھ ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی کی نماز فوت ہوگئی تو یاد آنے پر اس کی قضاء کرے اور اس کو وقعیہ پر مقدم کرے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک فوائت اور وقتیہ کے درمیان ترتیب واجب ہے یعنی فائتہ نماز کو وقتیہ پر مقدم کرنا واجب ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ترتیب مستحب ہے، فائتہ کو وقتیہ پر مقدم کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہر فرض بذات خود اصل ہے ابدا وہ دوسرے کے لئے شرط نہ ہو گا کیونکہ شرط تابع ہوتی ہے۔ اور اصالت اور تبعیت کے اندر منافات ہے پس اگر وقتیہ نماز کے لئے فائتہ کا ادا کرنا واجب (شرط) قرار دیا جائے تو اس صورت میں فائتہ کا تابع ہونا لازم آئے گا حالانکہ فائیہ فرض ہونے کی وجہ سے بذات خود اصل ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ فائتہ کا وقتیہ پر مقدم کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔
ہماری دلیل اللہ کے نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فلم يذكرها الا وهو مع الامام فليصل التي هو فيها ثم ليصل التي ذكرها ثم لسعد التي مع الامام حدیث کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر نماز فوت ہوگئی اور یہ شخص امام کے ساتھ وقت یہ پڑھنے لگا تو امام کے ساتھ اپنی نماز پوری کرے پھر فائتہ پڑھے پھر اس نماز کا اعادہ کرے جو امام کے ساتھ پڑھی ہے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جو نماز امام کے ساتھ پڑھی ہے۔ چونکہ وہ فائتہ سے مقدم ہو گئی ہے حالانکہ فائنہ کا مقدم کرنا واجب تھا اس لئے اس کو لوٹانے کا حکم کیا گیا ہے تا کہ فائتہ اور وقتیہ کے درمیان ترتیب متحقق ہو جائے ۔ مگر یہاں ایک اعتراض ہے۔ وہ یہ کہ یہ حدیث اخبار آحاد میں سے ہے اور خبر واحد سے فرضیت ثابت نہیں ہوتی لہذا اس حدیث ے ترتیب کا فرض ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ جواب یہ حدیث خبر مشہور ہے نہ کہ خبر واحد اور اگر تسلیم کر لیں کہ خبر واحد ہے تو جواب یہ ہے کہ ترتیب تو کتاب اللہ یعنی اقیموا الصلوۃ سے ثابت ہوئی ہے۔ یعنی چونکہ کتاب اللہ مجمل ہے اس لئے یہ حدیث مجمل کتاب کا بیان واقع ہوگی۔
فوت شدہ اور وقتی نمازوں میں ترتیب
ولوخاف فوت الوقت، يقدم الوقتية، ثم يقضيها، لان الترتيب يسقط بضيق الوقت، وكذا بالنسيان وكثرة الفوائت كيلا يؤدى الى تفويت الوقتية
ترجمہ اور اگر وقت نکل جانے کا خوف ہو تو وقتیہ کو مقدم کرے پھر فائتہ کی اضاء کرے کیونکہ ترتیب تنگی وقت کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہے یونہی بھول جانے اور کثرت فوائت سے تا کہ وقت یہ کو فوت کرنا لازم نہ آئے۔
تشریح پہلے مسئلہ میں گر چکا ہے کہ فائتہ اور وقتیہ کے درمیان ترتیب واجب ہے لیکن اگر وقت تنگ ہو گیا اور اس بات کا اندیشہ پیدا ہو
Chapter on Making Up Missed Prayers. Translation: This chapter is about making up missed prayers. Explanation: The previous chapter dealt with performing prayers on time; this chapter deals with makeup prayers. Ada means fulfilling the exact obligation, qada means fulfilling its equivalent. The time for making up a missed prayer: Whoever misses a prayer should make it up when he remembers, and he should give it precedence over the current prayer. The principle is that order between missed and current prayers is obligatory according to us, and recommended according to al-Shafi'i, because every obligation is fundamental in itself, so it cannot be a condition for another. Our proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, and only remembers while with the Imam, should pray the one he is in, then pray the one he remembered, then repeat the one he prayed with the Imam.' ... Explanation: The rule is that order is obligatory. Al-Shafi'i's proof: Each obligation is independent, so one cannot be a condition for another. Our response: The hadith shows that the prayer with the Imam is given precedence, but since the missed prayer must come first, the re-prayer is commanded to establish order. Objection: This is a solitary hadith, so it cannot prove obligation. Answer: It is a well-known hadith, and even if solitary, it explains the general command 'Establish prayer' from the Quran. Exceptions: If one fears the current time will pass, he prays the current prayer first, then makes up the missed one, because order is dropped due to time constraint, forgetfulness, or many missed prayers to avoid losing the current prayer.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on making up missed prayers (qada al-fawa'it) and establishes the key ruling: when one remembers a missed prayer, he must make it up immediately and it must be prayed before the current prayer (except when time is tight). The author presents the Hanafi position that this order (tartib) is wajib (obligatory), contrasting with Imam al-Shafi'i who considers it mustahabb (recommended). The Hanafi proof is the hadith about a person who remembers a missed prayer while already in a congregational prayer: he completes his current prayer, then prays the missed one, then repeats the current one. This shows that the current prayer is only valid as an exception; normally the missed prayer comes first. The Shafi'i counterargument is that each fard is independent, so one cannot be a condition for another. The Hanafi response refutes that the hadith is mashhur (well-known) and explains the Quranic command. The passage also provides exceptions: if the current prayer's time is about to expire, one prays the current prayer first to avoid losing it entirely. This chapter is a model of usul al-fiqh reasoning, combining naqli (textual) and aqli (rational) proofs.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligation by performing its equivalent after its time has passed.
فوائت (fawa'it): Plural of fa'itah, meaning prayers whose prescribed time has passed without being performed.
ترتیب (tartib): The required order of precedence between missed prayers and the current prayer, i.e., performing the missed prayer before the current one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence for the Hanafi position that tartib is wajib?
A) Quranic command 'aqimu al-salah'
B) Hadith about the person who remembers a missed prayer while with the Imam
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Rational argument from independence of obligations

Key Takeaway
Order between missed and current prayers is wajib in the Hanafi school, and the proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) which requires precedence of the missed prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Exceptions to the Order of Missed and Current Prayers
Exceptions to the wajib order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three exceptions where the wajib order (tartib) is dropped and apply them to scenarios.

Core Idea
Tartib is dropped when time is tight, when one forgets, or when many prayers are missed.

While tartib is wajib in principle, the Hanafi school recognizes situations where requiring order would cause more harm than good. This lesson covers the three exceptions: fear of losing the current prayer's time, forgetfulness, and a large number of missed prayers. These exceptions prevent the loss of current prayers and facilitate the fulfillment of multiple obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception scenarios
The passage lists three situations: (1) fear of current prayer time expiring (ضيق الوقت), (2) forgetfulness (النسيان), (3) many missed prayers (كثرة الفوائت). In these cases, tartib is dropped.
These are not exhaustive but cover major cases.
2
Understand the rationale
The rationale is to avoid losing the current prayer entirely (تفويت الوقتية). Preserving the current prayer takes precedence over order because it is more harmful to miss an obligation entirely than to delay another.
This reflects the principle: if two obligations conflict, the greater is given priority.
3
Apply to the time constraint case
If the time for the current prayer is about to end (e.g., a few minutes before sunset for Asr), one prays the current prayer first, then makes up the missed prayer afterward.
This is the most common exception.
4
Apply to forgetfulness
If one forgets the missed prayer and only remembers after completing the current prayer, tartib is dropped. He does not need to repeat the current prayer; he simply makes up the missed prayer afterward.
This differs from the hadith case where he remembers during the prayer.
5
Apply to many missed prayers
If a person has missed more than five prayers (some say more than six), tartib is no longer required. He can pray the current prayer first and then make up the missed ones in any order.
The exact number is debated; the text says 'kathrat al-fawa'it' without specifying a number.
