نماز جائز ہو جائے گی یہ بات ذہن نشین رہے کہ یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ یہ جاہل ہو لیکن اگر عالم اور اس مسئلہ سے واقف ہے تو عشاء کی نماز بھی درست نہیں ہوگی ۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
He first performed the current Fajr, then he made up the previous day's Fajr. Since this person is obligated to observe order, giving priority to the current over the missed [prayer] rendered this prayer invalid, and the missed prayers became six: five from the previous day and one from today's Fajr. But when he made up the previous day's Fajr, and it is valid, then the missed prayers again became five: four prayers from yesterday (from Zuhr to Isha) and today's Fajr. Then at Zuhr time he first performed today's Zuhr, and later yesterday's Zuhr, so today's Zuhr became invalid because, although obligated to observe order, he gave priority to the current over the missed. Then when today's Zuhr became invalid, the missed prayers became six again (from yesterday's Zuhr to today's Zuhr), but when he performed yesterday's Zuhr and it was valid, the missed prayers again became five (from yesterday's Asr to today's Zuhr). Then Asr time came and he first performed today's Asr, so due to being obligated to observe order it became invalid, thus the number of missed prayers became six again, but when he prayed yesterday's Asr and it is correct, the missed remain five (from Maghrib to Asr). Then at Maghrib time he gave priority to the current, so due to being obligated to observe order, the current Maghrib became invalid and the missed became six (from yesterday's Maghrib to today's Maghrib), but when he made up yesterday's Maghrib, the missed again became five. Then when at Isha time he first performed the current, due to being obligated to observe order, the Isha prayer became invalid and the total missed became six (from yesterday's Isha to today's Isha), but when he made up yesterday's Isha and it is valid, the missed again became five. From this detail you have understood that if current prayers are given priority over missed ones, the missed are valid and the current are invalid, and it is also established that if the missed become few, i.e., less than six, then the obligation of order returns. The intent here is to prove this. And if current prayers are delayed, the detail is as follows: At today's Fajr time, yesterday's Fajr was performed first, but today's Fajr was not performed because he gave priority to the current over the remaining missed, despite the obligation of order requiring the missed to be given priority over the current. Apply analogical reasoning to the remaining prayers similarly. But at Isha time, when he first performed yesterday's Isha and then today's Isha, Imam Muhammad said that today's Isha would be valid because this person is under the impression that he has no missed prayers, whereas actually today's four prayers are missed. So this person became like one who forgot the missed prayers, and it has already been stated that forgetfulness nullifies the obligation of order. Thus when the order obligation was nullified, the Isha prayer becomes valid. Bear in mind that this ruling applies when he is ignorant, but if he is a scholar and aware of this issue, then the Isha prayer will also not be valid. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 225

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school explaining the intricate rules of tartib (order) between missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it) and current prayers (waqtiyyat). The author presents a detailed hypothetical scenario of a person who has five missed prayers from the previous day plus the current day's five prayers. The scenario demonstrates that if the sahib tartib (one obligated to maintain order) prays a current prayer before making up the missed ones, the current prayer becomes invalid (fasid) because the obligation of tartib was violated. However, the missed prayer when subsequently performed is valid. The number of missed prayers fluctuates depending on actions: whenever a current prayer is invalidated, it adds to the count of missed prayers, but when a missed prayer is made up, the count reduces. The key principle derived is that if the number of missed prayers becomes less than six, the obligation of tartib returns (i.e., the person must again observe order). The passage also discusses the opposite case where the person delays current prayers: if one inadvertently neglects tartib out of ignorance or forgetfulness, the later current prayers may be considered valid, as forgetfulness abrogates the order obligation. Imam Muhammad's view on this is cited. The author emphasizes that this leniency applies only to the ignorant, not the knowledgeable scholar who deliberately violates tartib.

Key Terms
ترتیب (tartib): The obligation to perform missed obligatory prayers before current ones when the number of missed prayers is six or more (or when they are less than six but the obligation has returned).
فوائت (fawa'it): Plural of fa'itah: missed obligatory prayers that are owed as qada.
وقتیہ (waqtiyyah): The current obligatory prayer that is being performed within its prescribed time.
صاحب ترتیب (sahib al-tartib): A person who is obligated to observe the order between prayers because the number of his missed prayers is large (six or more) or because the obligation has returned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Six
B) Five
C) Four
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
The core rule: for sahib tartib, current prayers prayed before missed are invalid, but missed prayers remain valid; the number of missed fluctuates, and when they drop below six the obligation of order returns.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Fate of a Prayer When Fardiyyah Is Lost
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity when fardiyyah is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad regarding the validity of a prayer when its fardiyyah is lost due to tartib violation, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to the ruling on wudu after qahqaha.

Core Idea
Loss of fardiyyah does not necessarily nullify the entire prayer; the tahrimah can sustain it as nafl.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: if a person prays Asr while knowingly having missed Zuhr, the prayer is invalid as fard due to violating tartib. But what happens to the prayer itself? Does it become completely void, or can it remain valid as nafl? The shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad differ on this, with a practical consequence regarding the effect of loud laughter (qahqaha) during such a prayer. We will analyze the reasoning behind each position and understand why the shaykhayn's view is the mufta bihi.

Guided Path
1
State the common ground
Identify the initial ruling: a person who prays Asr while remembering that he missed Zuhr has violated the obligation of tartib. The prayer is invalid as fard unless it is at the very end of Asr time. This is not disputed.
The exception at the end of time shows that tartib is dropped when time is too short.
2
Identify the two positions
The shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the original prayer does not become entirely invalid; it remains as a nafl prayer. Imam Muhammad holds that the entire prayer becomes invalid, counting neither as fard nor as nafl.
The dispute is about the effect of losing the fardiyyah attribute.
3
Follow each proof
Imam Muhammad argues: the tahrimah was contracted specifically for the fard of Asr; when that fard becomes invalid, the tahrimah itself is void, so the entire prayer is void. The shaykhayn respond: the tahrimah was contracted for the prayer with the attribute of fardiyyah; the loss of the attribute does not necessarily void the substance.
The shaykhayn view the fardiyyah as an accidental attribute, not an essential part of the prayer.
4
Examine the analogy used by the shaykhayn
The shaykhayn analogize to a person who begins fasting for expiation while poor, then becomes wealthy mid-day. The fast remains valid as nafl, even though it no longer counts for expiation. Similarly, the prayer remains valid as nafl.
This analogy shows the general Hanafi principle that loss of the specific purpose (fard) does not always nullify the act.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference appears if the person laughs loudly (qahqaha) during that prayer. According to the shaykhayn, since the prayer remains valid (as nafl), the laughter breaks wudu. According to Imam Muhammad, since the prayer is entirely invalid, the laughter occurs outside prayer and does not break wudu.
This concrete consequence illustrates the legal impact of each position.

شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ البتہ صوم نفل ہو جائے گا۔ اور کفارہ یمین میں اس لئے شمار نہیں ہو گا کہ دار آدمی کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ کفارہ یمین بالا طعام ادا کرے یا بالکسوۃ یا غلام آزاد کرے۔ ان تینوں پر عدم قدرت کی صورت میں روزہ
And whoever prays Asr while remembering that he has not prayed Zuhr, it is invalid, unless at the end of the time [of Asr]. This is the issue of order. And when the obligatory nature is invalidated, the original prayer does not become invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but according to Muhammad it becomes invalid, because the tahrimah was contracted for the fard; so when the fardiyyah is invalidated, the tahrimah becomes invalid entirely. And for them (the two) [the argument is that] it was contracted for the original prayer with the attribute of fardiyyah; so the invalidation of the attribute does not necessarily entail the invalidation of the original. Translation: And whoever prays Asr while remembering that he has not prayed Zuhr, his Asr prayer is invalid unless the remembrance occurs at the very end of the Asr time, and this is the issue of order. And when the obligatory nature is invalidated, according to the two shaykhs the original prayer does not become invalid. And according to Imam Muhammad it becomes invalid, because the tahrimah was contracted for the fard; so when the fardiyyah is invalidated, the tahrimah is also invalidated. And the proof of the two shaykhs is that the tahrimah was contracted for the original prayer with the attribute of fardiyyah; so the invalidation of the attribute does not necessarily require the invalidation of the act. Explanation: The issue is that a person prayed Asr while remembering that he has not yet prayed Zuhr, so his Asr prayer becomes invalid because he abandoned the order, although the order was obligatory for him. Yes, if he prayed Asr at the very end of Asr time and he remembers that he did not pray Zuhr, then the Asr prayer becomes correct, because the narrowness of time nullifies the order. As for the question: when the obligatory nature is invalidated due to the loss of order, does the original prayer become invalid or not? There is a difference of opinion. The two shaykhs said that the original prayer does not become invalid, meaning that due to the absence of order, the fulfillment of the fard of Asr is invalidated, but its being nafl remains. The gist is that this Asr prayer will not count as an obligatory prayer but will count as a supererogatory prayer. And Imam Muhammad said that when the fardiyyah is invalidated, the original prayer also becomes invalid, meaning this Asr prayer will count neither as fard nor as nafl. The practical consequence of this difference appears in the case where a person began the Asr prayer in the spacious time while remembering the missed Zuhr, then during the prayer he laughed loudly. According to the two shaykhs, his wudu would be broken because according to them the original prayer remains, and laughing loudly during prayer breaks wudu, so wudu breaks. According to Imam Muhammad, wudu would not break because according to him the original prayer itself became invalid, so this laughter did not occur during the state of prayer. And laughing loudly outside of prayer does not break wudu, so in this case laughing loudly does not break wudu. In the original issue, Imam Muhammad's proof is that the tahrimah was contracted for the fard of Asr, and that thing for which the tahrimah was contracted has become invalid, so the tahrimah also becomes invalid. Because the tahrimah is a means to obtain that thing; when the objective becomes invalid, its means and instrument also become invalid. When the tahrimah becomes invalid, the original prayer itself becomes invalid, and when the original prayer is invalid, neither fard nor nafl is performed. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the tahrimah was contracted for the original prayer which is described with the attribute of fardiyyah, and due to the loss of order, the attribute of fardiyyah of the Asr prayer has become invalid. It is not necessary [that the original becomes invalid], just as if a person due to his poverty and need started fasting three days for the expiation of an oath, then in the middle of the day he became wealthy, his original fast does not become invalid but the attribute of being valid for expiation of the oath becomes invalid; that fast will not count for the expiation of the oath but will become a nafl fast. It will not count for the expiation because it is necessary for a free person to fulfill the expiation of an oath by feeding or clothing or freeing a slave; in case of inability to do these three, then fasting

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute from the Hidayah concerning the validity of a prayer when a person prays Asr while knowingly having missed Zuhr. The initial ruling is that the Asr prayer is invalid (fasidah) because of violating the obligation of tartib, unless the person realizes the missed prayer at the very end of Asr time when the time constraint cancels the order obligation. The core dispute is about the consequence when the fardiyyah (obligatory nature) of the Asr prayer is lost due to the tartib violation. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf (the shaykhayn) hold that the original prayer does not become totally invalid; it remains as a nafl (supererogatory) prayer because the tahrimah (opening takbir) was contracted for the prayer with the attribute of fardiyyah, and the loss of the attribute does not necessitate the loss of the essence. They analogize to a person who begins fasting for expiation while poor, then becomes wealthy mid-day: the fast remains valid as nafl, though it doesn't count for expiation. Imam Muhammad argues that since the tahrimah was specifically contracted for the fard of Asr, once that fardiyyah is invalidated, the tahrimah itself is void, and thus the entire prayer is nullified, counting neither as fard nor nafl. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) appears in a scenario where the person laughs loudly (qahqaha) during that prayer. According to the shaykhayn, since the prayer is still a valid prayer (as nafl), the laughter breaks wudu. According to Imam Muhammad, since the prayer is entirely invalid, the laughter occurred outside of prayer and does not break wudu. The passage provides detailed proof for each position, highlighting the nature of the tahrimah and the relationship between the object and its attributes.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) and the state it creates which initiates the prayer and prohibits actions that were previously permissible.
فرضیت (fardiyyah): The quality or attribute of being obligatory (fard). In this context, the prayer was intended as fard, but due to tartib violation, that fardiyyah is invalidated.
قہقہہ (qahqaha): Loud, uncontrollable laughter that invalidates wudu if it occurs during salah in the Hanafi school.
ترتیب (tartib): Order: the obligation to pray prayers in their prescribed sequence (Zuhr before Asr, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what happens to a person's wudu if they laugh loudly (qahqaha) during a prayer that was started as fard but whose fardiyyah was lost due to tartib violation?
A) Wudu is broken because the prayer is valid as nafl
B) Wudu is not broken because the prayer is entirely invalid
C) Wudu is broken only if the laughter is intentional
D) Wudu is not broken because loud laughter never breaks wudu

Key Takeaway
The shaykhayn's position that loss of fardiyyah does not void the entire prayer is the mufta bihi, and it has practical effect on the nullification of wudu by qahqaha.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Missing Tarteeb and Its Effect on Prayer Validity
Explains the dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on whether missing tarteeb invalidates the essence of prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the Sheikhain (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad on the effect of missing tarteeb on the asl salah, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to determine the ruling on wudu-breaking laughter.

Core Idea
Missing tarteeb invalidates the fardiyyah but not the essence — the prayer becomes nafl according to the majority.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person prays Asr while remembering that Zuhr was missed, does the prayer become completely invalid (batil) or does it retain its essence as a nafl? The Sheikhain (Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree on whether the attribute of obligatory status is separable from the prayer's essence. The practical difference appears in unexpected places, such as whether laughing with qahqaha breaks wudu.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify the act: praying Asr while remembering that Zuhr was missed. The ruling is that the prayer is fasid (defective) because tarteeb was wajib and was missed. Note the exception: if Asr is at the end of its time, tarteeb drops and the prayer is valid.
Tarteeb is a condition for the fardiyyah to be fulfilled, not for the prayer itself.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
The dispute is whether the loss of tarteeb invalidates the essence (asl) of the prayer or only its obligatory attribute. The Sheikhain (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) say the essence remains valid as a nafl; Imam Muhammad says the entire prayer is invalid (neither fard nor nafl).
The term 'Sheikhain' here refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, not the two Sahibayn.
3
Analyse Imam Muhammad's proof
Imam Muhammad argues that the tahrimah (opening takbir) is specifically concluded for the obligatory prayer. Since the obligation is invalidated by the missed tarteeb, the tahrimah itself becomes invalid, and thus the entire prayer is void.
This is a position that emphasises the dependency of the means on the end.
4
Analyse the Sheikhain's proof and response
The Sheikhain argue that the tahrimah is concluded for the asl salah which has the attribute of fardiyyah. The attribute can be invalidated without affecting the essence. They draw a qiyas: a destitute person who starts fasting for kaffarah but becomes wealthy during the day — the fast becomes nafl, not invalid. Similarly, here the fardiyyah attribute is lost but the prayer remains as nafl.
The key principle: invalidation of a attribute does not entail invalidation of the essence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference appears when the worshipper laughs with qahqaha during the prayer. According to the Sheikhain, since the asl salah is valid, the laughter breaks wudu. According to Imam Muhammad, since the entire prayer is invalid, the laughter occurs outside prayer and does not break wudu.
The mufta bihi is the Sheikhain's view, which is the majority and preferred in Al-Hidayah.

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے عصر کی نماز پڑھی اور اس کو یہ یاد ہے کہ ابھی تک ظہر نہیں پڑھی ہے تو عصر کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ اس نے ترتیب کو چھوڑ دیا ہے۔ حالانکہ اس پر ترتیب فرض تھی۔ ہاں اگر عصر کی نماز عصر کے آخری وقت میں ادا کی اور یہ یاد ہے کہ عمر نہیں پڑھی ہے تو عصر کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی کیونکہ وقت کا تنگ ہونا ترتیب کو ساقط کر دیتا ہے۔
رہی ہیہ بات کہ ترتیب کے فوت ہونے سے جب فرضیت باطل ہوگئی تو اصل صلوۃ بھی باطل ہوگی یا نہیں ؟ سواس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ بیچین نے فرمایا کہ اصل صلوۃ باطل نہیں ہوگی یعنی ترتیب نہ پائی جانے کی وجہ سے عصر کی نماز کا فرض ادا ہونا اگر چہ باطل ہو گیا لیکن اس کا نفل ہونا باقی ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ عصر کی یہ نماز اداء فرض شمار نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اداء فضل شمار ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ فرضیت باطل ہونے سے اصل نماز بھی ہل ہو جائے گی ۔ یعنی عصر کی یہ نماز نہ فرض شمار ہوگی اور نہ نک شمار ہوگی ۔ شمرہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ظاہر ہوگا کہ جس شخص نے وسعت وقت میں عصر کی نماز شروع کی درانحالیکہ اس کو ظہر کی فائتہ یاد ہے پھر یہ شخص بحالت نماز قہقہہ مارکز ہنس پڑا تو شیخین کے نزدیک اس کا وضو لوٹ جائے گا۔ کیونکہ شیخین کے نزدیک اصل صلاۃ باقی ہے اور بحالت نماز قہقہ لگا کر ہنسنا ناقض وضو ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک وضو نہیں ٹوٹے گا کیونکہ امام محمد کے نزدیک اصل نماز ہی باطل ہو گئی ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک یہ نہ مارنا نماز کی حالت میں نہیں ہوگا۔ اور نماز کی حالت کے علاوہ قہقہ لگا کر ہنسنا ناقض وضو نہیں ہوتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں قہقہہ لگا کر ہنستا ناقض وضو نہیں ہوگا۔
اصل مسئلہ میں امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تحریمہ فریضہ عصر کے لئے منعقد کیا گیا ہے اور ہر وہ چیز کہ جس کے لئے تحریمہ متعقد کیا جائے اب وہ باطل ہو گئی تو تحریمہ بھی باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ تحریمہ اس شے کو حاصل کرنے کا ذریعہ ہوتا ہے پس جب مقصود باطل ہو گیا تو اس کا میلہ اور ذریعہ بھی باطل ہو جائے گا اور جب تحریمہ باطل ہو گیا تو اصل صلاۃ ہی باطل ہوگئی اور جب اصل صلاۃ باطل ہوگئی تو نہ فرض ادا ہوگا
شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تحریمہ منعقد کیا گیا ہے اصل صلاۃ کے لئے جو وصف فرضیت کے ساتھ موصوف ہے اور ترتیب کے فوت ہونے ی وجہ سے عصر کی نماز کا وصف فرضیت باطل ہو گیا ہے۔ ضروری نہیں ہے جیسے کسی شخص نے اپنی تنگدستی اور غربت کی وجہ سے کفارہ یمین کے اور تین روزے رکھنا شروع کر دیئے پھر دن کے درمیان وہ مالدار ہو گیا تو اس کا اصل روزہ باطل نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس روزہ کا کفارہ واقع ہونے کا اف باطل ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی وہ روزہ کفارہ یمین میں شمار نہیں ہو گا۔ البتہ صوم نفل ہو جائے گا۔ اور کفارہ یمین میں اس لئے شمار نہیں ہو گا کہ دار آدمی کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ کفارہ یمین بالا طعام ادا کرے یا بالکسوۃ یا غلام آزاد کرے۔ ان تینوں پر عدم قدرت کی صورت میں روزہ رکھنے کا حکم ہے۔ پس جب اس نے تنگدستی کی وجہ سے روزے کے ساتھ کفارہ ادا کرنا شروع کیا لیکن دن کے اندر روزے کی حالت میں شخص مالدار ہو گیا تو اس روزے کا وصف وقوع کفارہ باطل ہو گیا۔ لیکن اصل روزہ باطل نہیں ہوا۔ پس جس طرح یہاں بطلان وصف بطلان اصل نہیں ہوا۔ اسی طرح متن کے مسئلے میں بھی وصف فرضیت کے باطل ہونے سے اصل نماز باطل نہیں ہوگی۔
Explanation of the issue: A person prayed Asr while remembering that he had not yet prayed Zuhr, so the Asr prayer becomes invalid (fasid) because he left the order (tarteeb) while tarteeb was obligatory upon him. Yes, if he performed Asr at the last time of Asr and remembers that he did not pray Zuhr, then the Asr prayer is valid because the narrowness of time drops the tarteeb. As for the matter that when the obligatory status (fardiyyah) becomes invalid due to the loss of tarteeb, does the essence of the prayer (asl salah) also become invalid or not? There is disagreement about this. So the Sheikhain (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) said that the asl salah does not become invalid, meaning that due to the absence of tarteeb, the performance of the obligation of Asr prayer became invalid, but its being nafl remains. In summary, this Asr prayer will not be counted as an obligatory performance, but as a supererogatory performance. And Imam Muhammad said that with the invalidation of the obligatory status, the asl salah also becomes invalid, i.e., this Asr prayer will not be counted as fard nor as nafl. The fruit of this disagreement will appear in the case where a person started Asr prayer in wide time while remembering his missed Zuhr, then this person laughed with qahqaha (uncontrollable laughter) while in prayer. According to the Sheikhain, his wudu will be broken because, according to them, the asl salah remains, and laughing with qahqaha during prayer breaks wudu, so according to them wudu breaks. According to Imam Muhammad, wudu will not break because, according to him, the asl prayer itself has become invalid, so this laughter does not occur in the state of prayer. And laughing with qahqaha outside the state of prayer does not break wudu, so in this case, laughing with qahqaha is not a breaker of wudu. Regarding the original issue, Imam Muhammad's proof is that the tahrimah (opening takbir) was concluded for the purpose of the Asr obligatory prayer, and everything for which the tahrimah is concluded, if that thing becomes invalid, then the tahrimah also becomes invalid. Because the tahrimah is a means to obtain that thing, so when the objective becomes invalid, its means also become invalid. When the tahrimah becomes invalid, the asl salah itself becomes invalid, and when the asl salah becomes invalid, neither the obligation is fulfilled. The proof of the Sheikhain is that the tahrimah is concluded for the asl salah which is characterized by the attribute of obligatory status, and due to the loss of tarteeb, the attribute of obligatory status of the Asr prayer has become invalid. It is not necessary (that the asl becomes invalid) just like a person who, due to his destitution and poverty, started fasting three days for the expiation of an oath, then he became wealthy during the day. Then his original fast does not become invalid, but the effectiveness of that fast for expiation becomes invalid, i.e., that fast will not be counted for the expiation of the oath; rather, it becomes a supererogatory fast. And it is not counted for the expiation of the oath because it is necessary for a free person to perform expiation for an oath by feeding or clothing or freeing a slave; the ruling to fast is only when unable to do these three. So when he started to perform expiation by fasting due to destitution, but during the day while fasting he became wealthy, the attribute of expiation occurrence of that fast became invalid, but the original fast did not become invalid. Just as here the invalidation of an attribute did not result in the invalidation of the essence, similarly in the issue of the text, the invalidation of the attribute of obligatory status does not cause the asl salah to become invalid.
Source pages p. 226

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute recorded in the commentary on Al-Hidayah. The issue is whether a prayer performed while remembering a missed previous prayer becomes invalid in essence or only in its obligatory quality. The text first states the base ruling: if one prays Asr remembering that Zuhr was missed, the Asr prayer is invalid (fasid) because tarteeb was wajib. However, an exception is noted: if Asr is prayed at the end of its time, the narrowness of time drops the obligation of tarteeb, making the prayer valid. The core dispute arises: does the loss of tarteeb invalidate the prayer entirely (asl salah) or only its status as an obligatory prayer? Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that the entire prayer becomes invalid—it is neither fard nor nafl. The Sheikhain (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the essence of the prayer remains valid as a nafl, though it does not count as the obligatory Asr. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is illustrated by the case of qahqaha (uncontrollable laughter). According to the Sheikhain, since the asl salah remains, laughter during it breaks wudu. According to Imam Muhammad, since the asl salah is invalid, the laughter occurs outside prayer and does not break wudu. Each side provides a proof. Imam Muhammad argues that the tahrimah (opening takbir) was specifically for the obligatory prayer; since the obligation is invalid, the tahrimah itself becomes invalid, and thus the entire prayer is void. The Sheikhain argue that the tahrimah was for the asl salah which has the attribute of obligatory status; the attribute can be invalidated without affecting the essence. They draw a qiyas (analogy) with fasting for expiation: if a destitute person begins fasting for kaffarah but becomes wealthy during the day, the fast becomes nafl, not invalid. Similarly, here the fardiyyah attribute is lost but the prayer remains as nafl. This is a classic Hanafi usuli argument about the relationship between attribute and essence.

Key Terms
ترتیب (tarteeb): The obligation to perform missed prayers in order, i.e., making up a missed Zuhr before praying Asr when one remembers.
فساد موقوف (fasād muwaqqif): Temporary invalidity that can be removed by the occurrence of a large number of prayers (six), after which the prayers become valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa (in the position reported), if a person prays Asr remembering that Zuhr was missed, what is the status of the Asr prayer?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated as the obligation.
B) It is valid as the obligatory Asr.
C) It is invalid as fard but valid as nafl.
D) It is valid only if performed at the end of Asr time.

Key Takeaway
The loss of tarteeb due to remembering a missed prayer does not nullify the essence of the prayer according to the majority of Hanafi imams; it remains valid as a nafl, and the practical effect appears in cases like laughter breaking wudu.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Fasad Muwaqqif vs Fasad Ba't: The Hanafi Dispute on Asr Prayer When Tarteeb is Violated
Intra-Hanafi dispute on suspended vs absolute invalidity in Asr prayer when tarteeb is broken.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fasad muwaqqif and fasad ba't and apply Abu Hanifa's view to determine the validity of a sequence of prayers when tarteeb is violated.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: Asr with broken tarteeb becomes valid after six prayers; Sahibayn: it never becomes valid—dispute over when the cause for dropping tarteeb operates.

This lesson examines a renowned intra-Hanafi dispute about the nature of invalidity when a person prays Asr while remembering a missed Zuhr. Does the invalidity remain forever, or can it be removed by subsequent actions? Imam Abu Hanifa introduces the concept of 'fasad muwaqqif' (suspended invalidity), while his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), argue for 'fasad ba't' (absolute invalidity). The difference hinges on a subtle usul principle: whether the cause for dropping tarteeb is the existence of six prayers or the moment when the sixth prayer is completed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial hukm
A person prays Asr knowing he missed the previous Zuhr. The Asr prayer is invalid (fasid) due to loss of tarteeb. Note that the invalidity is not due to a missing pillar but to violating the required sequence.
Tarteeb is obligatory only when the missed prayer is one to five. This is the baseline.
2
State the dispute: muwaqqif vs ba't
Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the invalidity is 'muwaqqif' (suspended), meaning it can become valid later. The Sahibayn rule that it is 'ba't' (absolute), never becoming valid.
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school itself, so both views are authoritative.
3
Trace Abu Hanifa's reasoning
The cause (illa) of invalidity is the obligation of tarteeb. If the person continues praying the next five prayers (Maghrib, Isha, Fajr, next Zuhr, next Asr) without making up the missed Zuhr, then after the sixth prayer (next Asr), six prayers have been performed after the missed Zuhr. This constitutes kathrat al-fawa'it, which drops the obligation of tarteeb. Since the cause ceases, the invalidity of all six prayers is removed retroactively.
The number six includes the initial Asr plus five subsequent prayers. The missed Zuhr itself is not counted among the six.
4
Trace Sahibayn's reasoning
Sahibayn argue that the ruling (sqt al-tarteeb) follows the cause. The cause for dropping tarteeb is the existence of six missed prayers. At the moment each of the five prayers is performed, there are only 1–5 missed prayers (the missed Zuhr plus possibly others that are invalid). Therefore, tarteeb is still obligatory, and each prayer is absolutely invalid. Even after the sixth is performed, the earlier prayers cannot become valid because the cause did not exist at their time.
Sahibayn emphasize that rulings cannot be retroactive; they apply at the time of the action.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical difference
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's view (fasad muwaqqif). Practically, this means that if a person inadvertently violates tarteeb and continues to pray, his prayers become valid after the sixth one, avoiding the need to repeat them. Sahibayn's view would require repeating all six prayers.
The Hanafi school often follows the more lenient view when it is well-supported by usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم العصر يفسد فسادا موقوفا حتى لوصلى ست صلوات، ولم يعد الظهر، انقلب الكل جائزا، وهذا عند ابي حنيفة، وعندهما يفسد فسادا باتا لاجواز لها بحال، وقد عرف ذلك في موضع
ترجمہ پھر عصر فساد موقوف کے طور پر فاسد ہوگی۔ حتی کہ اگر چھ نمازیں پڑھیں اور ظہر کا اعادہ نہیں کیا تو تمام نمازیں جائز ہو کرنا جائیں گی۔ یہ حکم امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک عصر قطعی طور پر فاسد ہوگی۔ وہ اب کسی حال میں جائز نہیں ہے ہے۔ اور نیا اپنے موقع پر معلوم ہو چکا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ مذکورہ یعنی عصر کی نماز پڑھی اور یہ یادر ہے کہ ظہر کی نماز بھی نہیں پڑھی ہے۔ تو اس صورت میں فرمایا تھا کہ ترتیب ۔ فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے عصر کی نماز فاسد ہے لیکن اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ عصر کی یہ نماز موقوفا غامد ہوئی ہے یا قطعا اور حتماً۔ سوامام الانبا نے کہا کہ عصر کی نماز موقوفا فاسد ہوئی ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر چھ نمازیں پڑھ لیں ۔ یعنی آج کی عصر سے کال آئندہ کی عصر تک اور ظہر کی قائین ابھی تک قضاء نہیں کیا ہے تو یہ سب نمازیں جائز ہو جائیں گی۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ عصر اور اس کے بعد پانچ نمازوں تک فساد کی علت وجوب ترتیب ہے یعنی عصر، مغرب، عش ، فجر اور اگلے دن کاکی اس لئے فاسد ہیں کہ اس نے ابھی تک کل گذشتہ کی ظہر کو ادا نہیں کیا ہے۔ حالانکہ ترتیب کا مقتضی یہ تھا کہ پہلے کل گذشتہ کی ظہر کی قضا لیکن جب اس نے اگلے دن کی عصر ادا کی تو اب گویا کل گذشتہ کی ظہر کے بعد چھ نمازیں فاسد ہوئیں اور چھ نمازوں سے کثرت ثابت جاتی ہے اور پہلے گذر چکا کہ کثرت فوائت سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جاتی ہے پس جب اس شخص نے اگلے دن کی عصر ادا کر لی تو کثرت نوال سے ترتیب ساقط ہوگئی اور جب ترتیب ساقط ہوگئی تو تمام نمازیں جائز ہو جائیں گی۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ عصر کی نماز حتما اور قطعا فاسد ہو جائے گی یعنی کسی حال میں بھی جائز نہیں ہو سکتی ہے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ایک شخص نے ظہر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے۔ پھر اس کے بعد کی پانچ وقت تک پانچ نمازیں اپنے اپنے وقت پر پڑھیں تو صاحبین کے ناری پانچوں فاسد ہیں۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ترتیب ساقط ہونے کی علت کثرت فوائت ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ حکم علت سے مؤخر ہو پس سقوط ترتیب کا حکم اس وقت ہوگا جبکہ فوائت کثیر (چھ) ہو جائیں۔ لہذا ائتہ یعنی نماز ظہر کی قضاء کئے بغیر اگر پانچ نمازیں اہے۔ وقت میں پڑھیں تو پانچوں نمازیں قطعی طور پر فاسد ہو جائیں گی۔ کیونکہ سقوط ترتیب کی علت نہیں پائی گئی۔
Then Asr becomes invalid with a suspended invalidity (fasad muwaqqif), such that if he prays six prayers and does not repeat Zuhr, all become permissible. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Sahibayn), it becomes invalid with an absolute invalidity (fasad bat), not permissible in any case. And that has been known in its place. Translation: Then Asr will be invalid in the manner of suspended invalidity. Such that if he prays six prayers and does not repeat Zuhr, all prayers become permissible. This ruling is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And according to the Sahibayn, Asr will be absolutely invalid, not permissible in any case. And it has been known in its place. Explanation of the mentioned issue: He prayed Asr and remembers that he did not pray Zuhr. In this case, it was said that due to the loss of tarteeb, the Asr prayer is invalid. But there is disagreement whether this Asr prayer is invalid in a suspended manner or absolutely and definitively. So Imam al-A'zam (Abu Hanifa) said that Asr prayer is invalid in a suspended manner. Such that if he prays six prayers, i.e., from today's Asr to tomorrow's Asr, and the Zuhr qada is not yet performed, then all these prayers become permissible. The proof is that the cause of invalidity for Asr and the five prayers after it is the obligation of tarteeb. That is, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, Fajr, and the next day's Zuhr are invalid because he has not yet performed yesterday's Zuhr, while the requirement of tarteeb was to first perform the qada of yesterday's Zuhr. But when he performed the next day's Asr, now six prayers became invalid after yesterday's Zuhr. And from six prayers, a large number (kathrah) is established. And it has passed earlier that large number of missed prayers drops tarteeb. So when this person performed the next day's Asr, tarteeb dropped due to the large number, and when tarteeb dropped, all prayers become permissible. The Sahibayn said that Asr prayer will be invalid absolutely and definitively, meaning it can never be permissible in any case. Its scenario: A person did not pray Zuhr, then he prayed five prayers at their respective times for the next five prayer times. According to the Sahibayn, all five are invalid. The proof of the Sahibayn is that the cause for dropping tarteeb is a large number of missed prayers, and the rule is that the ruling is subsequent to the cause. So the ruling of dropping tarteeb will occur only when the missed prayers become numerous (six). Therefore, if without performing the qada of Zuhr, he prays five prayers in their times, all five prayers are absolutely invalid because the cause for dropping tarteeb is not found.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage continues the intra-Hanafi dispute, now focusing on the concept of 'fasad muwaqqif' (suspended invalidity) versus 'fasad ba't' (absolute invalidity). The text first quotes the Arabic from Al-Hidayah: 'then Asr becomes invalid with a suspended invalidity, such that if he prays six prayers and does not repeat Zuhr, all become permissible. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Sahibayn), it becomes invalid with an absolute invalidity, not permissible in any case.' The Urdu commentary expands: If a person prays Asr remembering missed Zuhr, the Asr is invalid due to loss of tarteeb. But what kind of invalidity? Imam Abu Hanifa says it is 'fasad muwaqqif'—a temporary invalidity that can be removed if a large number of prayers accumulate. Specifically, if he continues praying the next five prayers (Maghrib, Isha, Fajr, the next day's Zuhr, and Asr) without making up the missed Zuhr, then six prayers in total have been performed after the missed Zuhr. Once the sixth prayer (the next day's Asr) is complete, the number of missed prayers reaches six, which constitutes 'kathrah fawa'it' (large number of missed prayers). A prior rule is that kathrah fawa'it drops the obligation of tarteeb. Therefore, all six prayers become valid. The logic: the cause (illa) of invalidity is the existence of tarteeb; when tarteeb drops, invalidity ceases. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. They say the invalidity is absolute (fasad ba't). Their proof: the ruling of dropping tarteeb is contingent on the existence of a large number (six) of missed prayers. At the time of each prayer, the number of missed prayers is less than six, so tarteeb still applies, and each prayer is invalid and can never become valid later. The five prayers remain invalid even if later a sixth is added because the ruling cannot retroactively change. This highlights a subtle usuli principle: whether the illa (cause) for dropping tarteeb is the existence of six invalid prayers (Abu Hanifa's view) or the occurrence of a large number at the moment of prayer (Sahibayn's view).

Key Terms
فساد موقوف (fasād muwaqqif): Suspended invalidity: a prayer that is initially invalid but can become valid upon the fulfillment of a condition (here, the accumulation of six prayers causing tarteeb to drop).
فساد بات (fasād bā't): Absolute invalidity: a prayer that is invalid from the outset and can never become valid.
کثرت فوائت (kathrat al-fawa'it): The condition of having six or more missed prayers, which drops the obligation of sequencing (tarteeb) in making them up.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Sahibayn, why does the Asr prayer never become valid even after the person prays six prayers?
A) Because the missed Zuhr was not made up.
B) Because the invalidity is absolute and the cause for dropping tarteeb (six missed prayers) must exist at the time of each prayer.
C) Because the person did not intend to follow tarteeb.
D) Because the prayer was performed before its time.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when tarteeb is violated in one prayer, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the invalidity is suspended and can be lifted by performing a total of six prayers, while the Two Companions hold it is absolute and cannot be undone—a key intra-madhhab dispute hinging on the timing of the cause.

Ruling on Praying Fajr Without Having Performed Witr
States the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the effect of missing Witr before Fajr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of Fajr prayer when Witr is missed and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Witr's wajib status leads to tarteeb; Sahibayn's sunnah view means no tarteeb, so Fajr is valid.

You may have heard that Witr is an emphasized prayer. But what happens if you pray Fajr while remembering that you missed Witr the night before? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagreed on this very question. The dispute exposes a deeper difference: the legal weight of Witr itself. This lesson will walk you through that dispute and its practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its scenario
The act is praying Fajr while remembering that Witr has not been performed. Note that the person is mindful of the omission, not forgetful.
Forgetfulness would change the ruling—tarteeb is only binding if one remembers.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa rules the Fajr prayer invalid (fasid); the Sahibayn rule it valid (sahih).
3
Identify the root cause of ikhtilaf
The disagreement stems from the legal status of Witr. Abu Hanifa considers Witr wajib (obligatory, though lesser than fard). The Sahibayn consider it sunnah mu'akkadah (highly recommended).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not between madhahib.
4
Apply the principle of tarteeb
Tarteeb (order) is required between obligatory prayers (fard and, for Abu Hanifa, wajib). If Witr is wajib, then one must pray it before Fajr; violating this order invalidates the later prayer. If Witr is sunnah, no tarteeb applies, so Fajr remains valid.
The principle: 'La tarteeba bayna al-fara'id wa al-sunan' — no order between obligatory and sunnah prayers.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view: Witr is sunnah mu'akkadah, so Fajr is valid. This is the operative position for fatwa.
The tarjih is based on weight of evidence and practicality.

Commentary
This brief passage introduces a related ruling: If a person prays Fajr while remembering that they have not performed Witr (the night prayer), the Fajr prayer is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn). The reason for the difference is the status of Witr. Abu Hanifa considers Witr to be wajib (obligatory, though of a lower category than fard), while the Sahibayn consider it sunnah (recommended). Since tarteeb (order) is only required between obligatory prayers (fara'id and possibly wajibat according to Abu Hanifa), if Witr is wajib, then missing it before Fajr invalidates Fajr, just like missing a fard. But if Witr is sunnah, there is no tarteeb between sunnah and fard, so Fajr remains valid. This passage is likely the beginning of a longer discussion; the text cuts off after 'ثم تود' (which may mean 'then he prays...'). The commentary should be limited to what is present in the clean text.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, considered wajib by Abu Hanifa and sunnah by the Sahibayn.
ترتيب (tarteeb): The required sequential order of prayers: a later fard or wajib prayer must follow an earlier one without another obligatory prayer in between.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute over the validity of Fajr after missing Witr is resolved by adopting the Sahibayn's position that Witr is sunnah, making Fajr valid.

Ruling on 'Asr Prayer When Missing Zuhr: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on 'Asr prayer invalidity when Zuhr is missed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the invalidity of 'Asr prayer when Zuhr is missed, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: invalidity is temporary; Sahibayn: permanent — the difference hinges on when order drops.

This lesson explores a key intra-Hanafi dispute about the 'Asr prayer prayed while remembering a missed Zuhr. The central question: is the invalidity temporary or permanent? The answer affects whether subsequent prayers can become valid, providing relief for those with a backlog of missed prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the act
The issue is the ruling on praying 'Asr while knowing that Zuhr has been missed. The act is invalid due to missing tartib (order) between prayers.
Tartib in qada' is a condition according to the Hanafi school.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the invalidity is suspended (fasād mawqūf): the 'Asr prayer becomes valid once six prayers (including the missed Zuhr) accumulate without making up Zuhr.
Six prayers means the missed Zuhr plus five subsequent prayers up to the next 'Asr.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the invalidity is permanent (fasād bā'in): the 'Asr prayer and all subsequent prayers after it remain invalid forever.
They argue that the cause for dropping order (kathrat al-fawa'it) is not yet present.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
According to Abu Hanifa, if one prays up to the next 'Asr without making up Zuhr, all six prayers become valid. According to the Sahibayn, they remain invalid.
This affects whether the person must repeat those prayers.
5
Note the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hidayah does not specify tarjih, but later Hanafi authorities generally prefer Abu Hanifa's view, making it the mufta bihi.
This reflects the principle that hardship is alleviated when many prayers are missed.

ترجمہ: پھر عصر فساد موقوف کے طور پر فاسد ہوگی۔ حتی کہ اگر چھ نمازیں پڑھیں اور ظہر کا اعادہ نہیں کیا تو تمام نمازیں جائز ہو کر جائیں گی۔ یہ حکم امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک عصر قطعی طور پر فاسد ہوگی، وہ اب کسی حال میں جائز نہیں ہوگی۔ اور یہ اپنے موقع پر معلوم ہو چکا ہے۔

Chapter: Making up Missed Prayers. Then 'Asr prayer becomes invalid with suspended invalidity such that if he prays six prayers and does not make up Zuhr, all become valid. This is according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it becomes invalid with permanent invalidity, having no validity at all. This is known in its place. Translation: Then 'Asr will be invalid with suspended invalidity. So much so that if he prays six prayers and does not repeat Zuhr, all prayers will become valid. This ruling is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions, 'Asr will be entirely invalid, it will not be valid in any case. And this has been known in its place. Explanation: The mentioned issue: he prayed 'Asr while remembering that he has not prayed Zuhr. In this case, it was said that due to the loss of order (tartib), 'Asr prayer is invalid. But there is a difference: is this 'Asr prayer invalid with suspended invalidity or permanently? Imam Abu Hanifa said that 'Asr prayer is invalid with suspended invalidity, such that if he prays six prayers, i.e., from today's 'Asr until tomorrow's 'Asr, and he has not yet made up Zuhr, then all these prayers become valid. The proof is that the cause of invalidity for 'Asr and the five prayers after it is the obligation of order, i.e., 'Asr, Maghrib, 'Isha, Fajr, and next day's Zuhr are invalid because he has not yet performed yesterday's Zuhr, whereas order requires that he first make up yesterday's Zuhr. But when he performed tomorrow's 'Asr, now six prayers have become invalid after yesterday's Zuhr, and from six prayers multitude is established, and it has passed before that multitude of missed prayers drops the requirement of order. So when this person performed tomorrow's 'Asr, order dropped due to multitude of missed prayers, and when order dropped, all prayers become valid. The two companions said that 'Asr prayer will be entirely and permanently invalid, i.e., it cannot be valid in any case. Its scenario: a person has not prayed Zuhr, then he prays five prayers in their times; according to the two, all five are invalid. Their proof is that the cause for dropping order is multitude of missed prayers, and the rule is that the ruling is delayed from the cause; so the ruling of dropping order will occur only when the missed prayers become many (six). Hence, now (without making up Zuhr), if he prays five prayers in their time, all five will be entirely invalid because the cause for dropping order is not found.
Source pages p. 227

Commentary
This passage discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the 'Asr prayer when one remembers missing Zuhr. The author first states the matn: 'then 'Asr becomes invalid with suspended invalidity...' He then provides the Urdu translation and a detailed commentary. The ruling: if one prays 'Asr while remembering that he has not prayed Zuhr, the 'Asr prayer is invalid due to missing the required order (tartib) between prayers. However, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that this invalidity is suspended (mawquf), meaning it can be removed if a sufficient number of prayers accumulate. Specifically, if the person goes on to pray six prayers (from this 'Asr to the next day's 'Asr) without making up Zuhr, the requirement of order drops due to the multitude of missed prayers (kathrat al-fawa'it), and all those prayers become valid. His proof (dalil) is the established principle that when missed prayers become many (six or more), the order between them is no longer obligatory, as this would cause undue hardship. The two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree, holding that the invalidity is permanent (battan). They argue that the cause for dropping order is the actual occurrence of six missed prayers (kathrat al-fawa'it). Since the person has only five prayers after 'Asr (Maghrib, 'Isha, Fajr, Zuhr of next day, and 'Asr of next day? Actually, the calculation: the missed Zuhr plus 'Asr, Maghrib, 'Isha, Fajr, and next day's Zuhr make six? The text says: if he prays five prayers after 'Asr without making up Zuhr, they remain invalid because the condition of six is not met. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that according to Abu Hanifa, the later prayers can become valid if the count reaches six, while according to the Sahibayn, they remain invalid forever.

Key Terms
فساد موقوف (fasād mawqūf): Invalidity that is suspended pending a condition; if the condition is met, the act becomes valid retroactively.
فساد بائن (fasād bā'in): Permanent invalidity that cannot become valid under any circumstance.
كثرة الفوائت (kathrat al-fawā'it): A multitude of missed prayers, specifically six or more, which drops the requirement to pray them in order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Witr's Legal Status and Its Effect on Fajr Validity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Witr and tartīb

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on Fajr's validity when Witr is missed, and apply the same principle to the 'Isha case.

Core Idea
Whether Witr is wajib or sunnah determines if order with Fajr is required.

This passage tackles a practical scenario: you pray Fajr but remember you haven't prayed Witr. Is your Fajr valid? The answer depends on a fundamental difference between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding the legal status of Witr. Understanding this dispute not only clarifies this specific ruling but also illustrates how a single principle—tartib (order) between prayers—yields different results based on the classification of an act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
The passage opens with the ruling: Fajr prayed while remembering missed Witr is invalid (fāsid) according to Abu Hanifa, but valid according to Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Pinpoint the exact point of disagreement.
Focus on the hukm: invalid vs. valid.
2
Trace the Underlying Cause
The text explicitly states the basis: Abu Hanifa considers Witr wājib, Sahibayn consider it sunnah. Since tartīb (order) is required between farā'id (including wājibāt) but not between a fard and a sunnah, the classification of Witr directly affects the ruling.
Tartīb is the key principle at work.
3
Apply the Same Principle to the 'Isha Case
The passage extends the logic: a person prays 'Isha, then makes fresh wudu and prays the sunnah and Witr, only to discover 'Isha was invalid (no wudu). According to Abu Hanifa, he repeats 'Isha and its sunnah but not Witr; according to Sahibayn, he repeats Witr as well. Analyze why.
Witr's independence (Abu Hanifa) vs. dependence on 'Isha (Sahibayn) is the key.
4
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilāf)
In the first case, the practical difference is whether Fajr must be repeated. In the second, it's whether Witr must be repeated. Note how a single difference (wujūb vs. sunnah) cascades into multiple divergent rulings.
This shows the real impact of a theoretical disagreement.

و لو صلى الفجر وهو ذاكر انه لم يوتر، فهى فاسدة عند ابي حنيفة خلافا لهما، وهذا بناء على ان الوتر واجب عنده سنة عندهما، ولا ترتيب فيما بين الفرائض والسنن، وعلى هذا اذا صلى العشاء، ثم توضأ و صلى السنة و الوتر، ثم تبين انه صلى العشاء بغير طهارة ، فانه يعيد العشاء والسنة دون الوتر، لان الوتر فرض على حدة عنده، وعندهما يعيد الوتر ايضا لكونه تبعا للعشاء، والله اعلم
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے فجر کی نماز پڑھی اور یہ یاد ہے کہ وتر کی نماز ادا نہیں کی ہے، تو یہ فاسد ہے، ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک، صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے۔ اور یہ اس بات پر مبنی ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک وتر واجب ہے، صاحبین کے نزدیک سنت ہے اور فرائض اور سنن کے درمیان ترتیب نہیں ہے۔ اور اسی بناء پر اگر عشاء کی نماز پڑھی پھر وضو کیا اور سنت اور نماز وتر پڑھیں پھر ظاہر ہوا کہ عشاء بغیر طہارت کے پڑھی تھی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک عشاء اور سنت دونوں کا اعادہ کرے نہ کہ وتر کا، کیونکہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک وتر علیحدہ فرض ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وتر کا بھی اعادہ کرے کیونکہ وہ عشاء کے تابع ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے فجر کی نماز پڑھی، حال یہ کہ اس نے وتر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی تھی، اور اس کو وتر نہ پڑھنے کا یاد بھی ہے تو اس صورت میں امام صاحب کے نزدیک فجر کی نماز فاسد ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک فاسد نہیں ہے۔ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان یہ اختلاف اس بات پر مبنی ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک نماز وتر واجب ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک سنت ہے۔ اور یہ بات طے شدہ ہے کہ ترتیب فقط فرائض کے درمیان واجب ہے فرائض اور سنتوں کے درمیان واجب نہیں ہے۔ پس چونکہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک وتر واجب ہے اس لئے وتر اور فجر کے درمیان ترتیب واجب ہوگی، اور مذکورہ صورت میں چونکہ ترتیب موجود نہیں ہے اس لئے فجر کی نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وتر سنت ہے اس لئے فجر اور وتر کے درمیان ترتیب واجب نہ ہوگی اور چونکہ وتر اور فجر کے درمیان ترتیب واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے فجر کی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی اگرچہ یہ یاد ہے کہ وتر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے۔
نماز عشاء کے بعد نئے وضو سے سنت ووتر ادا کئے پھر معلوم ہوا عشاء بغیر وضو پڑھی ہے تو کیا حکم ہے؟ اسی اصول پر کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک وتر واجب ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک سنت ہے، اگر کسی نے عشاء کی نماز پڑھ لی پھر وضو کیا اور عشاء کے بعد کی سنتیں اور نماز وتر ادا کی، پھر واضح ہوا کہ عشاء کی نماز بغیر وضو کے ادا کی ہے۔ تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عشاء کی نماز اور سنت دونوں کا اعادہ کرے گا، وتر کا اعادہ نہیں کرے گا۔ وتر کا اعادہ تو اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ وتر امام صاحب کے نزدیک واجب ہے اور اس کو اس کے وقت میں بہ ترتیب ادا بھی کر لیا ہے کیونکہ وتر کا وقت وہی ہے جو عشاء کا وقت ہے۔ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ عشاء اور وتر میں ترتیب نہیں پائی گئی، تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عذر نسیان کی وجہ سے ترتیب ساقط ہوگئی ہے، لہذا وتر کا اعادہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور سنت کا اعادہ اس لئے ہوگا کہ سنت فرض کے تابع ہوتی ہے، پس جب فرض کا اعادہ ہو گا تو اس کے تابع کا اعادہ بھی ضرور ہو گا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وتر چونکہ سنت ہے اور سنت عشاء کے فرضوں کے تابع ہے اس لئے عشاء کی نماز کے ساتھ وتر کا اعادہ بھی ضروری ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم
Ruling on praying Fajr without having prayed Witr. And if he prays Fajr while remembering that he did not pray Witr, then it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Sahibayn). This is based on the fact that Witr is wajib according to him and sunnah according to them, and there is no order between obligatory and sunnah prayers. And on this basis, if he prayed 'Isha, then performed ablution and prayed the sunnah and Witr, then it became clear that he prayed 'Isha without purification, then he repeats 'Isha and the sunnah but not Witr, because Witr is a separate obligatory prayer according to him. And according to the two, he repeats Witr as well because it is dependent on 'Isha. And Allah knows best. Translation: And if he prayed Fajr while remembering that he has not performed Witr prayer, then it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. The two companions differ. And this is based on the fact that according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) Witr is wajib, according to the two it is sunnah, and there is no order between obligatory and sunnah prayers. And on this basis, if he prayed 'Isha, then made wudu and prayed sunnah and Witr, then it became apparent that 'Isha was prayed without purification, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, he should repeat 'Isha and the sunnah, not Witr, because according to Imam, Witr is a separate obligatory prayer. And according to the two, he should also repeat Witr because it is dependent on 'Isha. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The scenario is that a person prayed Fajr while he had not prayed Witr, and he remembers that he did not pray Witr. In this case, according to Imam, Fajr prayer is invalid, and according to the two, it is not invalid. This difference between Imam and the two is based on the fact that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Witr prayer is wajib, and according to the two, it is sunnah. And it is established that order is only obligatory between obligatory prayers, not between obligatory and sunnah prayers. So since according to Abu Hanifa, Witr is wajib, order is obligatory between Witr and Fajr, and in the mentioned scenario, since order is not present, Fajr prayer becomes invalid. According to the two, since Witr is sunnah, order is not obligatory between Fajr and Witr, and since order is not obligatory, Fajr prayer does not become invalid even if he remembers not having prayed Witr. The ruling on performing sunnah and Witr after 'Isha with fresh wudu, then discovering 'Isha was without wudu: On the same principle, if someone prayed 'Isha, then made wudu and performed the sunnah after 'Isha and Witr prayer, then it became clear that 'Isha was performed without wudu. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, he should repeat 'Isha and the sunnah, not Witr. Witr is not repeated because according to Imam, Witr is wajib and he has performed it in its time properly, because the time of Witr is the same as the time of 'Isha. At most, it can be said that order between 'Isha and Witr was not observed; the answer is that due to the excuse of forgetfulness, order is dropped, so repeating Witr is not necessary. Sunnah is repeated because sunnah is dependent on the obligatory prayer; when the obligatory is repeated, its dependent must also be repeated. According to the two, since Witr is a sunnah and sunnah is dependent on the obligatory of 'Isha, repeating Witr along with 'Isha is necessary. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of missing Witr on the validity of Fajr prayer, and a related case of 'Isha. The matn states that if one prays Fajr while remembering that he has not prayed Witr, Abu Hanifa rules the Fajr invalid, while the Sahibayn rule it valid. The underlying cause ('illa) is the status of Witr: Abu Hanifa considers Witr wajib, the Sahibayn consider it sunnah. Since order (tartib) is only required between obligatory prayers (fard and wajib according to Hanafi terminology), if Witr is wajib, then it must be prayed before Fajr; failing that, Fajr is invalid due to missing order. If Witr is sunnah, no order is required between it and Fajr, so Fajr remains valid. The commentary then applies this principle to a secondary case: a person prays 'Isha, then with fresh wudu prays the sunnah and Witr, then discovers 'Isha was invalid due to lack of wudu. Abu Hanifa says: repeat 'Isha and the sunnah, but not Witr. Why? Because Witr is an independent wajib prayer; its time is the same as 'Isha, and the forgetfulness of 'Isha's impurity excuses the order between 'Isha and Witr. The sunnah is repeated because it is dependent on the fard (i.e., the sunnah of 'Isha follows the fard). The Sahibayn say: repeat Witr as well, because for them Witr is sunnah and thus follows 'Isha like any other sunnah. This shows how a difference in the classification of an act affects multiple rulings.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): An odd-numbered prayer (usually 3 rak'ahs) performed after 'Isha, considered wājib by Abu Hanifa and sunnah by the Sahibayn.
ترتيب (tartīb): The obligation to pray missed prayers in their correct chronological order, applied between farā'id and wājibāt in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on Fajr prayer if one remembers not having prayed Witr?
A) Fajr is valid because Witr is sunnah.
B) Fajr is invalid because Witr is wājib and order is required.
C) Fajr must be repeated only if Witr was prayed after it.
D) Fajr is valid but Witr must be made up immediately.

Key Takeaway
The legal status of Witr (wājib vs. sunnah) determines the validity of Fajr when Witr is missed, illustrating how a single principle can produce different rulings within a madhhab.

Sujud al-Sahw: Definition and Purpose
Defines Sujud al-Sahw and its causal relationship with forgetfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Sujud al-Sahw and explain the linguistic relationship between 'sujud' and 'sahw' in the idafah construction.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw compensates prayer deficiencies from forgetfulness—its name shows the cause.

Having completed the sections on performing prayers on time (ada) and making up missed ones (qada), the author now turns to a crucial topic: how to rectify errors that occur in prayer due to forgetfulness. This introductory passage defines Sujud al-Sahw and explains that its name reflects the causal relationship between forgetfulness and the prostration, setting the stage for the detailed rulings to follow.

Guided Path
1
Understand the chapter's placement
Recognize that after discussing ada and qada, the author introduces a topic that addresses defects in these prayers. Sujud al-Sahw is the mechanism to compensate for such defects.
The passage explicitly states this sequence.
2
Identify the definition of Sujud al-Sahw
Locate the statement: 'that which compensates for the deficiency occurring in performance and makeup, i.e., Sujud al-Sahw.' This is the core definition.
3
Analyze the linguistic construction
The passage explains that 'Sujud al-Sahw' is an idafah (construct state) where the cause (sahw – forgetfulness) is added to the effect (sujud – prostration). This highlights that forgetfulness is the reason for the prostration.
This is an example of idafah al-musabbab ila al-sabab.
4
Recognize the purpose
The purpose of Sujud al-Sahw is to compensate (talaafi) for shortfalls in prayer caused by forgetfulness. It is not a punishment but a corrective act that perfects the prayer.
This understanding is essential for the detailed rules that follow.

Source Text

باب سجود السهو
ترجمہ: (یہ) باب سہو کے سجدوں کے (بیان میں) ہے۔
تشریح: ادا اور قضاء کے بیان سے فراغت پا کر اب اس چیز کو بیان کریں گے جو ادا اور قضاء میں واقع ہونے والے نقصان کی تلافی کرے، یعنی سجدہ سہو۔ سجود السہو کی ترکیب اضافت المسبب الی السبب کے قبیلہ سے ہے، کیونکہ نماز کے اندر سہو ہی سجدہ کا سبب ہے۔
Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. Translation: This chapter is (for) the prostrations of forgetfulness. Explanation: After completing the discussion of performance (ada) and makeup (qada), we will now discuss that which compensates for the deficiency occurring in performance and makeup, i.e., Sujud al-Sahw. The construction 'Sujud al-Sahw' is of the type idafah of the cause to the effect (musabbab ila al-sabab), because forgetfulness in prayer is the cause of this prostration.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw (Prostration of Forgetfulness). The author first provides the chapter title in Arabic, then an Urdu translation, and a brief explanation. After completing the section on how to perform prayers on time (ada) and make up missed ones (qada), the author turns to a topic that addresses defects that may occur in these prayers, specifically those caused by forgetfulness. The linguistic construction 'Sujud al-Sahw' is explained as an idafah in which the cause (forgetfulness) is added to the effect (prostration), meaning the prostration is caused by forgetfulness. The purpose of these prostrations is to compensate for any shortfall or error that occurred in the prayer due to forgetfulness, thereby perfecting the prayer. This sets the stage for the detailed rulings that follow in the chapter.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Two additional prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for errors or omissions caused by forgetfulness.
سہو (sahw): Forgetfulness that occurs during prayer, leading to an omission or addition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To invalidate a prayer if a mistake is made.
B) To compensate for deficiencies in prayer caused by forgetfulness.
C) To prolong the prayer for extra reward.
D) To mark the end of a prayer.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw compensates prayer deficiencies from forgetfulness; its name reveals the causal link between forgetfulness and prostration.

Tartib Between Witr and Fajr: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tartib between witr and fajr with two scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on witr and apply the principle of tartib to determine the validity of prayers when sequence is broken.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school; tartib is required only between wajib acts, not between wajib and sunnah.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the requirement of order (tartib) between witr and Fajr prayer. The difference stems from the legal status of witr: is it wajib or sunnah? The answer determines whether Fajr is valid if performed without having prayed witr. We will examine two scenarios that illustrate the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dispute centers on the legal status of witr (wajib vs. sunnah) and its impact on the requirement of tartib between prayers.
Tartib is a condition for validity only among acts of the same category (fard/wajib).
2
Analyze Scenario 1: Fajr without witr
A person prays Fajr while remembering they did not pray witr. According to Abu Hanifa, Fajr is invalid (fasid) because witr is wajib, and tartib is required. According to the Sahibayn, Fajr is valid because witr is sunnah and no tartib is required between sunnah and fard.
3
Analyze Scenario 2: Isha invalid, then sunnah and witr performed
A person prays Isha without wudu, then later prays the sunnah and witr. Upon discovering the invalidity of Isha, according to Abu Hanifa, only Isha and its sunnah are repeated (witr is independent wajib already valid). According to the Sahibayn, witr is also repeated as it is subordinate to Isha.
The difference again stems from witr's status: independent wajib vs. sunnah subordinate to Isha.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that witr is wajib, following Imam Abu Hanifa. Therefore, tartib is required and the rulings of Abu Hanifa are operative for fatwa.
This tarjih is based on stronger dalil and is the view adopted in Al-Hidayah and later works.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
If someone prays Fajr after having performed witr, but then remembers that witr was invalid (e.g., due to impurity), the tartib is broken and Fajr must be repeated.
The principle applies whenever a wajib prayer is missed before a fard.

Source Text

صاحبین کے نزدیک و تر عشاء سے ہے اس لئے فجر اور وتر کے درمیان ترتیب واجب نہ ہوگی اور چونکہ وتر اور فجر کے درمیان ترتیب واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے فجر کی نماز فاسد نہ ہوگی۔ اگرچہ یہ یاد ہے کہ وتر کی نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے۔ نماز عشاء کے بعد نئے وضو سے سنت ووتر ادا کئے پھر معلوم ہوا عشاء بغیر وضو پڑھی ہے تو کیا حکم ہے، اسی اصول پر کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک وتر واجب ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک سنت ہے، اگر کسی نے عشاء کی نماز پڑھ لی پھر وضو کیا اور عشاء کے بعد کی نتیں اور نماز وتر ادا کی۔ پھر واضح ہوا کہ عشاء کی نماز بغیر وضو کے ادا کی ہے۔ تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک عشاء کی نماز اور سنت دونوں کا اعادہ کرے گا وتر کا اعادہ نہیں کرے گا۔ وتر کا اعادہ تو اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ وتر امام صاحب کے نزدیک واجب ہے اور اس کو اس کے وقت میں مہارت کے ساتھ ادا بھی کر لیا ہے کیونکہ وتر کا وقت وہی ہے جو عشاء کا وقت ہے۔ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ عشاء اور وتر میں ترتیب نہیں پائی گئی ۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عذر نسیان کی وجہ سے ترتیب ساقط ہوگئی ہے۔ لہذا وتر کا اعادہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور سنت کا اعادہ اس لئے ہوگا کہ سنت فرض کے تابع ہوتی ہے۔ پس جب فرض کا اعادہ ہو گا تو اس کے تابع کا اعادہ بھی ضرور ہو گا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک وتر چونکہ نت ہے اور سنت عشاء کے فرضوں کے تابع ہے اس لئے عشاء کی نماز کے ساتھ وتر کا اعادہ بھی ضروری ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
If he prays Fajr while remembering that he has not performed the witr prayer, then it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This is based on the fact that witr in his view is wajib, while in their view it is sunnah, and there is no order (tartib) between obligatory prayers and sunnahs. And on this basis, if he prays Isha, then performs wudu and prays the sunnah and witr, then it becomes apparent that he prayed Isha without purity, then he repeats Isha and the sunnah but not the witr, because witr is a separate obligation in his view, while in their view he also repeats the witr because it is subordinate to Isha. And Allah knows best.
Translation: If he prayed Fajr and he remembers that he has not performed the witr prayer, then it is invalid. There is a difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. And this is based on the fact that in Imam's view, witr is wajib, and in the Sahibayn's view it is sunnah, and there is no order between obligatory acts and sunnahs. On this basis, if he prayed Isha, then made wudu and prayed the sunnah and witr, then it became clear that Isha was prayed without purity, then according to Imam, he repeats Isha and the sunnah but not witr, because in Imam's view witr is a separate obligation, and according to the Sahibayn he also repeats witr because it is subordinate to Isha. And Allah knows best. Explanation: The scenario is that a person prayed Fajr while he had not prayed witr, and he remembers that he did not pray witr. In this case, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, Fajr prayer is invalid, and according to the Sahibayn it is not invalid. This difference between Imam and the Sahibayn is based on the fact that in Imam's view, witr prayer is wajib, and in the Sahibayn's view it is sunnah. It is established that order is only required between obligatory acts, not between obligatory acts and sunnahs. So since in Imam Abu Hanifa's view, witr is wajib, therefore order between witr and Fajr is required. In the mentioned case, since order is not present, Fajr prayer becomes invalid. According to the Sahibayn, witr is from Isha, so order between Fajr and witr is not required, and since order is not required, Fajr prayer does not become invalid, even if he remembers that he has not prayed witr. After Isha prayer, with a new wudu, he performed the sunnah and witr, then it became known that Isha was prayed without wudu. What is the ruling? On the same principle: in Imam's view, witr is wajib, in Sahibayn's view it is sunnah. If someone prayed Isha, then made wudu and performed the sunnan after Isha and witr prayer, then it became clear that the Isha prayer was performed without wudu. Then in Imam Abu Hanifa's view, he will repeat Isha prayer and the sunnah, but will not repeat witr. He will not repeat witr because witr in Imam's view is wajib and he has already performed it in its time with due care, because the time of witr is the same as the time of Isha. At most, it can be said that order between Isha and witr was not observed. The answer is that due to the excuse of forgetfulness, order is dropped. Therefore, repetition of witr is not required. And he repeats the sunnah because the sunnah is subordinate to the fard. So when the fard is repeated, its subordinate must also be repeated. According to the Sahibayn, since witr is sunnah, and the sunnah is subordinate to the fard of Isha, therefore, along with Isha prayer, repetition of witr is also necessary. And Allah knows best. Jameel Ahmad Afa 'anhu.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the obligation of sequence (tartib) between witr and other prayers. The core issue is whether witr is wajib (Imam) or sunnah (Sahibayn). The first scenario: a person prays Fajr while remembering that he has not prayed witr. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, since witr is wajib, tartib is required between wajib acts, so Fajr is invalid due to omitted tartib. The Sahibayn, considering witr sunnah, see no tartib requirement between a sunnah and a fard, so Fajr remains valid. The second scenario: after praying Isha without wudu, one later performs wudu and prays sunnan and witr, then discovers the earlier Isha was invalid. According to Imam, one repeats Isha and its sunnan but not witr, because witr is an independent wajib already performed correctly; the missed tartib is excused due to forgetfulness. The Sahibayn require repeating witr as well, since they consider it sunnah subordinate to Isha. The commentary clarifies these rules, emphasizing the principle that tartib only applies among fard acts, not between fard and sunnah. The teacher should note that the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that witr is wajib, following Imam Abu Hanifa, as this is the relied-upon view in the madhhab.

Key Terms
ترتیب (tartib): The obligation to perform prayers in a specific order; here, between witr and fajr, or between Isha and its sunnahs.
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha. Its legal status is disputed within the Hanafi school: wajib (Abu Hanifa) vs sunnah muakkadah (Sahibayn).
صاحبين (sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi position, if a person prays Fajr while remembering that he has not prayed Witr, what is the ruling on Fajr?
A) It is valid because Witr is sunnah.
B) It is invalid because Witr is wajib and tartib is required.
C) It is valid because tartib is not required between any prayers.
D) It is invalid but no repetition is needed.

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib according to the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school; therefore, tartib between witr and Fajr is required, and Fajr prayed without performing witr is invalid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling of Sajdah Sahw: Method, Proof, and Differences
Ruling with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of sajdah sahw, explain its proof (dalil), and compare it with the Shafi'i position, including the preferred number of salams and the recitation in the sitting.

Core Idea
Sajdah sahw is wajib after salam to compensate for forgetfulness without repeating the prayer.

This passage from al-Hidayah covers the essential rulings of sajdah sahw: when it is required, its precise method, and why it is performed after the final salam. It also presents the Shafi'i dispute and resolves it through explicit hadith and rational reasoning. Additionally, it discusses secondary differences on the number of salams and where to recite blessings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling and method
The passage states that sajdah sahw is performed for any increase or decrease in the prayer. The method is: after the final salam, perform two sajdahs, then sit and recite tashahhud, then give salam again.
This sequence is wajib in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The primary proof is the saying of the Prophet (ﷺ): 'For every forgetfulness, there are two prostrations after the salam' (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah). A supporting narration of his action after salam is also cited.
The saying (qawl) is given precedence over conflicting action narrations.
3
Understand the Shafi'i counter-proof
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith of Abdullah ibn Malik in Bukhari where the Prophet prostrated before salam after forgetting the first tashahhud.
This is an action narration that seems to contradict the Hanafi action narration.
4
Analyze the Hanafi tarjih methodology
The two action narrations (before and after salam) contradict each other. In Hanafi usul, when actions conflict, the explicit saying (qawl) is preferred. Additionally, a rational argument is given: sajdah before salam could lead to repetition, which is impermissible by consensus.
Rational proof (istidlal 'aqli) strengthens the position.
5
Note secondary issues
The passage discusses whether to give one or two salams after the sajdah (author prefers two) and whether to recite blessings and supplication in the sitting before or after the sajdah (author prefers after).
These are intra-Hanafi differences of preference.
