باب سجود السهو
يسجد للسهو فى الزيادة والنقصان سجدتين بعد السلام، ثم يتشهد ثم يسلم. وعند الشافعي يسجد قبل السلام لماروى انه عليه السلام سجد للسهو قبل السلام. ولنا قوله عليه السلام: لكل سهو سجدتان بعد السلام. وروى انه عليه السلام سجد سجدتي السهو بعد السلام. فتعارضت روايتا فعله، فبقى التمسك بقوله سالما. ولان سجود السهو مما لايتكرر، فيؤخر عن السلام حتى لو سهى عن السلام ينجبر به. وهذا الخلاف في الاولوية. ويأتى بتسليمتين هو الصحيح صرفاً للسلام المذكور الى ما هو المعهود. ويأتى بالصلواة على النبي عليه السلام والدعاء في قعدة السهو، هو الصحيح لان الدعاء موضعه آخر الصلوة.
ترجمہ: زیادتی اور نقصان کی صورت میں سلام کے بعد سہو کے دو سجدے کرے۔ پھر تشہد پڑھے۔ پھر سلام پھیر دے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک سلام سے پہلے سجدہ کرے کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سلام سے پہلے سہو کا سجدہ کیا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ہر سہو کے لئے سلام کے بعد دو سجدے ہیں اور روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سلام کے بعد سہو کے دو سجدے کئے ہیں پس آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فعل کی دونوں روایتیں متعارض ہیں تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول سے استدلال کرنا بلا معارضہ باقی رہ گیا۔ اور اس لئے کہ سجدہ سہو ان چیزوں میں سے ہے جو مکرر نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا اسلام سے مؤخر کیا جائے گا تاکہ اگر سلام سے سہو کرے تو یہ بھی سجدہ سے پورا ہو جائے۔ اور یہ اختلاف اولویت میں ہے۔ اور دو سلام پھیرے یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ احادیث میں جو سلام مذکور ہے وہ معہود سلام کی طرف مراجع ہے۔ اور قعدہ میں حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم پر درود پڑھے اور اپنے لئے دعا مانگے یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ دعا کا مقام نماز کا آخر ہے۔
تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر نماز کے اندر کسی فعل کی زیادتی کر دی گئی یا کمی کر دی گئی تو اس پر دو سجدے سہو کے واجب ہوں گے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ سلام کے بعد واجب ہوں گے یا سلام سے پہلے تو جواز کے اندر کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ سب کا اتفاق ہے کہ سجدہ سہو سلام سے پہلے کرے یا سلام کے بعد کرے دونوں جائز ہیں البتہ روایات میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ احناف کے نزدیک سلام کے بعد اولی ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک سلام سے پہلے اولی ہے۔ اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ اگر مصلی کا سہو نقصان سے ہے تو سجدہ سہو سلام سے پہلے کرے اور اگر زیادتی ہوگئی تو سلام کے بعد سجدہ سہو کرے۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سجدہ سہو سلام سے پہلے کیا ہے جیسا کہ صحاح ستہ میں عبد اللہ بن مالک کی حدیث ہے۔ بخاری کے الفاظ یہ ہیں: ان النبي صلى الظهر فقام فى الركعتين الأوليين و لم يجلس فقام الناس معه حتى اذا قضى الصلاة وانتظر الناس تسليمه كبر وهو جالس فسجد سجدتين قبل ان يسلم۔ یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ظہر کی نماز پڑھی اور پہلے دو رکعتوں میں بغیر قعدہ کئے کھڑے ہو گئے آپ کے ساتھ لوگ بھی کھڑے ہو گئے حتی کہ جب نماز قریب ختم ہوگئی اور لوگ آپ کے سلام پھیرنے کا انتظار کرنے لگے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیٹھے بیٹھے تکبیر کہی اور سلام پھیرنے سے پہلے دو سجدے کئے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ سہو قبل السلام ہے۔
احناف کی دلیل آنحضور کا قول لكل سهو سجدتان بعد السلام ہے۔ (ابوداؤد، ابن ماجہ) دوسری دلیل حدیث فعلی ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سلام کے بعد دو سجدے کئے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ دو حدیث فعلی متعارض ہو گئیں ہیں پس ان دونوں کو چھوڑ کر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول پر عمل کریں گے اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول یہ ہے کہ سہو کے دو سجدے سلام کے بعد ہیں۔
احناف کی عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بالاجماع سجدہ سہو مکرر نہیں ہوتا۔ اور سلام سے پہلے سجدہ سہو کرنے کی صورت میں تکرار کا امکان ہے بایں طور کہ سلام سے پہلے سجدہ کر لیا پھر جب سلام پھیرنے کا وقت آیا تو اس کو شک ہو گیا کہ تین رکعتیں ہوئیں یا چار ہوئیں۔ اسی سوچ میں پڑا رہا یہاں تک کہ سلام میں تاخیر ہو گئی پھر یاد آیا کہ چار رکعتیں ہو گئیں ہیں تو اب تاخیر سلام کی وجہ سے اس پر دوبارہ سجدہ سہو واجب ہوا ہے۔ اب یہ شخص دوبارہ سجدہ سہو کرے گا یا نہیں۔ دو ہی صورتیں ہیں اگر اس نے دوبارہ سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تو نماز میں ایسا نقص باقی رہ گیا جس کی تلافی نہیں کی گئی ہے اور اگر دوبارہ سجدہ سہو کیا تو سجدہ سہو مکرر ہو جائے گا حالانکہ یہ بالاجماع غیر مشروع ہے۔ اس لئے مناسب یہ ہے کہ سجدہ سہو سلام کے بعد کیا جائے تاکہ تمام سہووں کی تلافی ممکن ہو۔
رہی یہ بات کہ سجدہ سہو سے پہلے دونوں طرف سلام پھیرے یا ایک طرف۔ اس بارے میں مصنف ہدایہ کے نزدیک راجح یہ ہے کہ دونوں طرف سلام پھیرے اس کے قائل شمس الائمہ السرخی اور صدر الاسلام اور فقیہ ابو اللیث ہیں۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ اور شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ، علامہ فخر الاسلام اور صاحب ایضاح کے نزدیک راجح یہ ہے کہ فقط دائیں طرف سلام پھیرے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ بیان کی ہے کہ احادیث میں جہاں لفظ سلام مذکور ہے اس سے متعارف اور معہود سلام مراد ہے اور متعارف دونوں طرف سلام پھیرنا ہے نہ کہ ایک طرف۔ اس لئے دونوں طرف سلام پھیرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ وغیرہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سلام کے دو حکم ہیں ایک تو قوم کے لئے تحیۃ اور دوم تحلیل اور یہ سلام جو سجدہ سہو کے لئے ہے اس میں تحیہ مراد نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ جو سلام تحیہ اور دعا کے لئے ہوتا ہے وہ قاطع احرام ہوتا ہے اور یہاں نماز کو قطع کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ تحلیل مراد ہے اور تحلیل میں تکرار نہیں ہوتا اس لئے تکرار سلام کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ ایک طرف کافی ہوگا۔
رہی یہ بات کہ درود علی النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اور دعاء ماثورہ قعدہ مصلوۃ میں پڑھے یا قعدہ سہو میں۔ قعدہ صلوۃ سے مراد سجدہ سہو سے پہلے کا قعدہ ہے اور قعدہ سہو سے مراد سجدہ سہو کے بعد کا قعدہ ہے۔ اس بارے میں امام طحاوی نے فرمایا کہ دونوں قعدوں میں پڑھے یعنی قعدہ صلوۃ میں بھی اور قعدہ سہو میں بھی۔ اور شیخین کے نزدیک قعدہ صلوۃ میں پڑھے یعنی سجدہ سہو سے پہلے۔ اور امام محمد کے نزدیک قعدہ سہو میں پڑھے یعنی سجدہ سہو کے بعد، مصنف ہدایہ نے اس کو صحیح کہا ہے۔ امام طحاوی نے اپنے مذہب کی تائید میں ایک ضابطہ بیان کیا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ قعدہ جس کے آخر میں سلام ہو اس میں درود علی النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم پڑھا جائے گا۔ پس اس ضابطہ کی روشنی میں دونوں قعدوں میں درود پڑھا جائے گا یعنی سجدہ سہو سے پہلے بھی اور اس کے بعد کیونکہ ان دونوں قعدوں یعنی قعدہ صلوۃ اور قعدہ سہو کے آخر میں سلام ہے۔
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. He performs two prostrations for forgetfulness due to increase and decrease after the salam, then he recites the tashahhud, then he makes the salam. According to al-Shafi'i, he prostrates before the salam because it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) prostrated for forgetfulness before the salam. Our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'For every forgetfulness, there are two prostrations after the salam.' And it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) performed the two prostrations of forgetfulness after the salam. So the two narrations of his action are contradictory, so clinging to his saying remains without opposition. And because the prostration of forgetfulness is something that is not repeated, so it is delayed after the salam so that if he forgets the salam, it is compensated by it. This difference is a matter of preference. And he performs two salams; this is the correct view, turning the mentioned salam to what is customary. And he sends blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and makes supplication in the sitting of forgetfulness; this is the correct view because the place of supplication is the end of the prayer. Translation: In case of increase and decrease, perform two prostrations for forgetfulness after the salam. Then recite tashahhud. Then turn the salam. According to Imam Shafi'i, he prostrates before the salam because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed the prostration for forgetfulness before the salam. Our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'For every forgetfulness, there are two prostrations after the salam.' And it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed the two prostrations of forgetfulness after the salam. So the two narrations of his action are contradictory, so inferring from his saying is left without opposition. And because the prostration of forgetfulness is among those things that are not repeated. Therefore, it is delayed after the salam so that if he forgets the salam, this is also completed by the prostration. This difference is in preference. And he should turn two salams; this is correct because the salam mentioned in the hadiths refers to the customary salam. And in the sitting, he should send blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and ask for supplication for himself; this is correct because the place of supplication is the end of the prayer. Elaboration: The issue is that if within the prayer an act is increased or decreased, then two prostrations for forgetfulness become obligatory. As for whether they are obligatory after the salam or before the salam, there is no difference in permissibility. All agree that performing the prostration of forgetfulness before the salam or after the salam is permissible; however, there is difference in narrations. Thus, according to the Hanafis, after the salam is preferable, and according to Imam Shafi'i, before the salam is preferable. Imam Malik said: If the forgetfulness of the worshipper is from deficiency, then he should perform the prostration of forgetfulness before the salam; if there was an increase, then after the salam. Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed the prostration of forgetfulness before the salam as in the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Malik in the Sahih Sitta. The wording of Bukhari is: 'Indeed the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Zuhr, and he stood up in the first two rak'ahs and did not sit, so the people stood with him until when he finished the prayer and the people waited for his salam, he said the takbir while sitting and performed two prostrations before the salam.' Meaning the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Zuhr and without sitting in the first two rak'ahs, he stood up; people also stood with him until when the prayer was nearly finished and people began waiting for his salam, he (peace be upon him) said takbir while sitting and performed two prostrations before turning the salam. From this hadith it is understood that prostration for forgetfulness is before the salam. The Hanafi proof is the saying of the Prophet: 'For every forgetfulness, there are two prostrations after the salam' (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah). The second proof is a hadith of action that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed two prostrations after the salam. The author of Hidayah says: The two hadiths of action contradict each other; so leaving both, we act upon the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him), and his saying is: 'Two prostrations for forgetfulness are after the salam.' The rational proof of the Hanafis is that, by consensus, the prostration of forgetfulness is not repeated. And if one prostrates before the salam, there is possibility of repetition in that he prostrates before the salam, then when the time comes to turn the salam, he becomes doubtful whether three rak'ahs were performed or four; he remains in this thought until there is delay in salam, then he remembers that four rak'ahs were done. Now due to the delay of salam, another prostration for forgetfulness becomes obligatory upon him. Now this person will repeat the prostration for forgetfulness or not? Two possibilities: if he does not repeat, then a deficiency remains in the prayer that is not compensated; if he repeats, then the prostration becomes repeated, while by consensus it is not legislated. So it is appropriate that the prostration for forgetfulness be performed after the salam so that compensation for all forgetfulness is possible. As for whether he should turn the salam to both sides before the prostration of forgetfulness or to one side, in this regard, according to the author of Hidayah, the preponderant view is that he should turn the salam to both sides; those who hold this are Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi, Sadr al-Islam, and Faqih Abu al-Layth. Some said that according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, the ruling is also this. And according to Shaykh al-Islam Khwahrizadah, 'Allama Fakhr al-Islam, and the author of Idah, the preponderant view is that he should turn the salam only to the right side. The author of Hidayah has stated the proof of the correct view: that wherever the word 'salam' is mentioned in the hadiths, the customary and familiar salam is intended, and the customary is to turn the salam to both sides, not to one side. Therefore, turning the salam to both sides is necessary. The proof of Shaykh al-Islam Khwahrizadah etc. is that the salam has two rulings: one is a greeting for the congregation, and the second is tahlil (making lawful what was forbidden during prayer). And this salam which is for the prostration of forgetfulness, greeting cannot be intended because the salam that is for greeting and supplication is a breaker of the state of ihram (i.e., it ends the prayer), and here cutting the prayer is not intended. So it is understood that tahlil is intended, and tahlil is not repeated; therefore, repetition of salam is not very necessary; rather, one side is sufficient. As for whether he should recite blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the prescribed supplication in the sitting of the prayer or in the sitting of forgetfulness. By 'sitting of the prayer' is meant the sitting before the prostration of forgetfulness, and by 'sitting of forgetfulness' is meant the sitting after the prostration. Regarding this, Imam Tahawi said: he should recite in both sittings, i.e., in the sitting of the prayer and in the sitting of forgetfulness. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he should recite in the sitting of the prayer, i.e., before the prostration of forgetfulness. According to Imam Muhammad, he should recite in the sitting of forgetfulness, i.e., after the prostration. The author of Hidayah has declared this correct. Imam Tahawi has stated a principle in support of his view: that every sitting at the end of which there is salam, blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) should be recited. So in light of this principle, blessings should be recited in both sittings, i.e., before the prostration of forgetfulness and after it, because at the end of both these sittings (the sitting of prayer and the sitting of forgetfulness) there is salam.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Sujūd al-Sahw (Prostration of Forgetfulness). It begins by stating the ruling: sajdah sahw is performed for any increase or decrease in the prayer. The method is to perform two prostrations after the salam (final salutation), then recite tashahhud, then give salam again. The author then presents the Shafi'i position that it should be before the salam, citing the hadith of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) prostrating before salam. The Hanafi proof is twofold: first, the explicit saying of the Prophet 'for every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam' (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah); second, a narration that he prostrated after salam. The author resolves the apparent conflict between the two conflicting action narrations by adhering to the explicit saying, which is unequivocal. A rational argument is also given: sajdah sahw cannot be repeated. If done before salam, a situation may arise where a second sajdah becomes necessary due to delay in salam, creating a paradox: either the deficiency remains uncompensated or the sajdah is repeated (which is impermissible by consensus). Doing it after salam avoids this. The passage then discusses a secondary issue: whether to give two salams (right and left) or one after the sajdah. The author of Hidayah declares two salams correct, because the word 'salam' in the hadiths refers to the customary salam, which is to both sides. Opponents argue that here the salam is for tahlil (ending the prayer), not greeting, so one side suffices. Finally, the passage discusses where to recite blessings and supplication: the author prefers the sitting after the sajdah (qādat al-sahw), contrary to Imam Tahawi who requires it in both sittings, and the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who prefer before. The author's tarjih is based on the principle that the place for supplication is the end of the prayer.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness (increase or decrease) in the prayer.
السلام (al-salām): The final salutation of the prayer, turning the head to the right and left saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'.
قعدة السهو (qadat al-sahw): The sitting after the two prostrations of forgetfulness, before the final salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is the correct sequence for sajdah sahw?
A) Salam, sajdah, tashahhud, salam.
B) Sajdah, salam, tashahhud, salam.
C) Sajdah, tashahhud, salam.
D) Salam, sajdah, salam, tashahhud.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah sahw is a wajib compensation for forgetfulness in prayer, performed after the salam, and its timing is based on explicit hadith and sound reasoning.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Hadith Proof for Sujud al-Sahw After Salam
Hanafi proof that sujud al-sahw is after salam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proof that sujud al-sahw is performed after salam and explain how the school reconciles contradictory action hadith by preferring the explicit saying.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw after salam is proven by the Prophet's explicit saying, which takes precedence over conflicting actions.

This passage addresses a central dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the timing of sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The Hanafi school relies on the Prophet's explicit statement that it is after the salam, while the Shafi'is cite a hadith where the Prophet performed it before salam. The author of al-Hidayah resolves the conflict by prioritizing the saying over action, and adds a rational argument against repetition. Understanding this proof strengthens your ability to weigh conflicting evidences in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
State the Hanafi ruling: sujud al-sahw is wajib and performed after the salam. Note that the proof is a combination of textual and rational evidence.
The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Examine the Hanafi textual proof
The primary proof is the prophetic saying: 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam.' (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah). This is a clear command indicating timing.
The dalil is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Analyze the conflict resolution
Two action hadith appear contradictory (one before salam, one after). Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah leaves both actions aside and acts on the explicit saying, because saying takes precedence over action in Hanafi usul.
This is a key usul principle: al-qawl muqaddam 'ala al-fi'l.
4
Evaluate the rational argument
Performing sujud before salam could lead to a situation where doubt about rak'ahs causes delay, necessitating a second sujud, which is impermissible by consensus. Doing it after salam avoids repetition.
This rational proof (dalil 'aqli) supports the textual evidence.
5
Note the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis say salam first, then sujud. Shafi'is perform sujud before salam. The practical difference affects the sequence to be followed by the muqtadi and the imam.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو
e.g., حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ظہر کی نماز پڑھی اور پہلے دور کعتوں میں بغیر قعدہ کئے کھڑے ہو گئے آپ کے ساتھ لوگ بھی کھڑے ہو گئے حتی کہ جب نماز قریب ختم ہوگئی اور لوگ آپ کے سلام پھیرنے کا انتظار کرنے لگے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بیٹھے بیٹھے تکبیر کہی اور سلام پھیرنے سے پہلے دو سجدے کئے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ سہو قبل السلام ہے۔
احناف کی دلیل آنحضور کا قول لكل سهو سجدتان بعد السلام ہے۔ (ابوداؤد، ابن ماجہ ) دوسری دلیل حدیث فعلی ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے سلام کے بعد دو سجدے کئے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ دو حدیث فعلی متعارض ہو گئیں ہیں پس ان دونوں کو چھوڑ کر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے قول پر عمل کریں گے اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول یہ ہے کہ کہو کے دو سجدے سلام کے بعد ہیں۔ احناف کی عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بالا جماع سجدہ سہو کر نہیں ہوتا ۔ اور سلام سے پہلے سجدہ سہو کرنے کی صورت میں تکرار کا امکان ہے بایں طور کہ سلام سے پہلے سجدہ کر لیا پھر جب سلام پھیر نے کا وقت آیا تو اس کو شک ہو گیا کہ تین رکعتیں ہوئی ہیں یا چار ہوئیں۔ اسی سوچ میں پڑا رہا یہاں تک کہ سلام میں تاخیر ہو گئی پھر یاد آیا کہ چار رکعتیں ہو گئیں ہیں تو اب تاخیر سلام کی وجہ سے اس پر دوبارہ سجدہ سہو واجب ہوا ہے اب یہ شخص دوبارہ سجدہ سہو کرے گا یا نہیں ۔ دو ہی صورتیں ہیں اگر اس نے دوبارہ سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تو نماز میں ایسا نقص باقی رہ گیا جس کی تلافی نہیں کی گئی ہے اور اگر دوبارہ سجدہ سہو کیا تو سجدہ سہو مکرر ہو جائے گا حالانکہ یہ بالا جماع غیر مشروع ہے۔ اس لئے مناسب یہ ہے کہ سجدہ سہو سلام کے بعد کیا جائے تا کہ تمام سہووں کی تلافی ممکن ہو۔
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. For example, the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed the Zuhr prayer and stood up from the first two rak'ahs without sitting; the people with him also stood up until when the prayer was nearly complete and the people waited for him to say the salam, he said takbir while sitting and performed two prostrations before saying the salam. This hadith indicates that sujud al-sahw is before the salam. The proof of the Hanafis is the saying of the Prophet: 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after the salam.' (Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah). The second proof is a hadith of action that the Prophet performed two prostrations after the salam. The author of al-Hidayah says that two action-based hadith have become contradictory, so we leave both and act upon the Prophet's saying, and his saying is that the two prostrations are after the salam. The rational proof of the Hanafis is that repetition of sujud al-sahw does not occur by consensus. And if sujud al-sahw is performed before the salam, there is a possibility of repetition, as follows: if he performed the prostration before the salam, then when the time came to say the salam, he doubted whether he had prayed three or four rak'ahs, and remained in that thought until the salam was delayed. Then he remembered that he had prayed four rak'ahs, so due to the delay of the salam, another sujud al-sahw became obligatory. Now does this person perform sujud al-sahw again or not? There are two possibilities: if he does not perform sujud al-sahw again, then there remains a deficiency in the prayer that has not been compensated. And if he does perform sujud al-sahw again, then sujud al-sahw becomes repeated, whereas this is not legislated by consensus. Therefore, it is appropriate that sujud al-sahw be performed after the salam, so that it is possible to compensate for all forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the timing of sujud al-sahw. The author begins by narrating a hadith where the Prophet performed sujud al-sahw before salam, which is used by the Shafi'i school. The Hanafis counter with the Prophet's explicit statement that sujud al-sahw is after salam. The author of al-Hidayah resolves the conflict between two contradictory action hadith by preferring the explicit saying (qawl) over action (fi'l). He then provides a rational argument (dalil 'aqli) that performing sujud al-sahw before salam could lead to the need for repetition, which is not permitted by consensus. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that sujud al-sahw is performed after salam.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for deficiencies or additions in the prayer due to forgetfulness.
حدیث فعلی (hadith fi'li): A hadith that reports an action of the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should sujud al-sahw be performed?
A) Before the salam
B) After the salam
C) Either before or after, equally valid
D) Only if the imam forgets

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is wajib after salam, proven by the Prophet's explicit saying and the rational need to avoid repetition.

Number of Salams Before Sujud al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on number of salams before sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the number of salams before sujud al-sahw and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The salam before sujud al-sahw: tahlil or tahiyyah? The answer determines whether one side or both are needed.

Sujud al-sahw is a special prostration to rectify errors in prayer, but it has its own procedures. One point of difference among Hanafi scholars is whether the salam that precedes sujud al-sahw should be to both sides or just the right. This lesson examines the two views and their proofs, as discussed in al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What exactly is being disputed? The number of salams said before performing sujud al-sahw.
2
Identify the two Hanafi positions
One group (al-Marghinani, al-Sarkhasi) says salam to both sides; another (Khwahar-zada, Fakhr al-Islam) says only to the right.
3
Analyze the proof for both sides
Al-Hidayah argues that the word 'salam' in hadith refers to the customary salam, which is to both sides.
4
Analyze the proof for one side
The opposing view distinguishes between tahlil (exiting prayer) and tahiyyah (greeting). Since the salam before sujud is for tahlil, repetition is unnecessary.
Tahlil does not require repetition; one salam suffices.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The author of al-Hidayah prefers both sides, and this view is relied upon in later Hanafi works.
Both views are valid, but the safer practice is to follow the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہی یہ بات کہ سجدہ سہو سے پہلے دونوں طرف سلام پھیرے یا ایک طرف۔ اس بارے میں مصنف ہدایہ کے نزدیک راجح یہ ہے کہ دونوں طرف سلام پھیرے اس کے قائل شمس الائمہ السرخی اور صدر الاسلام اور فقیہ ابو اللیث ہیں۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ اور شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ، علامہ فخر الاسلام اور صاحب ایضاح کے نزدیک راجح یہ ہے کہ فقط دائیں طرف سلام پھیرے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے قول صحیح کی دلیل یہ بیان کی ہے کہ احادیث میں جہاں لفظ سلام مذکور ہے اس سے متعارف اور معہود سلام مراد ہے اور متعارف دونوں طرف سلام پھیرنا ہے نہ کہ ایک طرف۔ اس لئے دونوں طرف سلام پھیرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ شیخ الاسلام خواہر زادہ وغیرہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سلام کے دو حکم ہیں ایک تو قوم کے لئے تحیۃ اور دوم تحلیل اور یہ سلام جو سجدہ سہو کے لئے ہے اس یں تیہ مراد نہیں ہوسکتا کیونکہ جو سلام تحیہ اور دعا کے لئے ہوتا ہے وہ قاطع احرام ہوتا ہے اور یہاں نماز کو قطع کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ تحلیل مراد ہے اور تحلیل میں تکرار نہیں ہوتا اس لئے تکرار سلام کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ ایک طرف کافی ہوگا۔
Remains the matter whether one should say salam to both sides or one side before sujud al-sahw. Regarding this, the author of al-Hidayah considers the preponderant view to be that one says salam to both sides; Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi, Sadr al-Islam, and Faqih Abu al-Layth are of this view. Some have said that Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf also held this ruling. And Sheikh al-Islam Khwahar-zada, Allama Fakhr al-Islam, and the author of al-Idah consider the preponderant view to be that only the right side is addressed. The author of al-Hidayah gives the proof for the correct saying that wherever the word 'salam' appears in the hadith, it refers to the customary and accustomed salam, and the customary is to say salam to both sides, not one side. Therefore, it will be necessary to say salam to both sides. The proof of Sheikh al-Islam Khwahar-zada et al. is that the salam has two rulings: one is a greeting (tahiyyah) for the people, and the second is tahlil (exiting the prayer). And this salam which is for sujud al-sahw cannot intend greeting because the salam that is for greeting and supplication cuts the ihram (sanctity of prayer), and here cutting the prayer is not intended. Therefore, it is understood that tahlil is intended, and there is no repetition in tahlil, so repetition of salam is not necessary. Rather, one side is sufficient.
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about how many salams to say before sujud al-sahw. The author of al-Hidayah (Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani) holds that one must say salam to both sides, based on the customary meaning of salam in hadith. This is also the view of Shams al-A'imma al-Sarkhasi and others. However, another group of Hanafi scholars, including Khwahar-zada, hold that only the right side suffices, arguing that the salam before sujud is for tahlil (exiting the prayer), not greeting, and tahlil does not require repetition. The author of al-Hidayah prefers the first view.

Key Terms
تحلیل (tahlil): The act of exiting the prayer; the salam that ends the prayer.
تحیۃ (tahiyyah): Greeting; the salam as a greeting to the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Hidayah, how many sides should one say salam to before sujud al-sahw?
A) Only the right side
B) Only the left side
C) Both sides
D) No salam needed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two positions on the number of salams before sujud al-sahw; the relied-upon view is to say salam to both sides.

Timing of Darud Recitation During Sujud al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of darud recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi positions on the timing of darud during sujud al-sahw and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The final salam determines where darud is recited — but which salam is final?

When sujud al-sahw is performed, the prayer extends to include two sitings: one before the prostrations (qa'dah al-salah) and one after (qa'dah al-sahw). The question arises: in which of these sitings should the darud and supplication be recited? The Hanafi school has three distinct views, each based on a different understanding of which sitting is the 'final' one of the prayer. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and identifies the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State the views of Imam al-Tahawi (recite in both sitings), the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: recite before sujud only), and Imam Muhammad (recite after sujud only).
2
Understand the reasoning of Imam al-Tahawi
Imam al-Tahawi applies a principle: every sitting that ends with salam should include darud. Since both sitings end with salam, darud is recited in both.
This principle is a general legal maxim (qa'ida) but is not accepted as decisive here.
3
Analyze the proof of the Shaykhayn
The Shaykhayn hold that the first salam (before sujud) exits the prayer, making the qa'dah before sujud the final sitting. Hence darud is recited there.
They consider the salam for sujud as a complete exit from the prayer.
4
Analyze the proof of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad argues that the first salam does not exit the prayer; only the second salam (after sujud) does. Therefore, the qa'dah after sujud is the final sitting, where darud should be recited.
His view is considered the most sound by the author of al-Hidayah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and thamarah
The author of al-Hidayah adopts Imam Muhammad's view as correct. Thus, the operative ruling (mufta bihi) is to recite darud after sujud al-sahw, in the qa'dah al-sahw.
Practical consequence: a person who recites darud before sujud should repeat it after sujud to fulfill the wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رہی یہ بات کہ درود علی النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم اور دعاء ماثورہ قعدہ مصلوۃ میں پڑھے یا قعدہ کہو میں ۔ قعدہ مصلوۃ سے مراد سجدہ سہو سے پہلے کا قعدہ ہے اور قعدہ کہو سے مراد سجدہ سے بعد کا قعدہ ہے اس بارے میں امام طحاوی نے فرمایا کہ دونوں قعدوں میں پڑھے یعنی قعدہ صلوۃ میں بھی اور قعدہ سہو میں بھی اور شیخین کے نزدیک قعد صلوٰۃ میں پڑھے یعنی سجدہ سہو سے پہلے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک قعدہ کہو میں پڑھے یعنی سجدہ کہو کے بعد ، مصنف ہدایہ نے اس کو صحیح کہا ہے۔ امام طحاوی نے اپنے مذہب کی تائید میں ایک ضابطہ بیان کیا ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ قعدہ جس کے آخر میں سلام ہو اس میں درود علی النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم پڑھا جائے گا۔ پس اس ضابطہ کی روشنی میں دونوں قعدوں میں درود پڑھا جائے گا یعنی جود کہو سے پہلے بھی اور اس کے بعد کیونکہ ان دونوں قعدوں یعنی قعدہ صلوٰۃ اور قعدہ سہو کے آخر میں سلام ہے۔
شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ درود اور دعاختم صلوۃ کے قعدے میں پڑھے جاتے ہیں اور جس شخص پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہو اس کا وہ سلام جو جدہ سہو کے لئے ہے وہ نماز سے نکال دیتا ہے۔ پس جب یہ سلام نماز سے نکال دیتا ہے تو قعد صلوۃ ہی قعدہ ختم ہوا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک چونکہ ہی سلام نماز سے خارج نہیں کرتا بلکہ مجود سہو کے بعد جو سلام ہے وہ نماز سے نکال دیتا ہے اس لئے قعدہ سبو قعدہ ختم ہوگا نہ کہ قعدہ مصلوۃ اور درود اور دعا کا مقام چونکہ نماز کا آخر ہے اس لئے قعدہ سہو میں درود اور دعا پڑھے گا نہ کہ قعدہ صلوۃ میں ۔ امام محمد کا قول ہی مفتی بہ ہے۔
Remains the matter whether one should recite the darud (salutations) upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the supplication (du'a') in the qa'dah of prayer (salah) or in the qa'dah of forgetfulness (sahw). Qa'dah of prayer means the sitting before sujud al-sahw, and qa'dah of forgetfulness means the sitting after the prostration. Regarding this, Imam al-Tahawi said that one should recite in both sitings, i.e., in the qa'dah of prayer and the qa'dah of forgetfulness. According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), one recites in the qa'dah of prayer, i.e., before sujud al-sahw. And according to Imam Muhammad, one recites in the qa'dah of forgetfulness, i.e., after sujud al-sahw. The author of al-Hidayah declared this (Imam Muhammad's view) to be correct. Imam al-Tahawi mentioned a principle in support of his view: every sitting that ends with salam should have the darud recited in it. According to this principle, darud should be recited in both sitings because both sitings end with salam. The proof of the two shaykhs (Shaykhayn) is that darud and supplication are recited in the final sitting of the prayer, and the salam that is for sujud al-sahw takes one out of the prayer. So when this salam takes one out, the qa'dah of prayer is the final sitting. According to Imam Muhammad, since this salam does not take one out of the prayer, but the salam after sujud al-sahw takes one out, the qa'dah of forgetfulness is the final sitting. And since the place for darud and supplication is the end of prayer, he will recite them in the qa'dah of forgetfulness, not in the qa'dah of prayer. Imam Muhammad's statement is the one given for fatwa (mufta bihi).
Source pages p. 230

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when to recite the darud and supplication when sujud al-sahw is performed. There are three views: (1) Imam al-Tahawi: recite in both sitings (before and after sujud). (2) Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): recite only before sujud (qa'dah of prayer). (3) Imam Muhammad: recite only after sujud (qa'dah of forgetfulness). The author of al-Hidayah considers Imam Muhammad's view correct and mufta bihi. The reasoning revolves around which siting is considered the final one of the prayer. The two shaykhs say the salam before sujud takes one out, so the qa'dah before sujud is final. Imam Muhammad argues that the actual exit from prayer occurs only after sujud, so the qa'dah after sujud is final, hence darud should be recited there.

Key Terms
قعدہ صلوۃ (qa'dah al-salah): The sitting before sujud al-sahw, i.e., the final tashahhud sitting of the original prayer.
قعدہ سہو (qa'dah al-sahw): The sitting after sujud al-sahw, before the final salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only before sujud al-sahw
B) Only after sujud al-sahw
C) Both before and after
D) Darud is not recited in such cases

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to recite darud and supplication in the sitting after sujud al-sahw, as held by Imam Muhammad.

General Principle for Sujud al-Sahw Due to Addition
Ruling statement with rational proof via analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for when sujud al-sahw becomes wajib and identify the condition of forgetfulness.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib for a forgetful addition of the genus of salah that is not part of it.

This passage from al-Hidayah establishes a key principle: sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory when a person forgetfully adds an action that resembles the acts of prayer (like an extra bow or prostration) but is not a prescribed component. The text also defends the wajib status of sujud al-sahw by comparing it to the compulsory blood offerings in Hajj. Understanding this principle will help you distinguish between mistakes that require compensation and those that invalidate the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the general rule
Commit to memory the statement: 'Sujud al-sahw becomes necessary from every addition that is of the genus of salah but is not a part of it.' This is the core axiom.
The rule applies only to forgetful additions.
2
Identify the key condition
Note that the addition must be done forgetfully (sahw). Intentional additions invalidate the prayer. The condition of forgetfulness is implied throughout.
Forgetfulness is a required condition for sujud al-sahw.
3
Recognize the analogy to Hajj
The text uses qiyas: just as dam (blood offering) compensates for deficiencies in Hajj, sujud al-sahw compensates for deficiencies in salah. This supports the ruling that sujud al-sahw is wajib.
This analogy strengthens the proof for wujub.

Source Text

قال ويلزمه السهو اذا زاد فى صلوته فعلا من جنسها ليس منها، وهذا يدل على ان سجدة السهو واجبة هو الصحيح لانها تجب لجبر نقصان تمكن فى العبادة، فتكون واجبة كالدماء في الحج، واذا كان واجبا لا يجب الا بترك واجب او تاخیره او تاخیر رکن ساهيا، هذا هو الأصل، وانما وجبت بالزيادة لانها لا تعرى عن تاخیر رکن او ترک واجب
ترجمہ اور سہولا زم ہوگا جبکہ اپنی نماز میں ایس فعل زیادہ کیا جونماز کی جنس تو ہے (لیکن) نماز کا جز نہیں ہے اور یہ اس بات پر دال ہے کہ سجدہ سہو واجب ہے یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ سجدہ سہو اس نقصان کو پورا کرنے کے لئے واجب ہے، جو نقصان عبادت میں متمکن ہو گیا ہو یہ واجب ہوگا، جیسا کہ حج کے اندر قربانیاں ہیں اور جب یہ سجدہ واجب ٹھہر اتو واجب نہ ہوگا مگر سہو اترک واجب سے ، تاخیر سے یا کسی رکن کی تاخیر سے ضابطہ یہی ہے اور سجدہ سہو زیادتی سے اس لئے واجب ہوا کہ وہ کسی رکن کی تاخیر یا ترک واجب سے خالی نہیں ہوتا۔ تشریح اول باب میں بیان کیا تھا کہ سجدہ سہو زیادتی اور نقصان کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے مگر یہ ذکر نہیں کیا گیا کہ کون کی زیادتی اور نقصان موجب سہو ہے پس یہاں سے اس کی تفصیل اور تغییر مذکور ہے۔ چنانچہ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ سجدہ سہو ہر اس فعل کو زیادہ کرنے سے لازم ہوگا جو فل نماز کی جنس سے تو ہے مگر نماز کا جز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً ایک رکعت کے دور کوع کر لئے یا تین سجدے کر لئے تو ایک رکوع اور ایک سجدہ جو زائد ہے وہ اگر چہ نماز کی جنس سے ہے مگر نماز کا جز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا ایک رکوع کے بجائے دور کوع کئے دو سجدوں کی جگہ تین سجدے کئے تو اس زیادتی کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہو جائے گا۔
Sujud al-sahw becomes necessary from every addition that is of the genus of salah but is not a part of salah. He said: 'Sujud al-sahw becomes necessary when one adds an action in his prayer that is of its genus but not from it.' This indicates that sujud al-sahw is wajib, and this is correct because it becomes obligatory to compensate for a deficiency that has taken place in the worship, so it is wajib like the blood offerings (dam) in Hajj. And when it is wajib, it is not obligatory except by leaving a wajib, delaying it, or delaying a rukn forgetfully. This is the principle. And it became obligatory due to addition because it does not lack delaying a rukn or leaving a wajib. Translation: Sujud al-sahw becomes necessary when one adds an act in his prayer that is of the genus of prayer but not a part of it. This indicates that sujud al-sahw is wajib, and this is correct because sujud al-sahw is wajib to compensate for a deficiency that has settled in the worship. So it will be wajib, like the blood offerings in Hajj. And when it is wajib, it is not obligatory except by leaving a wajib, delaying it, or delaying a rukn forgetfully. This is the principle. And sujud al-sahw became obligatory due to addition because it is not free from delaying a rukn or leaving a wajib.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that establishes the general principle for when sujud al-sahw becomes compulsory. The author quotes al-Quduri: sujud al-sahw is required when one adds an act that is of the same genus as salah (e.g., bowing, prostrating) but is not a prescribed part of the prayer. For example, if someone performs two bows in one rak'ah or three prostrations, the extra act necessitates sujud al-sahw. The passage also argues for the wujub (obligatory nature) of sujud al-sahw, comparing it to the dam (blood offering) in Hajj. It clarifies that sujud al-sahw is only required for forgetfulness, not intentional actions, and it compensates for either a delay in a rukn or an omission of a wajib.

Key Terms
جنس صلوۃ (jins al-salah): Actions that are of the same type as the acts of prayer (e.g., ruku, sujud, qiyam) but not prescribed parts.
دماء (dima'): Blood offerings (sacrifices) required in Hajj for violations.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what condition makes sujud al-sahw obligatory due to addition?
A) Adding any extra action intentionally
B) Adding an action that is of the genus of salah but not part of it, forgetfully
C) Adding any extra rakah
D) Adding a word in prayer

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is wajib for any forgetful addition of an act that is from the genus of salah but not a prescribed part of the prayer.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Reciting Darud and Dua in the Qa'dah for Sujud al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of darud in sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad regarding the recitation of darud and dua in sujud al-sahw and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Where darud is recited depends on which salutation truly exits the prayer.

When sujud al-sahw becomes wajib, a question arises: should the worshipper recite the tashahhud, darud, and dua before the first salutation (which initiates sujud al-sahw) or after completing the prostrations and before the final salutation? This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Imam Muhammad on this point, and identifies the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed act and context
Recognize that the dispute is about the timing of reciting darud and dua when sujud al-sahw is wajib. Both parties agree that darud/dua are recited in the final qa'dah, but they differ on which qa'dah is final.
2
State the Shaykhayn's position and reasoning
The Shaykhayn hold that the first salutation (before sujud al-sahw) exits the prayer, making that qa'dah the final one. Therefore, darud/dua are recited before sujud al-sahw.
Opposing position: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position and reasoning
Imam Muhammad argues that the first salutation does not truly exit the prayer; only the final salutation after sujud al-sahw does. Hence the qa'dah after sujud al-sahw is the final qa'dah, where darud/dua are recited.
This is the mufta bihi view.
4
Determine the practical implication
The thamarah al-khilaf: According to Shaykhayn, darud is recited before sujud; according to Imam Muhammad, after sujud. The fatwa follows Imam Muhammad's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ درود اور دعا ختم صلوۃ کے قعدے میں پڑھے جاتے ہیں اور جس شخص پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہو اس کا وہ سلام جو سجدہ سہو کے لئے ہے وہ نماز سے نکال دیتا ہے۔ پس جب یہ سلام نماز سے نکال دیتا ہے تو قعدہ صلوۃ ہی قعدہ ختم ہوا اور امام محمد کے نزدیک چونکہ یہ سلام نماز سے خارج نہیں کرتا بلکہ سجود سہو کے بعد جو سلام ہے وہ نماز سے نکال دیتا ہے اس لئے قعدہ سہو قعدہ ختم ہوگا نہ کہ قعدہ صلوۃ اور درود اور دعا کا مقام چونکہ نماز کا آخر ہے اس لئے قعدہ سہو میں درود اور دعا پڑھے گا نہ کہ قعدہ صلوۃ میں ۔ امام محمد کا قول ہی مفتی بہ ہے۔
The proof of the two Shaykhs is that darud and dua are recited in the final qa'dah of the prayer, and the person upon whom sujud al-sahw is obligatory — the salutation that is for sujud al-sahw takes him out of the prayer. So when this salutation takes him out of the prayer, the qa'dah of the prayer ends. And according to Imam Muhammad, since this salutation does not exit from the prayer, but rather the salutation after sujud al-sahw exits from the prayer, therefore the qa'dah of sujud al-sahw becomes the final qa'dah, not the qa'dah of the prayer. And since the place of darud and dua is the last part of the prayer, he will recite darud and dua in the qa'dah of sujud al-sahw, not in the qa'dah of the prayer. Imam Muhammad's saying is the mufta bihi.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the correct place to recite darud and dua when sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory. The Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) argue that the first salutation, which initiates sujud al-sahw, exits the prayer. Therefore, the qa'dah before this salutation is the final qa'dah of the prayer, and darud and dua should be recited there before the salutation. Imam Muhammad holds that this initial salutation does not actually exit the prayer; rather, the prayer continues, and the final exit is only after sujud al-sahw and the second salutation. Thus, the qa'dah after sujud al-sahw is the true final qa'dah, and darud and dua should be recited there. The text states that Imam Muhammad's view is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position for fatwa).

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for errors or forgetfulness in prayer, either for an addition or omission.
مفتی بہ (mufta bihi): The relied-upon position in the school for giving fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view, where does the worshipper recite darud and dua when sujud al-sahw is wajib?
A) Before sujud al-sahw in the last qa'dah of the prayer
B) After sujud al-sahw in the qa'dah of sujud
C) Not at all
D) Before the first salutation

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school is to recite darud and dua in the qa'dah after sujud al-sahw, because that is the true final qa'dah of the prayer.

Sujud al-Sahw Due to Addition of a Same-Genus Act
Matn and sharh establishing wujub of sujud al-sahw for same-genus addition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why sujud al-sahw is wajib for adding a same-genus act to prayer, using the Hanafi qiyas on dam in Hajj.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw is wajib because it compensates the deficiency in worship, just as dam compensates in Hajj.

In this lesson, we study the ruling that sujud al-sahw is wajib when one adds an action of the same genus as prayer (like an extra ruku' or sajda) but not a part of it. The passage from Al-Hidayah states the ruling and provides a proof by analogy (qiyas) to the necessity of blood sacrifices (dam) in Hajj. We will also address an intra-Hanafi disagreement and the underlying principle that sujud al-sahw is only triggered by neglect or delay of a wajib or rukn, and how an increase implicitly causes such neglect or delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The matn states that sujud al-sahw is necessary when one adds an act that is of the same genus as prayer but not a part of it. Identify the act (sujud al-sahw) and the condition (forgetfulness and the type of increase).
2
Examine the proof for wujub
The commentator argues that the matn indicates wujub because sujud al-sahw is meant to repair a deficiency in worship, analogous to dam in Hajj. If not compensated, repetition of the prayer becomes wajib, which shows the importance of sujud.
The dalil is qiyas (analogy) on the necessity of dam in Hajj and the necessity of i'adah.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The principle is that sujud al-sahw is only obligated due to forgetful neglect or delay of a wajib or a rukn. This seems to exclude increases, but the commentator clarifies that any increase necessarily involves either delaying a rukn or omitting a wajib.
Example: performing three sajdas delays the standing (rukn); adding an extra rak'ah results in omitting the wajib salutation.
4
Address the objection
An objection is raised: if sujud is only for neglect/delay, why is it required for an increase? The answer: the increase is never free from delaying a rukn or leaving a wajib. Trace how each example (extra ruku', extra sajda, extra rak'ah) fits.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis like Imam al-Karkhi considered sujud al-sahw sunnah, but the majority and the text hold it as wajib. Understand the proof and the mufta bihi.
The text says 'هو الصحيح' (this is the correct view).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

سہو زیادتی سے اس لئے واجب ہوا کہ وہ کسی رکن کی تاخیر یا ترک واجب سے خالی نہیں ہوتا۔ تشریح اول باب میں بیان کیا تھا کہ سجدہ سہو زیادتی اور نقصان کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے مگر یہ ذکر نہیں کیا گیا کہ کون سی فرض ہے اس میں تاخیر لازم آئے گی اور اگر قعدہ اولی کے بعد بھول کر پانچویں رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا اور اس کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید بھی کر دیا تو حکم یہ ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ چھٹی رکعت ملا لے تا کہ چار رکعت فرض اور دو رکعت نفل ہو جائے۔ اب آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ ان دو رکعتوں کی زیادتی کی وجہ سے چار رکعت پر سلام جو واجب تھا وہ ترک ہو گیا پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ زیادتی بھی تاخیر رکن یا ترک واجب کو لازم ہے۔
Sujud al-sahw becomes necessary from every increase that is of the genus of prayer but not a part of prayer. He said: 'And sujud al-sahw becomes necessary when he adds in his prayer an action of its genus that is not from it.' And this indicates that the prostration of forgetfulness is obligatory — this is the correct view — because it is obligated to repair a deficiency that has occurred in the worship, so it is obligatory like the blood sacrifices in Hajj. And when it is obligatory, it is only obligatory due to the neglect of an obligatory act, or its delay, or the delay of a pillar forgetfully. This is the principle. And it was only obligated due to the increase because the increase is not free from delaying a pillar or neglecting an obligatory act. [Translation of the Urdu summary: Sujud al-sahw will be necessary when one performs an action in his prayer that is of the genus of prayer but not a part of it. This indicates that sujud al-sahw is obligatory — this is the correct view. It is wajib to repair a deficiency that has occurred in the worship, like the blood sacrifices in Hajj. It is only obligated due to the neglect or delay of a wajib or the delay of a pillar. The increase leads to either delaying a pillar or neglecting a wajib. The commentary elaborates with examples (two ruku's, three sajdas, etc.) and addresses an objection: if the principle is that sujud al-sahw is only for neglect/delay, then why is it required for increase? The answer: increase inevitably involves delaying a pillar or neglecting a wajib, as shown by the example of adding an extra rak'ah leading to omitting the obligatory salutation.]
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage begins with a matn from Al-Hidayah stating that sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory when one adds an act that is of the same genus as prayer (i.e., physically similar to prayer actions) but is not an integral part of it. The commentator explains that this matn proves the obligation (wujub) of sujud al-sahw. The correct view is that it is wajib, not sunnah as some Hanafis (like al-Karkhi) hold. The proof is qiyas: just as negligence in Hajj requires a dam (sacrifice) to compensate, and if not compensated one must repeat the Hajj, similarly, a deficiency in salah caused by forgetfulness is compensated by sujud al-sahw, and if not done, the salah must be repeated. Thus, sujud al-sahw is wajib. The commentator then establishes a key principle: sujud al-sahw is only obligated when one forgetfully leaves a wajib, delays a wajib, or delays a pillar (rukn). This principle seems to exclude increases, but the author clarifies that any increase inherently involves either delaying a pillar (e.g., doing three sajdas delays the standing for the next rak'ah) or leaving a wajib (e.g., adding an extra rak'ah results in omitting the wajib salutation at the end of the four rak'ahs). The passage then gives practical examples: performing two ruku's in one rak'ah, three sajdas, or standing up for a fifth rak'ah. In each case, sujud al-sahw is wajib.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, due to addition or omission of same-genus acts.
دم جنایت (dam al-jinayah): The sacrificial animal required as expiation for violations during Hajj/Umrah.
زیادہ فعل من جنس الصلوة (ziyadat fi'l min jins al-salah): Addition of an act that is of the same genus as prayer (e.g., extra ruku', sajda) but not an integral part of it.
اعادہ (i'adah): Repetition of the prayer; becomes wajib if sujud al-sahw is omitted in cases where it is required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does adding an extra sajdah (prostration) require sujud al-sahw according to the principle stated in the passage?
A) Because it is a completely invalid action.
B) Because it delays the next pillar (the standing).
C) Because it is not of the same genus as prayer.
D) Because it is a sin.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is wajib for forgetfully adding a same-genus act to prayer because it compensates a deficiency, analogous to dam in Hajj.

Sujud al-Sahw for Leaving a 'Sunna' Act that is Actually Wajib
Explains matn that sujud al-sahw is required for leaving a 'sunna' act meaning wajib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school obligates sujud al-sahw for leaving a 'sunna' act and correctly identify which acts trigger this obligation.

Core Idea
A 'sunna' act in this context means a wajib act proven by Sunnah; sujud al-sahw is only for omitting such acts, not for recommended sunan.

The matn states that sujud al-sahw becomes necessary when one leaves a 'sunna' act. This might confuse students, since leaving a recommended sunnah (like extra du'as) does not require sujud. The commentator resolves this by explaining that the author used 'sunna' to indicate acts whose obligation is established through the Sunnah of the Prophet (ﷺ), not through a direct Quranic command. In this lesson, we will unpack that terminological nuance and its legal implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent problem
Read the matn: 'Sujud al-sahw becomes necessary when he leaves a sunna act.' This seems to suggest that leaving any sunnah (recommended) act requires sujud. But that is not the Hanafi position. So what is going on?
2
Understand the commentator's clarification
The commentator (Marghinani) states that by 'sunna act' the author actually meant 'wajib act'. The term 'sunna' is used to indicate that the obligation of such acts is proven by the Sunnah, not by the Quran.
This is a key Hanafi terminological convention: sometimes 'sunna' is used for a wajib act that has a Sunnah proof.
3
Derive the ruling
Therefore, the ruling is: If a person forgetfully omits an act that is wajib and its obligation is established by the Sunnah (e.g., reciting Surah al-Fatihah, Qunut, Tashahhud, Takbirat al-Eidain), then sujud al-sahw becomes wajib.
Leaving a mere recommended sunnah (like additional voluntary prayers) does not require sujud al-sahw.
4
Identify the proof (dalil)
The proof is that the obligation of the act itself is established by the authoritative Sunnah of the Prophet (ﷺ). Although the commentator does not quote a specific hadith, the underlying dalil is the general authority of the Sunnah as a source of obligation.
5
Contrast with other schools
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may classify reciting Fatihah as fard (pillar) rather than wajib, and thus would require sujud al-sahw as well, but their reasoning differs. The Hanafi school uniquely distinguishes fard (from Quran) from wajib (from Sunnah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعل مسنون کے چھوڑے پر سجدہ سہولازم ہوتا ہے ( فعل مسنون کا مصداق ) قال ويلزمه اذا ترک فعلا مسنونا كانه اراد به فعلا واجبا الا أنه اراد بتسميته سنة ان وجوبها بالسنة ترجمہ اور سجدہ سہو لازم ہو گا جب کوئی فعل مسنون چھوڑا گویا اس سے فعل واجب کا اردہ کیا مگر اس کا سنت نام رکھنے سے یہ ارادہ کیا ہے کہ اس کا وجوب سنت سے ثابت ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ نمازی نے اگر کوئی فعل مسنون چھوڑ دیا تو اس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ متمن میں فعل مسنون سے مراد فعل واجب ہے کیونکہ فعل مسنون کو ترک کر دینے سے سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ترک واجب ہے ۔ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ متن کے اندر فعلا مسنونا کیوں کہا گیا ہے؟ جواب یہ بتلانے کے لئے کہ واجب کا وجوب سنت سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔
Sujud al-sahw becomes necessary upon leaving a sunna act. He said: 'And sujud al-sahw becomes necessary when he leaves a sunna act.' As if he intended by it a wajib act, except that he intended by naming it 'sunna' that its obligation is established by the Sunnah. [Urdu summary: Sujud al-sahw will be necessary when one leaves a sunna act. The commentator explains: the author of the matn meant a wajib act by 'sunna act,' because leaving an actual sunna (recommended) act does not require sujud al-sahw; only leaving a wajib does. The reason for calling it 'sunna' is to indicate that its obligation is proven by the Sunnah, not by the Quran.]
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage addresses a terminological issue in the matn. The matn says that sujud al-sahw is required for leaving a 'فعل مسنون' (sunna act). The commentator clarifies that this expression actually refers to a wajib act, because leaving a merely recommended (sunnah) act does not necessitate sujud al-sahw. The author deliberately used the term 'sunna' to indicate that the obligation of such acts is established through the Sunnah of the Prophet (ﷺ) rather than by an explicit Quranic text. Examples of such acts include reciting Surah al-Fatihah, Qunut, Tashahhud, and Takbirat al-Eidain. Thus, the ruling is: whoever forgetfully leaves an act that is proven wajib by the Sunnah must perform sujud al-sahw.

Key Terms
فعل مسنون (fi'l masnun): In this context, a wajib act whose obligation is proven by Sunnah (not Quran), e.g., reciting Fatihah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the matn use the term 'sunna act' (فعل مسنون) instead of 'wajib'?
A) To indicate the act is optional
B) To show its obligation is proven by the Sunnah
C) Because it is a mistake in the text
D) To distinguish it from pillars

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the term 'sunna' in the context of sujud al-sahw refers to a wajib act whose obligation is proven by Sunnah; omitting it forgetfully requires sujud al-sahw.

Specific Wajib Acts Requiring Sujud al-Sahw
Lists specific wajib acts requiring sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four wajib acts in prayer whose omission requires sujud al-sahw and explain the Hanafi proof based on the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah).

Core Idea
Continuous Prophetic practice (muwazabah) makes an act wajib; forgetting these four requires sujud al-sahw.

This passage identifies four specific acts in prayer—reciting Surah al-Fatihah, Qunut, Tashahhud, and the extra Takbirs of Eid—that are considered wajib in the Hanafi school. The author provides a key proof: the Prophet (ﷺ) continuously performed these acts without ever omitting them, which is an indicator of obligation (al-wujub). Understanding this ruling helps you distinguish between acts that require compensation (sujud al-sahw) when forgotten and those that do not, a critical skill for maintaining valid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Acts
List the specific acts mentioned: recitation of Surah al-Fatihah, recitation of Qunut, recitation of Tashahhud, and the extra Takbirs of Eid prayers. Note that each is considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
The passage emphasizes that these are not just sunnah but wajib, meaning their omission due to forgetfulness demands sujud al-sahw.
2
Understand the Proof: Muwazabah
The proof cited is the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) without ever omitting these acts. In Hanafi usul, such continuous practice is an indicator (amarah) of obligation (wujub).
This differs from direct textual commands; it is based on the Prophet's consistent action.
3
Connect to Sujud al-Sahw
Because these acts are wajib, forgetting any of them during prayer triggers the need for sujud al-sahw—two extra prostrations performed to compensate for the omission.
Sujud al-sahw itself is wajib when a wajib act is omitted unintentionally.
4
Note Cross-Madhhab Difference
Contrast with the Shafi'i school, which considers recitation of Surah al-Fatihah as fard (a pillar), not merely wajib. For them, omitting it invalidates the prayer, whereas Hanafis require only sujud al-sahw.
This practical difference highlights the importance of knowing which school's ruling one follows.
5
Confirm the Mufta Bihi
The passage ends by affirming that sujud al-sahw is the correct view (huwa al-sahih) for omission of these acts. This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement is mentioned here.

This passage enumerates specific acts whose omission due to forgetfulness makes sujud al-sahw wajib: recitation of Surah al-Fatihah in prayer, the Qunut (supplication in witr or fajr according to some), the Tashahhud (the testimony recited in the sitting), and the extra Takbirs in the 'Eid prayers. The proof given is that the Prophet (ﷺ) consistently performed these acts without ever omitting them, which indicates obligation. Additionally, these acts are attributed to the entire prayer (e.g., 'the Fatihah of the prayer'), showing they are integral to its completion. The commentator notes that Tashahhud applies to both the first and second sittings, and the recitation in both is wajib. The correct view is that sujud al-sahw is required for their omission.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in a specific position of prayer, often in witr or fajr, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
تکبیرات عیدین (takbirat al-'idayn): The extra takbirs recited in the Eid prayers (six in first rak'ah after opening takbir and five in second after rising from bowing).

The Prophet's continuous practice makes Fatihah, Qunut, Tashahhud, and Eid Takbirs wajib; forgetting them requires sujud al-sahw.

General Rule for Sajdah al-Sahw
States the principle triggering Sajdah al-Sahw with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three triggers of Sajdah al-Sahw according to the Hanafi school and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib when a wajib is omitted, a wajib is delayed, or a rukn is delayed.

This lesson introduces the foundational rule for Sajdah al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) in the Hanafi school. Understanding when Sajdah al-Sahw becomes obligatory is crucial for performing salah correctly. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the three key triggers that necessitate this prostration, along with illustrative examples and an important exception.

Guided Path
1
State the three triggers
Identify the three causes: omission of a wajib (tark wajib), delay of a wajib (ta'khir wajib), and delay of a rukn (ta'khir rukn). Memorize these conditions.
2
Distinguish omission from delay
Omission means the wajib act was completely left out (e.g., skipping the first sitting). Delay means the act was performed later than its proper time (e.g., standing for a fifth rak'ah delays the salam).
3
Work through the examples
Apply each trigger to the examples: leaving qa'dah ula (omission of wajib), standing for fifth rak'ah (delay of wajib), reciting durood in first sitting (delay of rukn).
4
Note the exception in Eid prayer
In Eid prayer, if extra takbirs are omitted, sajdah is not performed due to the crowd (izdiham). This is a special dispensation.
5
Recognize the hukm of Sajdah al-Sahw
Sajdah al-Sahw itself is wajib, not fard, because its obligation is established by non-definitive evidence. It compensates for the mistake but does not invalidate the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السيو
شرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم فاضل مصنف نے فرمایا چونکہ سجدۂ سہو واجب ہے اس لئے سجدہ سہو اس وقت واجب ہوگا جبکہ کہوا کوئی واجب چھوٹ گیا ہو یا واجب کوادا کرنے میں تاخیر ہوگئی ہو یا کسی رکن کی ادائیگی میں تاخیر ہوگئی ہو۔ ترک واجب کی مثالی قعدہ اولی کا ترک کرنا ہے یا عیدین کی نماز میں تکبیرات زوائد کا ترک کرنا ہے (لیکن عیدین کی نماز میں ازدحام کثیرہ کی وجہ سے سجدہ نہیں کیا جائے گا) تاخیر واجب کی مثال جیسے پانچوں رکعت کے لئے سہوا کھڑا ہو گیا تو اس سے سلام میں تاخیر ہوگئی اور سلام واجب ہے اور تا خیر رکن کی مثال جیسے قعد : 101 میں تشہد پڑھنے کے بعد درود پڑھنے لگا تو تیسری رکعت کا قیام جو فرض ہے اس میں تاخیر ہوگئی ۔ بہر حال سجدہ سہو واجب ہونے میں اصول یہی ۔۔ کہ سہو اترک واجب پایا جائے یا تاخیر واجب یا تاخیر رکن ۔
Chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah, the Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume two, said: Since Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib, Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib when some wajib is omitted, or there is delay in performing a wajib, or there is delay in performing a rukn. Example of omission of wajib: leaving the first sitting (qa'dah ula), or leaving the extra takbirs in the Eid prayer (but in Eid prayer due to great crowd, sajdah is not performed). Example of delay of wajib: such as one stood up for the fifth rak'ah inadvertently, then there was delay in salutation (salam) and salam is wajib. Example of delay of rukn: such as after reciting tashahhud in the first sitting, he started reciting durood, then the standing for the third rak'ah which is fard was delayed. In any case, the principle for Sajdah al-Sahw being wajib is this: that forgetfully an omission of a wajib occurs, or delay of a wajib, or delay of a rukn.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Sajdah al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) by stating the foundational rule according to the Hanafi school. The commentator explains that Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib (necessary) not optional, and it becomes binding in three scenarios: first, when a wajib act is completely omitted, such as skipping the first sitting (qa'dah ula) or leaving the extra takbirs in Eid prayer (though in crowded Eid prayer, sajdah is waived). Second, when a wajib act is delayed, like standing for a fifth rak'ah inadvertently which delays the obligatory salam. Third, when a rukn (integral) is delayed, like starting to recite durood after tashahhud in the first sitting, thereby delaying the standing for the third rak'ah which is fard. The principle is summarized: Sajdah al-Sahw is required whenever an omission of a wajib, or a delay of a wajib, or a delay of a rukn occurs forgetfully.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for mistakes in prayer.
ترک واجب (tark wajib): Omission of an obligatory component of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Deliberately skipping the first sitting
C) Inadvertently delaying the standing of the third rak'ah by reciting durood after tashahhud
D) Performing an extra prostration inadvertently

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib only when a wajib is omitted, a wajib is delayed, or a rukn is delayed forgetfully.

Increase in Prayer Necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw
Rational proof for Sajdah al-Sahw on increase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why any forgetful increase in prayer triggers Sajdah al-Sahw according to the Hanafi school, and apply this principle to specific scenarios.

Core Idea
An increase in prayer necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw because it necessarily causes delay or omission of a wajib.

We know that Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib when a wajib is omitted or delayed. But what about when we add an extra action by mistake? That seems like an increase, not an omission. This lesson resolves that paradox: the Hanafi school shows that every increase inevitably leads to a delay or omission, so the same rule applies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the objection
State the Hanafi rule: Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib for omission of a wajib or delay of a rukn. Then state the objection: an increase (extra action) does not appear to be an omission or delay, so why would it trigger sajdah?
The objection is the catalyst for the discussion.
2
Examine the Hanafi response
The response is that every increase necessarily entails either a delay of a rukn or an omission of a wajib. This is a rational inference (dalil aqli). The passage provides two examples to prove this point.
The key is causation: increase -> necessary consequence -> trigger.
3
Analyze the first example: extra prostrations
If a person performs an extra prostration, the standing (qiyam) which is a rukn is delayed. This delay triggers Sajdah al-Sahw. So the increase indirectly causes a delay.
Extra prostration delays the next rukn (standing).
4
Analyze the second example: extra rak'ah
If after the first sitting (qada ula) one forgetfully stands for a fifth rak'ah and completes it with prostrations, the correct remedy is to add a sixth rak'ah so that four become fard and two become nafl. This addition causes the obligatory salam (after four rak'ahs) to be omitted from its proper place.
The extra rak'ah leads to omission of a wajib (salam at its proper time).
5
Conclude the principle
Thus, any forgetful increase in prayer inevitably leads to either a delay of a rukn or an omission of a wajib. Therefore, Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib. The ruling is consistent.
No need to list every possible increase; the principle covers all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و انما وجبت الزيادة الخ سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ سجدہ سہو ترک واجب واجب ہوگا یا تاخیر واجب سے یا تاخیر رکن سے لیکن زیادتی کی صورت میں نہ ترک واجب ہے اور نہ تاخیر ہے الہند از یادتی کی صورت میں سجدہ سہو واجب نہ ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ اول باب میں کہا گیا ہے کہ زیادتی کی صورت میں سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ زیادتی کی صورت میں بھی تاخیر رکن یا ترک واجب لازم آتا ہے چنانچہ اگر تمین سجدے کئے تو قیام جور کن اور فرض ہے اس میں تاخیر لازم آئے گی اور اگر قعدہ اولی کے بعد بھول کر پانچویں رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا اور اس کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید بھی کر دیا تو حکم یہ ہے کہ اس کے ساتھ چھٹی رکعت مالا لے تا کہ چار رکعت فض اور دورکعت نفل ہو جائے۔ اب آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ ان دو رکعتوں کی زیادتی کی وجہ سے چار رکعت پر سلام جو واجب تھا وہ ترک ہو گیا پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ زیادتی بھی تاخیر رکن یا ترک واجب کو ستلزم ہے۔
And the phrase 'wa innama wajibat al-ziyadah' etc. is an answer to a question. The gist of the question is: You said that Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib from omission of a wajib, or from delay of a wajib, or from delay of a rukn, but in the case of increase, there is neither omission of a wajib nor delay. Especially in the case of increase, Sajdah al-Sahw should not be wajib, although at the beginning of the chapter it was said that in the case of increase, Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib. The answer is that in the case of increase, delay of a rukn or omission of a wajib is inevitably entailed. For example, if he performed extra prostrations, then the standing is delayed which is fard. And if after the first sitting he forgot and stood for the fifth rak'ah and also performed prostrations in it, then the ruling is that he should add a sixth rak'ah with it so that four rak'ahs become fard and two rak'ahs become nafl. Now observe that due to these two extra rak'ahs, the salutation which was wajib upon four rak'ahs was omitted. Thus it is proven that increase also entails delay of a rukn or omission of a wajib.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection: if Sajdah al-Sahw is triggered only by omission or delay, how does an increase (like adding an extra rak'ah or extra prostrations) cause it? The answer is that an increase inevitably leads to either a delay of a rukn or an omission of a wajib. For instance, if one performs extra prostrations, the standing for the next rukn is delayed. If one stands for a fifth rak'ah after the first sitting, the correct procedure is to add a sixth rak'ah to make the extra two rak'ahs nafl, but this causes the wajib salam to be omitted from its proper place. Thus, the increase itself is not the direct cause, but its necessary consequence is a valid trigger for Sajdah al-Sahw. This shows the internal consistency of the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
زیادتی (ziyadah): Increase in the actions of prayer, such as extra rak'ahs or extra prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Any addition invalidates the prayer
D) The increase is considered a form of omission

Key Takeaway
Every forgetful increase in prayer triggers Sajdah al-Sahw because it necessarily causes a delay of a rukn or an omission of a wajib.
