Wajib Acts Requiring Sajdah al-Sahw: Principle, Evidence, and Specifics
Ruling with proof: lists wajib acts and their evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five specific wajib acts whose omission necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw, explain the Hanafi evidence for their obligation, and resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute about Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs and the nature of the last sitting.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-Sahw is only required for omitting a wajib act – and five specific acts are wajib by the Prophet's continuous practice.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies that Sajdah al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) is not triggered by leaving a mere sunnah, but only by omitting a wajib (obligatory) element of prayer. The author explains why the base text uses the term 'recommended act' (fi'l masnun) – it is to highlight that the obligation is proven by the Sunnah, not the Qur'an. He then lists five specific wajib acts: reciting Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of fard, the Qunut supplication in Witr, Tashahhud in both sittings, the extra takbirs of Eid prayer, and reciting aloud/quietly in its proper place. For each, the proof is the Prophet's continuous practice and the fact that these acts are attributed to the whole prayer, indicating they are integral characteristics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
Sajdah al-Sahw is required only for omitting a wajib act, not a sunnah. The text's phrase 'fi'l masnun' is a metaphor for 'wajib' to indicate that the obligation is established by the Sunnah.
This is a key Hanafi usul point: the continuous practice of the Prophet (without ever omitting) is evidence of wujub.
2
List the five specific wajib acts
1) Reciting Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer. 2) Reciting Qunut in Witr. 3) Reciting Tashahhud in both the first and second sittings. 4) The extra takbirs of Eid prayers. 5) Reciting aloud where it is required to be audible, and quietly where required to be silent.
Note the intra-Hanafi difference: according to the mufta bihi view, Fatiha is wajib only in the first two rak'ahs of fard; leaving it in the last two does not require sajdah.
3
Understand the first proof: continuous practice
The Prophet (peace be upon him) continuously performed these acts without ever omitting them. In Hanafi usul, such continuous practice (muwazabah) is a sign of obligation (amarat al-wujub).
This is zanni al-thubut (probative transmission) because it comes from ahad reports, but it is binding.
4
Understand the second proof: attribution to the whole prayer
These acts are attributed to the entire prayer (e.g., 'Qunut of Witr', 'Takbirat of Eid prayer', 'Tashahhud of prayer'). This shows they are specific characteristics (khasa'is) of that prayer, and specificity is proven by obligation.
The logic: if something is uniquely associated with the prayer, it must be a required part (wajib), not merely recommended.
5
Resolve the objection about the last sitting
The text says 'all of that is wajib' (wa kullu dhalika wajib) but the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is actually fard. The author clarifies that 'leaving' here means delay (e.g., standing for a fifth rak'ah without intention), not complete omission. Complete omission invalidates the prayer; delay requires sajdah.
This is an example of takhsis (specification) in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعل مسنون کے چھوڑے پر سجدہ سہولازم ہوتا ہے ( فعل مسنون کا مصداق )
قال ويلزمه اذا ترک فعلا مسنونا كانه اراد به فعلا واجبا الا أنه اراد بتسميته سنة ان وجوبها بالسنة
ترجمہ اور سجدہ سہو لازم ہو گا جب کوئی فعل مسنون چھوڑا گویا اس سے فعل واجب کا اردہ کیا مگر اس کا سنت نام رکھنے سے یہ ارادہ کیا ہے کہ اس کا وجوب سنت سے ثابت ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، صاحب قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ نمازی نے اگر کوئی فعل مسنون چھوڑ دیا تو اس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ متمن میں فعل مسنون سے مراد فعل واجب ہے کیونکہ فعل مسنون کو ترک کر دینے سے سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوتا بلکہ ترک واجب ہے ۔ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ متن کے اندر فعلا مسنونا کیوں کہا گیا ہے؟
جواب یہ بتلانے کے لئے کہ واجب کا وجوب سنت سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔
سورہ فاتحہ یا قنوت یا تشہد یا تکبیرات عیدین چھوڑنے سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے
قال او ترك قراءة الفاتحة لانها واجبة او القنوت او التشهد او تكبيرات العيدين لانها واجبات فانه عليه السلام واظب عليها من غير تركها غير مرة وهى امارة الوجوب ولانها تضاف الى جميع الصلوة فدل انها من خصائصها وذلك بالوجوب ثم ذكر التشهد يحتمل القعدة الاولى والثانية والقراءة فيهما وكل ذلك واجب وفيها سجدة السهو هو الصحيح

ترجمہ کہا کہ یا فاتحہ کی قرآت چھوڑ دی کیونکہ ( نماز میں فاتحہ پڑھنا ) واجب ہے، یا دعاء قنوت چھوڑ دے یا تشہد یا تکبیرات عید بن چھوڑ دے کیونکہ یہ چیزیں واجبات ہیں۔ اس لئے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان پر مواظبت فرمائی ہے بغیر کبھی ترک کئے اور یہ علامت ہے وجوب کی ۔ اور اس لئے کہ ہی چیزیں پوری نماز کی طرف منسوب کی جاتی ہیں۔ پس اس بات پر دلالت ہوئی کہ یہ چیزیں نماز کے خصائص میں سے ہیں۔ اور یہ اختصاص واجب ہونے کی وجہ سے ہوگا۔ پھر تشہد کا (مطلقا) ذکر کرنا احتمال رکھتا ہے قعدہ اولیٰ اور ثانیہ کا اور ان دونوں میں التحیات پڑھے جانے کا۔ اور ان میں سے ہر ایک واجب ہے اور ان کے ترک میں سجدہ سہو لازم ہے۔ یہی صحیح ہے۔
تشریح اس عبارت میں ان چیزوں کی تفصیل ہے جن کے ترک کر دینے سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا کہ نماز کے اندر قرآت فاتحہ کو چھوڑنا بھی موجب سجدہ ہے کیونکہ قرآت فاتحہ واجب ہے لیکن یہ خیال رہے کہ فرض کی پہلی دو رکعتوں میں ترک فاتحہ سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا اور آخر کی دورکعتوں میں ترک فاتحہ سے سجدہ واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آخر کی دو رکعتوں میں فاتحہ کا پڑھنا واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ مستحب ہے۔ البتہ امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی روایت یہ ہے کہ اخربین میں بھی ترک قرآت فاتحہ سے سجدہ ہو
واجب ہو جائے گا۔
نماز وتر میں دعاء قوت چھوڑ نا اور تشہد کا چھوڑ نا اور تکبیرات عیدین کو چھوڑنا یہ سب موجب سجدہ ہیں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ تینوں چیزیں واجب ہیں اور ترک واجب سے سجدہ سہو واجب ہو جاتا ہے لہذا ان کے ترک سے بھی سجدہ واجب ہو جائے گا۔ اور ان چیزوں کے واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ان چیزوں پر مداومت فرمائی ہے اور کبھی ترک نہیں کیا ہے اور رسول پاک صلى الله عليه وسلم کا کسی چیز پر بغیر ترک کئے مداومت فرمانا اس کے واجب ہونے کی علامت ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان چیزوں کو پوری نماز کی طرف منسوب کیا جاتا ہے چنانچہ کہا جاتا ہے قنوت الوتر تکبیرات صلاۃ عیدین، تشہد صلاۃ ۔ پس ان چیزوں کو پوری نماز کی طرف منسوب کیا جانا دلیل ہے اس بات کی کہ یہ چیزیں نماز کے خصائص میں سے ہیں۔ اور اختصاص ثابت ہوتا ہے وجوب سے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ یہ چیزیں واجبات میں ہے ہیں۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ شیخ ابو الحسن قدوری نے لفظ تشہد ذکر کیا ہے۔ اور لفظ تشہد قعدہ اولی اور قعدہ اخیرہ اور التحیات پڑھنے پر بولا
جاتا ہے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک واجب ہے اور ان سب کے ترک میں سجدہ سہو لازم ہے یہی قول صحیح ہے۔ ہدایہ کی اس عبارت پر اعتراض ہے وہ یہ کہ صاحب ہدانہ نے فرمایا ہے و کل ذلک واجب اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ بھی واجب ہے حالانکہ قعدہ اخیرہ واجب نہیں ہے بکہ فرض ہے اس کو ترک کرنے سے نما ہی فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عبارت میں تخصیص ہے یعنی قعدہ اخیرہ کے ترک سے مراد اس کی تاخیر ہے یعنی بغیر قعدہ اخیرہ کئے اگر پانچویں رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا اور پانچویں رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا بلکہ قعدہ کی طرف لوٹ آیا تو سجدہ سہو کر کے نماز پوری کر لے چونکہ تاخیر میں بھی ایک گونہ ترک ہے اس لئے تاخیر کو ترک کے ساتھ تعبیر کر دیا گیا۔
جہری نماز میں سرا اور سری نماز میں جہراً قرآت سے بھی سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے
ولوجهر الامام فيما يخافت او خافت فيما يجهر تلزمه سجدتا السهو لان الجهر في موضعه والمخافتة
Upon leaving a recommended act (fi'l masnun), Sajdah al-Sahw becomes binding. (The referent of 'recommended act'.) He said: And it becomes binding upon him when he leaves a recommended act, as if he intended thereby a wajib act, but he intended by naming it sunnah that its obligation is established by the Sunnah. Translation: And Sajdah al-Sahw will become binding when a recommended act is left, as if he intended a wajib act by it, but by calling it sunnah he intended that its obligation is proven by the Sunnah. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that if a worshipper leaves a recommended act, Sajdah al-Sahw becomes wajib upon him. Sahib al-Hidayah says that in the text, by 'recommended act' he means a wajib act, because leaving a recommended act does not necessitate Sajdah al-Sahw, rather leaving a wajib does. As for why the text said 'a recommended act', the answer is to indicate that the obligation of that wajib is proven by the Sunnah. Leaving Surah al-Fatiha, or Qunut, or Tashahhud, or the takbirs of Eid prayers necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw. He said: Or he left recitation of Fatiha because it is wajib, or Qunut, or Tashahhud, or the takbirs of the two Eids because they are wajibat. Indeed, the Prophet (peace be upon him) continuously performed them without ever leaving them, and that is an indication of obligation. And because they are attributed to the entire prayer, so this indicates that they are among the specific characteristics of prayer, and that specificity is due to being wajib. Then the mention of Tashahhud possibly includes the first and second sitting and the recitation in them, and all of that is wajib, and upon omitting them, Sajdah al-Sahw is necessary – that is the correct view. Translation: He said: Or he left the recitation of Fatiha because it is wajib, or the Qunut supplication, or Tashahhud, or the takbirs of Eid because these are wajibat. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) continuously performed them without ever leaving them, and that is a sign of obligation. And because these things are attributed to the entire prayer. So this indicates that they are among the specific characteristics of prayer. And that specificity is due to being wajib. Then the mention of Tashahhud (absolutely) includes the first sitting and the second sitting and the recitation in both. And each of these is wajib, and upon their omission, Sajdah al-Sahw is necessary. This is the correct view. Explanation: In this phrase, there is a detail of those things whose omission necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw. Thus he said: Leaving the recitation of Fatiha in prayer also necessitates sajdah, because recitation of Fatiha is wajib. But it should be noted that in the first two rak'ahs of the fard prayer, leaving Fatiha necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw, but in the last two rak'ahs, leaving Fatiha does not necessitate sajdah, because in the last two rak'ahs reciting Fatiha is not wajib but rather mustahabb. However, from Imam Abu Hanifa, there is a narration by Hasan ibn Ziyad that in the last two rak'ahs as well, leaving Fatiha would necessitate Sajdah al-Sahw. Leaving the Qunut supplication in Witr prayer, leaving Tashahhud, and leaving the takbirs of the two Eids – all necessitate sajdah. The proof is that these three things are wajib, and leaving a wajib necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw, so their omission also necessitates sajdah. And the proof that these things are wajib is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) continuously performed them and never left them. And the continuous performance of a thing by the Prophet without leaving it is a sign of its obligation. A second proof is that these things are attributed to the entire prayer – for example, it is said: Qunut al-Witr, Takbirat Salah al-'Eidain, Tashahhud al-Salah. So their attribution to the entire prayer is proof that these things are among the specific characteristics of prayer. And specificity is proven by obligation. Thus it is established that these things are among the wajibat. Sahib al-Hidayah said that Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri mentioned the word Tashahhud. And the word Tashahhud is used for the first sitting and the last sitting and the recitation of al-Tahiyyat. And each of these is wajib, and upon omitting any of them, Sajdah al-Sahw is necessary – this is the correct saying. There is an objection on this phrase of Hidayah: Sahib al-Hidayah said 'and all of that is wajib'. From this it appears that the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is also wajib, whereas the last sitting is not wajib but rather fard; leaving it invalidates the prayer. The answer is that there is specification (takhsis) in the phrase – meaning by 'leaving the last sitting' what is intended is its delay. That is, if he stood for the fifth rak'ah without performing the last sitting and did not bind the fifth rak'ah with prostrations but returned to the sitting, then he should perform Sajdah al-Sahw and complete the prayer. Since delay also constitutes a type of leaving, the delay was expressed as leaving. Also, reciting quietly in a loud prayer and loudly in a quiet prayer necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw. And if the Imam recites loudly where he should recite quietly, or quietly where he should recite loudly, two sajdahs of forgetfulness are required because loudness in its place and quietness in its place are wajib.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage clarifies that Sajdah al-Sahw is required only for omitting a wajib act, not a mere sunnah. The author explains why the text says 'recommended act (fi'l masnun)' – it is to indicate that the obligation of these acts is established by the Sunnah (non-Qur'anic evidence), not that they are merely recommended. The specific wajib acts listed are: recitation of Surah al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer, the Qunut supplication in Witr, Tashahhud (in both sittings), and the extra takbirs in Eid prayers. The evidence for their being wajib is twofold: first, the Prophet's continuous practice without ever omitting them (which is an indicator of obligation in Hanafi usul); second, these acts are attributed to the entire prayer (e.g., 'Qunut of Witr', 'Takbirat of Eid prayer'), showing they are integral characteristics of those prayers. The passage also addresses an objection about the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah): it is fard, not wajib. The text's statement that 'all of that is wajib' is interpreted as referring to the delay of the last sitting (e.g., standing for a fifth rak'ah), not its complete omission, because complete omission would invalidate the prayer, not merely require sajdah. Finally, a separate ruling: reciting aloud where one should be silent or silently where one should be aloud also necessitates Sajdah al-Sahw.

Key Terms
فعل مسنون (fi'l masnun): A recommended act in prayer; in this context, it is used to refer to a wajib act whose obligation is established by the Sunnah.
وت ر (witr): The odd-numbered salah performed after 'Isha; Qunut is a supplication recited in it.
تشہد (tashahhud): The recitation of al-Tahiyyat in the sitting position of prayer.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetful omissions or additions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following acts is considered wajib in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayer and its omission requires Sajdah al-Sahw?
A) Reciting a surah after Fatiha
B) Reciting Surah al-Fatiha
C) Raising the hands for takbir
D) Saying 'Ameen' after Fatiha

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-Sahw is required only for omitting a wajib act, and five specific wajib acts are identified by the Prophet's continuous practice and their attribution to the whole prayer: Fatiha in first two rak'ahs, Qunut, Tashahhud in both sittings, Eid takbirs, and proper loud/quiet recitation.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
When the Imam Recites Loudly in Silent Prayer: The Hanafi Rule on Sajdah Sahw
Ruling and proofs for sajdah sahw when imam recites loudly in silent prayers or silently in loud prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that jahr and ikhfah are wajib upon the imam, identify the condition that sajdah sahw applies only to the imam, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimal amount that triggers the obligation.

Core Idea
Reciting at the wrong volume is a wajib violation – the imam must perform sajdah sahw.

Leading a congregation in prayer carries specific duties. Among them is reciting at the prescribed volume: loud for Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, and Jumu'ah; silent for Zuhr and Asr. What happens if the imam accidentally switches? In the Hanafi school, this is not a minor slip – it is an omission of a wajib that requires compensation through sajdah sahw. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the subtle disagreement within the school on how much is too much.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam's recitation volume: jahr (loud) in loud prayers, ikhfah (silent) in silent prayers. The Hanafi ruling is that this is wajib upon the imam. Violation (e.g., jahr in silent prayer) constitutes omitting a wajib.
The ruling does not apply to the individual praying alone (munfarid).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah): he always recited loudly in night prayers and silently in daytime prayers. Additionally, silent daytime prayer was prescribed to protect the Qur'an from disbelievers' mockery (as occurred in Mecca).
The rational proof (ta'lil) is that silence in daytime was a protective measure, and protecting the Qur'an is wajib.
3
Understand the condition
This rule applies exclusively to the imam leading a congregation. The individual praying alone is not bound by the volume requirement because jahr and ikhfah are specific characteristics (khasais) of jama'ah.
The text states: 'وهذا فى حق الامام دون المنفرد' – this is in the case of the imam, not the individual.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on amount
There is a difference of narration (ikhtilaf al-riwaya) regarding the minimal amount of the violation that triggers sajdah. Imam Abu Hanifah said: one verse. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: three verses.
The text calls the relied-upon position 'the most correct (asahh) is the amount that makes the prayer valid' – i.e., a 'large amount' (kathir) that cannot be avoided.
5
Distinguish the reliance
The 'asahh' view is that if the change is significant (a 'large amount'), sajdah is wajib. A slight, unavoidable change does not trigger it. In practice, many Hanafi scholars adopt the Sahibayn's three-verse minimum as the standard.
The text does not explicitly choose; it presents both views and declares the 'asahh' as the amount that makes prayer valid.

جہری نماز میں سرا اور سری نماز میں جہراً قرآت سے بھی سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے
ولوجهر الامام فيما يخافت او خافت فيما يجهر تلزمه سجدتا السهو لان الجهر في موضعه والمخافتة في موضعها من الواجبات واختلف الرواية فى المقدار والاصح قدرما تجوزبه الصلوة في الفصلين لان اليسير من الجهر و الاخفاء لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه وعن الكثير ممكن وما تصح به الصلوة كثير غيران ذلك عنده آية واحدة وعند هما ثلث آيات وهذا فى حق الامام دون المنفرد لان الجهر والمخافتة من خصائص الجماعة
ترجمہ اور اگر امام نے ان نمازوں میں جہر کیا جن میں اخفاء کرنا واجب ہے یا ان نمازوں میں اخفاء کیا جن میں جہر کرنا واجب ہے تو اس پر سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا کیونکہ جہر اپنے موقع پر اور اخفاء اپنے موقع پر واجبات میں سے ہے اور مقدار کے بارے میں روایت مختلف ہو گئی اور اصح دونوں صورتوں میں اتنی مقدار ہے جس سے نماز جائز ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ خفیف سا جہر، اور خفیف سا اخفاء اس سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں ہے اور کثیر مقدار سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے اور جس قدر سے نماز صحیح ہو جاتی ہے وہ کثیر ہے مگر یہ کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ مقدار ایک آیت ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تین آیتیں ہیں اور ان دونوں صورتوں میں سجدہ کا واجب ہونا امام کے حق میں ہے نہ کہ منفرد کے حق میں کیونکہ جہر اور اخفاء جماعت کے خصائص میں سے ہے۔ تشریح ہمارے نزدیک سری نماز کے اندر جہر کرنا اور جہری نماز میں اخفاء کرنا سجدہ سہو کو واجب کرتا ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ان صورتوں میں سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوتا ۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ اگر سری نماز میں جہر کیا تو سلام کے بعد سجدہ سہو کرے اور اگر جہری نماز میں اخفاء کیا تو سلام سے پہلے سجدہ کرے۔ امام احمد سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں اگر سجدہ کر لیا تو فالحمد اللہ علی ملک اور اگر سجدہ نہیں کیا تو بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا مستدل حضرت ابو قتادہ کی حدیث ہے یعنی ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کان يسمعنا الآية والايتين في الظهر والعصر یعنی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم ہم کو ظہر اور عصر میں ایک یا دو آیتیں سنادیا کرتے تھے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر اور عصر میں اخفاء واجب نہیں ہے پس جب ان نمازوں میں اخفاء واجب نہیں ہے تو رات کی نمازوں میں جہر کیونکر واجب ہوگا اور جب جہری نمازوں میں جہر اور سری نمازوں میں اخفاء واجب نہیں ہے تو اس کو چھوڑ دینے سے سجدہ سہو بھی واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ (الکفایہ ) ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ظہر اور عصر کی نماز میں جہر اس لئے کیا ہے کہ لوگوں کو معلوم ہو جائے کہ ظہر اور عصر میں بھی قرآت مشروع ہے پس جب آپ کا مقصد یہ تھا تو اس لئے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم پر سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جن نمازوں میں بالجہر قرآت کی جاتی ہے ان میں جہر کرنا امام پر واجب ہے۔ تا کہ امام کی قرآت کو مقتدی بھی سن لے اور امام کی قرآت مقتدی کے قائم مقام ہو جائے اور دن کی نمازوں میں امام پر اخفاء اس لئے واجب ہے کہ اخفاء اس میں مشروع کیا گیا ہے تاکہ کفار کے غلطی میں ڈالنے سے قرآن پاک کو محفوظ کیا جاسکے۔ چنانچہ آپ کو معلوم ہوگا کہ مدنی آقا نے اخفاء قرآت کا حکم اس وقت دیا ہے جبکہ کفار آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کو تلاوت فرمانے کے وقت غلطی میں ڈالنے کی کوشش کرتے تھے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ دن کی نمازوں میں اخفاء واجب ہے۔ رات کی نمازوں میں واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ رات میں وہ لوگ کپڑے سوتے رہتے تھے پس حاصل یہ ہوا کہ دن کی نمازوں میں اخفاء قرآن کی حفاظت کے پیش نظر شروع کیا گیا ہے اور اس طرح کی چیزوں سے قرآن کی حفاظت کرنا واجب ہے پس ثابت ہوا کہ دن کی نمازوں میں اخفاء واجب ہے۔ بہر حال جب سری نمازوں میں جہر کرنا اور جہری نمازوں میں اخفاء کرنا واجب ہوا تو اس کو ترک کرنے سے سجدہ سہو بھی واجب ہو جائے گا کیونکہ ترک واجب سے سجدہ واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ (الکفایہ )
Reciting silently in loud prayers and loudly in silent prayers also makes sajdah sahw obligatory. And if the imam recites loudly where he should be silent, or silently where he should be loud, the two prostrations of forgetfulness are incumbent upon him, because loudness in its place and silence in its place are among the wajibat. And the narration differs concerning the amount; the most correct is the amount that makes the prayer valid in both cases, because a slight loudness and a slight silence cannot be avoided, whereas a large amount can be avoided. And that which makes the prayer valid is a large amount—except that according to Abu Hanifah it is one verse, and according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is three verses. And this is in the case of the imam, not the individual (munfarid), because loudness and silence are among the specific characteristics of congregation. Translation: And if the imam recites loudly in prayers where silence is wajib, or silently in prayers where loudness is wajib, sajdah sahw becomes necessary. Because loudness in its place and silence in its place are among the wajibat. And the narration differs concerning the amount; the most correct is the amount that makes the prayer valid in both cases, because a slight loudness and a slight silence cannot be guarded against, whereas a large amount can be guarded against. And that which makes the prayer valid is a large amount—except that according to Imam Abu Hanifah this amount is one verse, and according to the two (Sahibayn) it is three verses. And in these two cases, the obligation of sajdah is for the imam, not for the one praying alone, because loudness and silence are from the peculiarities of congregation. Explanation: According to us, reciting loudly in silent prayers and silently in loud prayers makes sajdah sahw obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i said that in these cases sajdah sahw is not obligatory. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad said: if one recites loudly in a silent prayer, he should prostrate after the salam; and if he recites silently in a loud prayer, he should prostrate before the salam. From Imam Ahmad there is a narration that in these cases if he prostrates, then al-hamdu lillah, and if he does not prostrate, there is no harm. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Abu Qatada: that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم used to make us hear a verse or two in Zuhr and Asr. That is, the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم used to make us hear one or two verses in Zuhr and Asr. From this it is understood that silence in Zuhr and Asr is not wajib; so when silence in these prayers is not wajib, how can loudness in night prayers be wajib? And when loudness in loud prayers and silence in silent prayers are not wajib, then leaving them does not make sajdah sahw wajib. (Al-Kifayah) Our response is that the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم recited loudly in Zuhr and Asr in order to inform people that recitation is legitimate in Zuhr and Asr as well. Thus, since his purpose was this, sajdah sahw was not necessary for him. Our proof is that in prayers that are recited loudly, loudness is wajib upon the imam so that the followers may hear the imam's recitation and it suffices for them. And in daytime prayers, silence is wajib upon the imam because silence was prescribed in them to protect the Qur'an from the disbelievers' attempts to lead into error. Indeed, you will know that the Divine Master gave the command of silent recitation at a time when the disbelievers tried to lead the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم into error during his recitation. This is why silence in daytime prayers is wajib. It is not wajib in night prayers because at night those people were sleeping in their clothes. So the conclusion is that silence in daytime prayers was prescribed for the protection of the Qur'an, and such protection is wajib. Therefore, it is proven that silence in daytime prayers is wajib. In any case, when reciting loudly in silent prayers and silently in loud prayers is wajib, then leaving it makes sajdah sahw wajib, because leaving a wajib necessitates sajdah. (Al-Kifayah)
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. It addresses the obligation of sajdah sahw when an imam recites loudly in a silent prayer (like Zuhr, Asr) or silently in a loud prayer (like Maghrib, Isha, Fajr). The Hanafi position is that such a change is a wajib specific to the imam, and its omission requires sajdah sahw. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimal amount that triggers the obligation: Abu Hanifah says one verse, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say three verses. The relied-upon position (as per the text: 'the most correct') is the amount that renders the prayer valid, which is considered 'a large amount' – i.e., a verse or more that is considered significant. The passage then presents the views of other imams: al-Shafi'i holds no sajdah required, Malik and Ahmad (in one narration) require sajdah but differ on timing (after or before salam), and Ahmad has another narration that sajdah is optional. The Hanafi response to Shafi'i's dalil (the Prophet reciting audibly in Zuhr/Asr on occasion) explains that the Prophet did so for a specific purpose (teaching), not as a regular practice, so the general rule of silent daytime prayer remains. The Hanafis provide a rational justification: daytime silent prayers were instituted to protect the Qur'an from disbelievers' disturbance (as occurred historically), while night prayers are loud because there was no such risk. Therefore, the imam's loudness in silent prayers or silence in loud prayers violates a wajib, requiring sajdah sahw. This ruling applies only to the imam leading a congregation, not to an individual praying alone, because jahr and ikhfah are characteristics of congregational prayer.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation in prayers where it is prescribed (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, and Jumu'ah). It is wajib upon the imam.
الإخفاء (al-ikhfah): Silent recitation in prayers where it is prescribed (Zuhr, Asr). It is wajib upon the imam.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetful omission or alteration of a wajib in prayer. Here, violation of prescribed loudness/silence requires it.
صاحبین (al-Sahibayn): Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifah. Their view here: three verses minimal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount of loud recitation in a silent prayer that triggers sajdah sahw?
A) Any amount, even one word.
B) One verse (Abu Hanifah) or three verses (Sahibayn).
C) Half a juz.
D) Only if the entire prayer is recited loudly.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the imam must recite at the prescribed volume; any significant change due to forgetfulness requires sajdah sahw, and the minimal amount is a matter of intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Do Other Schools Require Sajdah? The Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Volume Violation
Ruling and proofs for sajdah sahw when imam recites loudly in silent prayers or silently in loud prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Shafi'i position on volume violation, cite the hadith of Abu Qatada, evaluate the Hanafi response, state the views of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the schools.

Core Idea
Shafi'is say no sajdah needed because the Prophet once recited audibly in Zuhr – Hanafis reply that was a teaching act.

The Hanafi ruling that volume violation requires sajdah sahw is not universal. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees entirely, while Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad have their own nuanced positions. This lesson dissects the inter-madhhab debate, focusing on the Shafi'i proof from the hadith of Abu Qatada and the Hanafi rejoinder. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between a general rule and an exceptional act of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and the opposing school's view
Hanafis: jahr/ikhfah are wajib, so violation requires sajdah. Shafi'is: these are not wajib, so no sajdah.
Malik and Ahmad hold positions requiring sajdah but with differences on timing.
2
Identify the opponent's dalil
Shafi'is cite the hadith of Abu Qatada: the Prophet used to make them hear a verse or two in Zuhr and Asr. This shows that silence was not always maintained, so it cannot be wajib.
The hadith is from Sahih Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue that the Prophet's audible recitation was an exceptional act to teach that recitation is lawful in Zuhr/Asr; it does not negate the general rule of silence. They also provide a rational proof: silence was prescribed to protect the Qur'an from disbelievers.
The Hanafi response emphasizes the distinction between a one-time teaching act and the continuous practice (muwazabah).
4
Note the positions of Malik and Ahmad
Imam Malik: if imam recites loudly in silent prayer, sajdah after salam; if silently in loud prayer, sajdah before salam. Imam Ahmad: two narrations – one similar to Malik, another that sajdah is optional.
These positions are presented in the passage but not elaborated with proofs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis require sajdah sahw for any significant volume violation; Shafi'is never require it; Malikis require it but at different times depending on the type of violation. Hanbalis have a lenient option.
This difference affects actual practice when leading mixed-madhhab congregations.

Source Text

جہری نماز میں سرا اور سری نماز میں جہراً قرآت سے بھی سجدہ سہو واجب ہوتا ہے
ولوجهر الامام فيما يخافت او خافت فيما يجهر تلزمه سجدتا السهو لان الجهر في موضعه والمخافتة في موضعها من الواجبات واختلف الرواية فى المقدار والاصح قدرما تجوزبه الصلوة في الفصلين لان اليسير من الجهر و الاخفاء لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه وعن الكثير ممكن وما تصح به الصلوة كثير غيران ذلك عنده آية واحدة وعند هما ثلث آيات وهذا فى حق الامام دون المنفرد لان الجهر والمخافتة من خصائص الجماعة
ترجمہ اور اگر امام نے ان نمازوں میں جہر کیا جن میں اخفاء کرنا واجب ہے یا ان نمازوں میں اخفاء کیا جن میں جہر کرنا واجب ہے تو اس پر سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا کیونکہ جہر اپنے موقع پر اور اخفاء اپنے موقع پر واجبات میں سے ہے اور مقدار کے بارے میں روایت مختلف ہو گئی اور اصح دونوں صورتوں میں اتنی مقدار ہے جس سے نماز جائز ہو جاتی ہے کیونکہ خفیف سا جہر، اور خفیف سا اخفاء اس سے بچاؤ ممکن نہیں ہے اور کثیر مقدار سے بچاؤ ممکن ہے اور جس قدر سے نماز صحیح ہو جاتی ہے وہ کثیر ہے مگر یہ کہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ مقدار ایک آیت ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تین آیتیں ہیں اور ان دونوں صورتوں میں سجدہ کا واجب ہونا امام کے حق میں ہے نہ کہ منفرد کے حق میں کیونکہ جہر اور اخفاء جماعت کے خصائص میں سے ہے۔ تشریح ہمارے نزدیک سری نماز کے اندر جہر کرنا اور جہری نماز میں اخفاء کرنا سجدہ سہو کو واجب کرتا ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ان صورتوں میں سجدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوتا ۔ امام مالک اور امام احمد نے فرمایا کہ اگر سری نماز میں جہر کیا تو سلام کے بعد سجدہ سہو کرے اور اگر جہری نماز میں اخفاء کیا تو سلام سے پہلے سجدہ کرے۔ امام احمد سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں اگر سجدہ کر لیا تو فالحمد اللہ علی ملک اور اگر سجدہ نہیں کیا تو بھی کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی کا مستدل حضرت ابو قتادہ کی حدیث ہے یعنی ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کان يسمعنا الآية والايتين في الظهر والعصر یعنی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم ہم کو ظہر اور عصر میں ایک یا دو آیتیں سنادیا کرتے تھے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظہر اور عصر میں اخفاء واجب نہیں ہے پس جب ان نمازوں میں اخفاء واجب نہیں ہے تو رات کی نمازوں میں جہر کیونکر واجب ہوگا اور جب جہری نمازوں میں جہر اور سری نمازوں میں اخفاء واجب نہیں ہے تو اس کو چھوڑ دینے سے سجدہ سہو بھی واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ Explanation: According to us, reciting loudly in silent prayers and silently in loud prayers makes sajdah sahw obligatory. Imam al-Shafi'i said that in these cases sajdah sahw is not obligatory. Thus, since his purpose was this, sajdah sahw was not necessary for him. Our proof is that in prayers that are recited loudly, loudness is wajib upon the imam so that the followers may hear the imam's recitation and it suffices for them. And in daytime prayers, silence is wajib upon the imam because silence was prescribed in them to protect the Qur'an from the disbelievers' attempts to lead into error. Indeed, you will know that the Divine Master gave the command of silent recitation at a time when the disbelievers tried to lead the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم into error during his recitation. This is why silence in daytime prayers is wajib. It is not wajib in night prayers because at night those people were sleeping in their clothes. So the conclusion is that silence in daytime prayers was prescribed for the protection of the Qur'an, and such protection is wajib. Therefore, it is proven that silence in daytime prayers is wajib. In any case, when reciting loudly in silent prayers and silently in loud prayers is wajib, then leaving it makes sajdah sahw wajib, because leaving a wajib necessitates sajdah. (Al-Kifayah)

The Hanafi position is that such a change is a wajib specific to the imam, and its omission requires sajdah sahw. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimal amount that triggers the obligation: Abu Hanifah says one verse, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say three verses. The relied-upon position (as per the text: 'the most correct') is the amount that renders the prayer valid, which is considered 'a large amount' – i.e., a verse or more that is considered significant. The passage then presents the views of other imams: al-Shafi'i holds no sajdah required, Malik and Ahmad (in one narration) require sajdah but differ on timing (after or before salam), and Ahmad has another narration that sajdah is optional. The Hanafi response to Shafi'i's dalil (the Prophet reciting audibly in Zuhr/Asr on occasion) explains that the Prophet did so for a specific purpose (teaching), not as a regular practice, so the general rule of silent daytime prayer remains. The Hanafis provide a rational justification: daytime silent prayers were instituted to protect the Qur'an from disbelievers' disturbance (as occurred historically), while night prayers are loud because there was no such risk. Therefore, the imam's loudness in silent prayers or silence in loud prayers violates a wajib, requiring sajdah sahw. This ruling applies only to the imam leading a congregation, not to an individual praying alone, because jahr and ikhfah are characteristics of congregational prayer.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation in prayers where it is prescribed (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, and Jumu'ah). It is wajib upon the imam in the Hanafi school.
الإخفاء (al-ikhfah): Silent recitation in prayers where it is prescribed (Zuhr, Asr). It is wajib upon the imam in the Hanafi school.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetful omission or alteration of a wajib in prayer. Here, violation of prescribed loudness/silence requires it (Hanafi view).
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): The Prophet's continuous and consistent practice. Hanafis use it to deduce wujub.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof used by Imam al-Shafi'i to argue that sajdah sahw is not required when the imam recites loudly in Zuhr or Asr?
A) No proof; he simply disagrees with Abu Hanifah.
B) The hadith of Abu Qatada: the Prophet audibly recited a verse or two in Zuhr and Asr.
C) The Quranic verse on silent prayer.
D) Consensus of the Medinan scholars.

Key Takeaway
The disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is on sajdah sahw for volume violation stems from differing interpretations of the Prophet's practice – whether silent recitation is wajib or sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Sajdah al-Sahw for Incorrect Jahr and Ikhfa
Ruling on sajdah for changing loudness in prayer with inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sajdah al-sahw for incorrect jahr/ikhfa, explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, and distinguish the rulings for imam vs. munfarid.

Core Idea
Changing prescribed loudness in prayer triggers sajdah for the imam, but only if the change is substantial.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario in congregational prayer: the imam inadvertently recites aloud in a silent prayer or softly in an audible prayer. The Hanafi school holds that such a change necessitates sajdah al-sahw, based on the principle that jahr and ikhfa are wajib acts in their respective contexts. However, this ruling is contested by other madhhabs and involves internal disagreement on the amount of change required.

Guided Path
1
Understand the base ruling
Identify that jahr in audible prayers and ikhfa in silent prayers are wajib for the imam. Omitting a wajib necessitates sajdah al-sahw.
This is the core Hanafi position.
2
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Examine Imam al-Shafi'i's objection using the hadith of Abu Qatada, and the Hanafi response distinguishing deliberate teaching from forgetfulness.
Note the role of intention in the Hanafi argument.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement on quantity
Compare the views of Abu Hanifa (one verse) vs. the Sahibayn (three verses) and the preferred view of Al-Hidayah (amount that validates prayer).
Understand why a small amount is exempted due to difficulty of avoidance.
4
Distinguish imam vs. munfarid
Recognize that jahr and ikhfa are characteristics of congregation; the munfarid has a choice, so no sajdah is required.
Address the objection regarding silent prayers using Nawadir vs. Zahir al-Riwayah.

ہونا تسلیم نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ سری نمازوں میں منفرد پر بھی اخفاء کے ساتھ قرآت کرنا واجب ہے۔ لہذا سری نمازوں میں ترک اخفاء کی وجہ سے منفرد پر بھی سجدہ سہو واجب ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اس صورت میں بھی منفرد پر سجدہ ہو واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ جواب یہ نوادر کی روایت ہے یعنی یہ سری نمازوں میں منفرد پر مخافت کا واجب ہونا نوادر کی روایت ہے اور ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق تو منفرد پر مخافت واجب نہیں شہرت ادا کی جائے اور منفرد کی نماز بر سبیل شہرت نہیں ہوتی اس لئے اس پر اختفاء کرنا واجب نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ اس کو اختیار ہو گا کہ وہ سری نمازوں میں بھی اخفاء کے ساتھ قرآت کرے یا جہر کے ساتھ کرے اور جب منفرد کو اختیار ہے تو ترک اخفاء کی وجہ سے اس پر سجدہ سہو واجب نہ ہوگا۔
امام کے بھولنے سے امام اور مقتدی دونوں پر سجدہ سہو لازم ہے
(عنابی)
قال وسهو الامام يوجب على المؤتم السجود لتقرر السبب الموجب فى حق الاصل ولهذا يلزمه حكم الاقامة بنية الامام فان لم يسجد الامام لم يسجد المؤتم لانه لايصير مخالفا وما التزم الاداء امتا بعا
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. [He said:] It is in its place from the obligatory acts. The narration differs regarding the amount, and the most correct is the amount with which prayer is valid in both cases, because a little loudness and a little softness cannot be avoided, but a large amount can be avoided. And what makes prayer valid is a large amount, except that according to Abu Hanifa it is one verse, and according to the two companions it is three verses. And this is in the right of the imam, not the individual, because loudness and softness are characteristics of congregation. Explanation: According to us, making loud in silent prayer and soft in loud prayer makes sajdah al-sahw obligatory. Imam Shafi'i said: In these cases, sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad said: If he made loud in silent prayer, he should perform sajdah after salam; if he made soft in loud prayer, he should perform sajdah before salam. From Imam Ahmad there is a narration: If he prostrated, then praise be to Allah; if he did not prostrate, there is no harm. Imam Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Abu Qatada: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to make us hear a verse or two in Zuhr and Asr.' From this it is understood that ikhfa in Zuhr and Asr is not obligatory; so if ikhfa is not obligatory in these prayers, how can jahr be obligatory in night prayers? And when jahr in loud prayers and ikhfa in silent prayers are not obligatory, then omitting them does not necessitate sajdah. (Al-Kifayah) Our response: The Prophet (peace be upon him) made loud in Zuhr and Asr to let people know that recitation is legislated in these prayers; since his purpose was that, sajdah was not obligatory. Our proof: In prayers where recitation is with jahr, it is obligatory for the imam to recite loudly so that the followers may hear and the imam's recitation substitutes for theirs. In day prayers, ikhfa is obligatory for the imam because it was legislated to protect the Quran from the disbelievers' attempts to cause confusion. Indeed, you know that the Medinan master gave the command of ikhfa when the disbelievers tried to confuse the Prophet during his recitation. That is why ikhfa is obligatory in day prayers, not in night prayers because at night those people were asleep. So the conclusion is that ikhfa in day prayers was introduced for the preservation of the Quran, and protecting the Quran from such things is obligatory. Thus it is proven that ikhfa is obligatory in day prayers. In any case, when making loud in silent prayers and soft in loud prayers is obligatory, then omitting it makes sajdah al-sahw obligatory because omitting a wajib necessitates sajdah. (Al-Kifayah) [Page 235] Remaining: Regarding how much ikhfa in loud prayers and how much jahr in silent prayers necessitates sajdah, the narrations differ. In Zahir al-Riwayah, little and much are equal: whether one made soft in loud prayer or loud in silent prayer, whether little or much, sajdah becomes obligatory. The author of Al-Hidayah said: The correct view is that it is the amount with which prayer is valid; if he makes ikhfa or jahr to that extent, sajdah becomes obligatory because a small amount of loudness or softness cannot be avoided, but a large amount can be avoided. Thus the ruling of forgetfulness is attached to a large amount, not a small amount. What makes prayer valid is large, and less than that is small. Regarding the amount of 'what makes prayer valid', there is disagreement: according to Abu Hanifa, one verse; according to the two companions, three verses. The author of Al-Hidayah says: The obligation of sajdah due to jahr in silent prayers and ikhfa in loud prayers is for the imam, not the individual. If the imam does this, sajdah becomes obligatory; if the individual does it, sajdah is not obligatory. The proof is that loudness and softness are characteristics of congregation; in loud prayers, the individual has a choice to recite loudly or softly. So when loudness or softness is not obligatory for the individual, omitting them does not necessitate sajdah. Some objected: The obligation of jahr in loud prayers being a characteristic of congregation is accepted because the individual has a choice, but the obligation of ikhfa in silent prayers being a characteristic of congregation is not accepted because in silent prayers it is obligatory for the individual to recite softly. Therefore, omitting ikhfa in silent prayers should necessitate sajdah for the individual as well, but the author of Al-Hidayah said that in this case too sajdah is not obligatory for the individual. The answer: This is a narration from Nawadir, i.e., the obligation of ikhfa for the individual in silent prayers is a Nawadir narration. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, ikhfa is not obligatory for the individual because ikhfa in day prayers was made obligatory to avoid the confusion from the disbelievers, and such confusion only occurs when prayer is performed publicly; the individual's prayer is not public, so ikhfa is not obligatory for him. Rather, he has a choice: he may recite softly or loudly in silent prayers. Since he has a choice, omitting ikhfa does not necessitate sajdah. The imam's forgetfulness necessitates sajdah for both the imam and the follower. (By way of annotation) He said: And the forgetfulness of the imam makes sajdah obligatory for the follower because the cause that makes it obligatory is established in the original, and for this reason the ruling of standing [in prayer] with the imam's intention applies to him. If the imam does not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate because he does not become an opponent, and he did not undertake the performance except by following.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses the ruling of sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) when an imam or individual prays with incorrect loudness (jahr) or softness (ikhfa). The author first establishes that changing the prescribed loudness triggers sajdah, as both jahr and ikhfa are wajib (obligatory acts) in their respective places. The text then delves into three major disputes: (1) Inter-madhhab: Imam Shafi'i holds that sajdah is not required in these cases, citing the hadith of Abu Qatada that the Prophet would occasionally recite aloud in Zuhr and Asr. Hanafi scholars reply that the Prophet did so deliberately to teach, not by forgetfulness. Malik and Ahmad have intermediate views on when to perform sajdah (before or after salam). (2) Intra-Hanafi: The amount of recitation that triggers sajdah is debated. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, any amount (little or much) suffices, but the author of Al-Hidayah prefers 'the amount with which prayer is valid'—considered 'kathir' (much). Abu Hanifa says one verse; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say three verses. (3) Implication for the individual (munfarid): The text rules that sajdah is only for the imam, because jahr and ikhfa are characteristics of congregation. The individual has no obligation; he may recite however he wishes. An objection arises regarding silent prayers where some narrations demand ikhfa for the individual, but the text clarifies that this is from Nawadir (rare transmissions), while Zahir al-Riwayah does not obligate it. The passage concludes with a separate ruling: if the imam forgets, both imam and follower must perform sajdah, but if the imam omits it, the follower does not do it alone.

Key Terms
جہر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayers where it is prescribed (e.g., Fajr, Maghrib, Isha).
اخفاء (ikhfa): Soft/quiet recitation in prayers where it is prescribed (e.g., Zuhr, Asr).
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for unintentional omissions or changes in the prayer.
منفرد (munfarid): An individual praying alone, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, if a person prays Zuhr alone and accidentally recites loudly, what is the ruling?
A) He must perform sajdah al-sahw after salam.
B) He must perform sajdah al-sahw before salam.
C) No sajdah al-sahw is required.
D) He must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
An imam who changes prescribed loudness in prayer must perform sajdah al-sahw if the change is substantial; the munfarid does not.

Salah — Prayer

Jahr and Ikhfa in Prayer: When Sujud al-Sahw is Wajib
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sujud al-sahw for jahr/ikhfa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when sujud al-sahw becomes wajib due to changing jahr/ikhfa and identify the mufta bihi position with its supporting proof.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw for jahr/ikhfa error is wajib only on the imam and only when the changed amount equals the minimum valid recitation.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya addresses a common scenario: a worshipper inadvertently changes from aloud to silent recitation or vice versa. Does this require sujud al-sahw? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the imam and the individual praying alone, and between small and large amounts of change. Understanding this ruling clarifies the obligations of the imam and the mercy shown to the munfarid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting views on the amount
Zahir al-Riwayah holds that any change, whether small or large, triggers sujud al-sahw. Sahib al-Hidayah restricts it to only a large amount (kathir).
The disagreement is over whether the amount matters.
2
Define kathir and qalil in this context
Kathir is the minimum amount of recitation that makes the prayer valid: according to Abu Hanifa, one verse; according to the Sahibayn, three verses. Qalil is less than that.
This definition is crucial to applying Sahib al-Hidayah's view.
3
Understand the distinction between imam and munfarid
The ruling of sajdah applies only to the imam, because jahr and ikhfa are obligations specific to congregational prayer (khasa'is al-jama'ah). The munfarid has full choice.
Even if the munfarid changes jahr/ikhfa, no sajdah is due.
4
Analyze the objection regarding sirri prayers
Some argue that ikhfa is wajib on the munfarid in sirri prayers, so omitting it should require sajdah. The response is that this view comes from Nawadir (rare narrations), not from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The authoritative position is based on Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that of Sahib al-Hidayah: sujud al-sahw is wajib only on the imam, and only when the amount changed is kathir.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

مطابق تو منفرد پر مخافت واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ دن کی نمازوں میں قرآت کے ساتھ اخفاء کرنا اس لئے واجب ہوا تھا تا کہ کفار کی طرف سے واقع ہونے والے مغالطہ کو دور کیا جائے اور کفار کا قرآت میں مغالطہ پیدا قرآت کرے یا جہر کے ساتھ کرے اور جب منفرد کو اختیار ہے تو ترک اخفاء کی وجہ سے اس پر سجدہ سہو واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume 2. There remains the matter: from how much lowering of voice in jahri prayer and from how much raising of voice in sirri prayer does sajdah become wajib? So regarding this, the narrations differ. Thus, in Zahir al-Riwayah, it is that in both cases, little and much are equal: i.e., whether one lowered the voice in jahri prayer or raised it in sirri prayer, whether a small amount or a large amount, in both cases sujud al-sahw will become wajib. The author of Hidaya said that the correct thing is that with the amount by which the prayer becomes valid, from its lowering and raising, in both cases sujud al-sahw: if one lowers that amount, then sujud al-sahw will become wajib, because it is not possible to avoid a small amount of jahr and ikhfa; however, it is possible to avoid a large amount. Therefore, the ruling of sahw is attached to a large amount, not a small amount. And the amount of recitation by which the prayer becomes valid is great, and less than that is little. As for what is the amount of 'ma yujiz bihi al-salah', there is disagreement about this: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is one verse, and according to the two companions (Sahibayn), it is three verses. The author of Hidaya says that in sirri prayers due to raising the voice and in jahri prayers due to lowering the voice, the ruling of obligation of sajdah applies to the imam, not to the munfarid: i.e., if the imam did so, sujud al-sahw will be wajib, and if the munfarid did so, sujud al-sahw will not be wajib. The proof is that jahr and ikhfa are among the specific characteristics of the congregation: i.e., jahr in jahri prayers and ikhfa in sirri prayers occur in the case of congregation. And if someone prays alone, he has choice: he may recite with jahr or with ikhfa. So when jahr or ikhfa is not wajib upon the munfarid, then sajdah also will not be wajib upon him for omitting it. And upon the imam, since it is wajib, therefore in the case of his omission, sajdah will be wajib upon the imam. Some people objected to this: that the obligation of jahr in jahri prayers being among the specific characteristics of the congregation is accepted, because in jahri prayers the munfarid has choice to recite with jahr or with ikhfa; but the obligation of ikhfa in sirri prayers being among the specific characteristics of the congregation is not accepted, because in sirri prayers, it is wajib upon the munfarid also to recite with ikhfa. Therefore, in sirri prayers, due to omitting ikhfa, sujud al-sahw should be wajib upon the munfarid also, whereas the author of Hidaya said that in this case also, sajdah is not wajib upon the munfarid. The answer is that this is a narration of Nawadir: i.e., the obligation of ikhfa upon the munfarid in these prayers is a narration of Nawadir, and according to Zahir al-Riwayah, ikhfa is not wajib upon the munfarid, because in daytime prayers, reciting with ikhfa was prescribed in order to remove the misunderstanding that used to occur from the disbelievers, and the disbelievers would create misunderstanding in recitation only when the prayer is performed publicly, and the prayer of a munfarid is not public. Therefore, ikhfa is not wajib upon him. Rather, he will have choice: in sirri prayers also, he may recite with ikhfa or with jahr. And when the munfarid has choice, sujud al-sahw will not be wajib upon him due to omitting ikhfa.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is from Ashraf al-Hidaya, a commentary on al-Hidaya, discussing the chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. It addresses the question: In jahri prayers (where recitation is aloud), when does lowering the voice (ikhfa') necessitate prostration of forgetfulness, and in sirri prayers (where recitation is silent), when does raising the voice (jahr) necessitate it? The author begins by stating that there are varying narrations. According to Zahir al-Riwayah (the core transmitted position of the Hanafi school), any amount of change—whether small or large—makes sajdah wajib in both cases. However, the author of Hidaya (al-Marghinani) corrects this by differentiating between small and large amounts based on the validity of prayer: the amount of recitation that makes the prayer valid (for sirri prayers, a minimum amount) is considered 'large' (kathir). If one makes ikhfa' in jahri prayer or jahr in sirri prayer in that large amount, then sajdah is wajib because it was avoidable; a small amount (less than that) is unavoidable and thus does not trigger sajdah. There is internal Hanafi disagreement on what constitutes the minimal valid recitation: Abu Hanifa says one verse, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say three verses. Next, the passage clarifies that the obligation of sajdah for this error applies only to the imam, not to the individual worshipper (munfarid). The reasoning is that jahr and ikhfa are obligations specific to congregational prayer (khasa'is al-jama'ah). In jahri prayers, the imam must recite aloud; in sirri prayers, he must recite silently. A munfarid, however, has the choice to recite aloud or silently in any prayer. Therefore, if he omits jahr or ikhfa, no sajdah is due. An objection is raised regarding sirri prayers: some argue that ikhfa is wajib upon the munfarid as well, so omitting it should necessitate sajdah. The response is that this view is from Nawadir (rare transmissions), not from Zahir al-Riwayah. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, ikhfa is not wajib upon the munfarid, because its original purpose (to avoid mockery by disbelievers) only applies to public congregational prayer. Hence, the munfarid retains choice, and no sajdah is due.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for certain errors in prayer.
جہر (jahr): Reciting aloud in prayer; required in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, and Jumu'ah for the imam.
اخفاء (ikhfa'): Reciting silently in prayer; required in Zuhr and Asr for the imam.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, representing the established transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or less-transmitted narrations from the founding imams, not part of the six core books.
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Sujud al-sahw is wajib on both imam and muqtadi.
B) Sujud al-sahw is wajib only on the imam.

D) Sujud al-sahw is wajib only on the muqtadi.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sujud al-sahw for an error in jahr/ikhfa is wajib only on the imam and only when the amount changed is considered kathir (the minimum for valid prayer).

Following the Imam in Sujud al-Sahw: The Hanafi Rule
Explains rule: imam's sahw makes sujud wajib on muqtadi as well.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on muqtadi's duty when the imam forgets, explain the supporting proof, and distinguish the Hanafi position from other schools.

Core Idea
The muqtadi follows the imam entirely; if the imam omits sujud, so does the muqtadi.

This lesson addresses a key fiqh question: When the imam forgets and must perform sujud al-sahw, does the muqtadi also have to perform it? And what if the imam neglects it? The Hanafi school gives a clear answer rooted in the principle of mutaba'ah (following the imam). We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the scholarly dispute with other madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (imam's forgetfulness causing sujud) and the hukm level for both imam and muqtadi.
The ruling is wajib for both, but conditional on the imam actually performing it.
2
Analyze the cause (sabab) and its effect
The forgetfulness occurring in the imam's prayer triggers the obligation of sujud. Because the muqtadi's prayer is subordinate, the same cause affects him.
The commentator uses the principle of subordination: the muqtadi's prayer follows the imam's in validity and completion.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The proof is based on the necessity of mutaba'ah: the muqtadi committed to follow the imam. Performing sujud alone would be mukhalafah (opposition), which is prohibited.
This is a talili (reasoning) argument, not a direct textual proof.
4
Consider the dispute with other schools
Imam al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that the muqtadi must perform sujud even if the imam does not, arguing that the obligation is independent.
The Hanafi response is that this would violate mutaba'ah.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi practice, the muqtadi does not perform sujud after the imam if the imam omitted it; in other schools, he does.
This difference affects congregational prayer practice.

Source Text

امام کے بھولنے سے امام اور مقتدی دونوں پر سجدہ سہو لازم ہے
(عنابی)
قال وسهو الامام يوجب على المؤتم السجود لتقرر السبب الموجب فى حق الاصل ولهذا يلزمه حكم الاقامة بنية الامام فان لم يسجد الامام لم يسجد المؤتم لانه لايصير مخالفا وما التزم الاداء الامتا بعا
رجمہ کیا کہ امام کا سہو کرنا مقتدی پر سجدہ واجب کرتا ہے کیونکہ اصل (امام) کے حق میں سجدہ واجب کرنے والا سبب منتظر رہو چکا ہے س بارے میں کی وجہ سے مقتدی پر اقامت کا حکم امام کی نیت سے لازم ہو جاتا ہے۔ پھر اگر امام نے مسجد نہیں کیا تو مقتدی بھی سجدہ نہ کرے کیونکہ مقتدی اپنے امام کا مخالف ہو جائے گا حالانکہ اس نے امام کی متابعت میں ادا کرنے کا التزام کیا تھا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ امام سے کوئی سہو ہو گیا تو سجدہ سہو امام پر بھی واجب ہوگا ، اور مقتدی پر بھی کیونکہ جو سب امام کے حق میں سجدہ سہو غدار کثیر کے ادب کرنے والا ہے وہ مقتدی کے حق میں بھی محقق ہو گیا ہے اس لئے کہ مقتدی نے صحت و فساد اور اقامت میں امام کی متابعت کو اپنے اوپر لازم کر لیا ہے پس امام کے سہو کی وجہ سے جو نقصان امام کی نماز میں ممکن (پیدا) ہو گیا ہے وہ نقصان مقتدی کی نماز میں بھی یقینا پیدا ہو آیت ہے اور کا اور جب امام اس نقصان کو پورا کرنے کے لئے سجدہ سہو کرے گا تو مقتدی پر بھی اپنی نماز میں پیدا ہونے والے نقصان کی تلافی کے لئے سجدہ سہو کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا ہے کہ چونکہ مقتدی کی نماز امام کی نماز کے تابع ہوتی ہے اس لئے اگر امام اور مقتدی سب مسافر ہوں اور م کے حق میں لیل یہ ہے کہ نماز کے دوران امام نے اقامت کی نیت کر لی تو تمام مقتدیوں کی فرض نماز چار رکعت ہو جائے گی اگر چہ مقتدیوں کی طرف سے نیت نہیں پائی گئی۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر سجدہ سہو واجب ہونے کے باوجود امام نے سجدہ سہو نہیں کیا تو مقتدی پر بھی سجدہ سہو کرنا واجب نہ ہو امام شافعی ، امام مالک اور امام احمد کے نزدیک مقتدی پر سجدہ کرنا واجب ہے۔ اگر چہ امام نے سجدہ نہیں کیا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر مقتدی نے بغیر امام کے سجدہ کے سجدہ سہو کیا تو امام کی مخالفت کرنا لازم آئے گا۔ حالانکہ التزام یہ کیا تھا کہ جماعت کے نام کے تابع ہو کر ادا کرے گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ التزام کیا تھا متابعت امام کا اور کی ہے مخالفت اور متابعت اور مخالفت کے درمیان منافات ہے
It is necessary that from the imam's forgetfulness, sujud al-sahw is wajib on both the imam and the muqtadi. (From al-`Inayah) He said: The forgetfulness of the imam obligates sajdah upon the muqtadi because the cause that obligates sajdah in the right of the origin (imam) is established, and for this reason the ruling of completing the prayer (iqamah) becomes incumbent upon him by the intention of the imam. So if the imam does not perform sajdah, the muqtadi also does not perform sajdah, because he would not be opposing, and he committed to perform the prayer by following. Explanation: If the imam forgets something, then sujud al-sahw is wajib upon the imam and also upon the muqtadi, because the cause that obligated sujud al-sahw in the right of the imam is also realized in the right of the muqtadi, because the muqtadi has made it necessary upon himself to follow the imam in validity and completion. So the deficiency that occurred in the imam's prayer due to the forgetfulness also occurs in the muqtadi's prayer. And when the imam performs sujud al-sahw to compensate for this deficiency, the muqtadi also must perform sujud al-sahw to compensate for the deficiency that occurred in his own prayer. The author of Hidaya said that because the muqtadi's prayer is subordinate to the imam's prayer, if both the imam and muqtadi are travelers and the imam makes the intention of iqamah during the prayer, then all the muqtadis' fard prayer becomes four rak'ats even if they did not intend it. Al-Quduri said: If sujud al-sahw becomes wajib but the imam does not perform it, then it is not wajib upon the muqtadi to perform sujud al-sahw either. Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad hold that it is wajib upon the muqtadi to perform sajdah even if the imam did not. Our proof is that if the muqtadi performs sujud al-sahw without the imam doing so, he will oppose the imam, whereas he had committed to follow the imam. In summary, he committed to follow the imam but he did opposition, and between following and opposition there is contradiction.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that when the imam commits forgetfulness (sahw) during prayer, sujud al-sahw becomes wajib upon both the imam and the muqtadi (follower). The author quotes the Arabic text from the matn: 'The forgetfulness of the imam obligates sujud upon the muqtadi because the cause is established concerning the origin (imam)...' The commentator explains that the muqtadi's prayer is connected to the imam's in terms of validity and completion (sihhah wa fasad wa iqamah). Therefore, any deficiency caused by the imam's forgetfulness also affects the muqtadi's prayer, and both must compensate by performing sujud al-sahw. However, if the imam deliberately omits the sujud al-sahw, the muqtadi should NOT perform it alone, because that would be opposing the imam, which violates the obligation of following. This is the Hanafi position. The passage then notes that Imam al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that the muqtadi must perform sujud even without the imam. The Hanafi response is that doing so would contradict the commitment to follow the imam. The commentator also mentions a principle from al-Quduri to support this: the muqtadi's prayer is subsidiary to the imam's.

Key Terms
مقتدی (muqtadi): The person following the imam in congregational prayer.
متتابعت (mutaba'ah): Following the imam in all actions of prayer; a wajib aspect of congregational prayer.
مخالفت (mukhalafah): Opposing or differing from the imam in an action of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the condition for the muqtadi's obligation to perform sujud al-sahw when the imam forgets?
A) The imam must have made a mistake that requires sujud.
B) The muqtadi must intend to follow the imam in all actions.
C) The imam must actually perform the sujud al-sahw.
D) The muqtadi must have also forgotten something.

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi's obligation to perform sujud al-sahw for the imam's forgetfulness is conditional on the imam actually performing it; otherwise, it must be omitted to preserve mutaba'ah.

Salah — Prayer

Sajdah al-Sahw: When the Imam Forgets – The Follower's Obligation
Ruling on sajdah al-sahw for imam and follower, with madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the follower's sajdah al-sahw when the imam forgets, and explain the Hanafi proof based on the principle of mutaba'ah.

Core Idea
If the imam omits sajdah al-sahw, the follower must not perform it alone; following the imam overrides individual correction.

This lesson examines a madhhab dispute: when the imam commits an error requiring sajdah al-sahw but fails to perform it, should the follower (muqtadi) perform the sajdah independently? The Hanafi school says no, because the follower's prayer is subordinate to the imam's. Other schools require the follower to perform it. We will analyse the evidence and practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
Determine the exact difference: whether the follower must perform sajdah when imam omits it.
2
State the Hanafi position
The follower does not perform sajdah because his prayer is subordinate.
Imam al-Quduri and al-Hidayah support this view.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The follower has committed to following the imam; independent action would be opposition (mukhalafah), which violates mutaba'ah.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the nature of congregational prayer.
4
Consider the opposing schools' view
Imams Shafi‘i, Maliki, and Hanbali hold that sajdah is individually obligatory and the follower must perform it even if the imam omits it.
Their proof: sajdah al-sahw rectifies a deficiency that is personal to each prayer.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In Hanafi school, the follower's prayer remains valid without sajdah; in other schools, the follower must perform sajdah or repeat the prayer.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (fruit of the difference).

Source Text

Chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. Translation: That the imam's forgetfulness makes sajdah obligatory on the follower because the cause that makes sajdah wajib on the imam has occurred, and due to this, the ruling of establishment (iqamah) becomes binding on the follower through the imam's intention. Then if the imam does not perform sajdah, the follower should also not perform sajdah because... Explanation of the issue: If the imam forgets, sajdah becomes wajib on the imam and also on the follower, because the deficiency that causes sajdah in the imam's prayer also occurs in the follower's prayer, since the follower has committed to following the imam in validity and invalidity and establishment. So when the imam performs sajdah to rectify the deficiency, the follower must also perform sajdah to rectify the deficiency in his own prayer. The author of al-Hidayah said that because the follower's prayer is subordinate to the imam's, if the imam and followers are all travelers and the imam intends to complete the prayer, all followers' prayers become four rak'ahs even if they did not intend it. Imam al-Quduri says: If sajdah is obligatory but the imam does not perform it, the follower is not obligated to do so. In case of omission: According to Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad, the follower must perform sajdah even if the imam does not. Our evidence: If the follower performs sajdah without the imam, he would be opposing the imam, whereas he committed to following. Result: He committed to following but did opposition, and between following and opposition there is contradiction. When opposition occurs, following is negated.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya (an Urdu commentary on al-Hidaya) addresses the ruling of sajdah al-sahw when the imam forgets. The primary rule is that if the imam commits an error that necessitates sajdah al-sahw, it becomes wajib on both the imam and the follower (muqtadi) because the follower's prayer is attached to the imam's. However, if the imam does not perform the sajdah, the follower must not perform it either, because doing so would constitute opposition to the imam, which violates the requisite of following. The passage then mentions the disagreement: Imams Shafi‘i, Maliki, and Hanbali hold that the follower must perform the sajdah even if the imam abandons it, because the sajdah is individually obligatory. The Hanafi response (dalil) is that the follower has committed to following the imam; performing sajdah alone would break that commitment. The follower's prayer is valid without the sajdah if the imam omits it. The principle is that the follower's prayer is subordinate (tabi‘) to the imam's; therefore, the follower cannot correct the imam's error independently.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.
مقتدی (muqtadi): The person praying behind the imam in congregation.
متابعت (mutaba'ah): Following the imam in actions of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if the imam forgets and does not perform sajdah al-sahw, what should the follower do?
A) Perform sajdah al-sahw alone after the imam's salam.
B) Not perform sajdah al-sahw, as the prayer is valid without it.
C) Repeat the entire prayer after the congregation ends.
D) Recite Subhan Allah to alert the imam.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the follower's prayer is subordinate to the imam's; therefore, if the imam omits sajdah al-sahw, the follower must not perform it independently.

Sajdah al-Sahw When the Follower Forgets
Ruling on sajdah when follower forgets

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the follower forgets a wajib element in congregational prayer and explain the legal reasoning why sajdah al-sahw is not performed.

Core Idea
Follower's forgetfulness does not trigger sajdah—preventing opposition or role inversion overrides compensation.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in congregational prayer: the follower (muqtadi) forgets a wajib element, such as omitting tashahhud in the first sitting. The Hanafi school rules that neither the imam nor the follower must perform sajdah al-sahw. The reasoning is based on preserving the integrity of the prayer's leadership structure, not on the nature of the omission itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The follower forgets a wajib action (e.g., first tashahhud) during congregational prayer. Determine who is affected: only the follower's prayer is deficient.
The imam's prayer remains sound; validity is assessed independently.
2
State the ruling
The Hanafi position: sajdah al-sahw is not required on the imam nor on the follower.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil aqli)
If the follower performed sajdah alone, he would oppose the imam (which is impermissible). If the imam followed him, the roles would invert (qalb mawdu‘), also impermissible.
Both options lead to prohibited outcomes; thus the default is no sajdah.
4
Understand the principle
The imam's prayer is not invalidated by the follower's error. Since the imam's prayer is sound, he has no need for sajdah; the follower cannot perform it alone because that would disrupt congregational harmony.
This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on maintaining the imam's authority.
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, no sajdah al-sahw is performed. The prayer continues and is valid without compensation. The follower should not repeat the prayer either, as the deficiency is minor and non-invalidating.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقتدی کی بھول سے امام اور مقتدی دونوں پر سجدہ سہو نہیں
فان سهى المؤتم لم يلزم الامام ولا المؤتم السجود لانه لو سجد وحده كان مخالفا لا مامه ولو تابعه الامام
رجمه پس اگر مقتدی نے سہو کیا تو نہ امام پر سجدہ کرنالازم ہے اور نہ مقتدی پر کیونکہ اگر تبا مقتدی کرے تو وہ اپنے امام کا مخالف ہوگا اور ئے اور منفرد کی ۔ اگر امام بھی اس کی متابعت کرے تو جو اصل تھا وہ تابع ہو جائے گا۔ فاء کے ساتھ
(جنایی)
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مقتدی سے نماز میں کوئی سہو ہو گیا مثلا قعدہ اولیٰ میں تشہد نہیں پڑھا تو اس کی وجہ سے نہ امام پر سجدہ سہو ازم ہوگا اور نہ مقتدی پر کیونکہ صحت و فساد کے اعتبار سے امام کی نماز مقتدی کی نماز پر یعنی نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے مقتدی کی نماز کے ناقص ہونے سے امام کی نماز ناقص نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور جب امام کی نماز میں کوئی نقص واقع نہیں ہوا تو اس پر سجدہ بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا اور تب امام پر لزمه حکم جدہ سہو واجب نہیں ہوا تو مقتدی پر بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اگر مقتدی پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہو تو وہ تنہا سجدہ کرے گا یا اس کا امام کی اس
کے ساتھ سجدہ کرے گا پہلی صورت میں امام کی مخالفت کرنا لازم آئے گا اور دوسری صورت میں قلب موضوع لازم آئے گا یعنی امام جواہر تھا وہ تابع ہو جائے گا اور مقتدی جو تابع تھا اصل ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ دونوں باتیں جائز نہیں ہیں ۔ یعنی مخالفت امام اور قلب موضوع ۔ پس جب یہ دونوں باتیں جائز نہیں ہیں تو مقتدی پر سجدہ سہو بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔
From the follower's forgetfulness, sajdah is not obligatory on the imam nor on the follower. Arabic: 'If the follower forgets, sajdah is not binding on the imam nor on the follower, because if he performs sajdah alone he would be opposing his imam, and if the imam follows him, the original would become the follower.' Translation: So if the follower forgets, it is not necessary for the imam to do sajdah nor for the follower, because if the follower does it alone, he will oppose his imam, and if the imam follows him, the original (imam) becomes follower. Explanation of the issue: If the follower forgets something in prayer, e.g., he did not recite tashahhud in the first sitting, then neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to perform sajdah, because in terms of validity and invalidity, the imam's prayer is not dependent on the follower's. Therefore, the follower's deficiency does not affect the imam's prayer. When the imam's prayer has no deficiency, sajdah is not wajib on him, and since sajdah is not wajib on the imam, it is not wajib on the follower either. Because if sajdah were wajib on the follower, he would either perform it alone (which would oppose the imam) or the imam would follow him (which would flip the roles: the imam becomes follower and the follower becomes imam). Both are impermissible. Hence, sajdah is not wajib on the follower.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage rules on the case when the follower (muqtadi) forgets an element of prayer, such as omitting the tashahhud in the first sitting. The key point is that the follower's forgetfulness does not necessitate sajdah al-sahw on either the imam or the follower. The reason is that the imam's prayer is not affected by the follower's mistakes; validity and invalidity are considered separately for each person. Since the imam's prayer remains sound, no sajdah is required from him. Moreover, if the follower were to perform sajdah alone, he would oppose the imam (which is forbidden). If the imam were to follow the follower in sajdah, it would invert the roles of imam and follower, which is also impermissible. Thus, no sajdah is required, and the prayer is valid as is.

Key Terms
قلب موضوع (qalb mawdu'): Inversion of roles: the imam becoming follower and the follower becoming imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the follower forgets to recite tashahhud in the first sitting, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Both imam and follower must perform sajdah al-sahw.
B) Only the follower must perform sajdah al-sahw.
C) Neither the imam nor the follower performs sajdah al-sahw.
D) The imam must perform sajdah al-sahw on behalf of the follower.

Key Takeaway
When only the follower forgets, no sajdah al-sahw is performed on anyone due to the prohibitions of opposing the imam and role inversion.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Forgetting the First Sitting: When to Return and Sajdah al-Sahw
Ruling on returning to first sitting if forgotten, based on proximity to sitting or standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on returning to the first sitting when forgotten, and determine whether sajdah al-sahw is required based on proximity.

Core Idea
If close to sitting, return and no sajdah; if close to standing, don't return and do sajdah.

Forgetting the first sitting (qada'ah ula) is a common occurrence in prayer. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on your physical position at the moment you remember. This ruling relies on the legal principle that something close to a thing takes its ruling (qarib al-shay'i ya'khudh hukmahu). Understanding this distinction helps avoid unnecessary sajdah al-sahw or incorrect repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The first sitting after two rak'ahs in three- or four-rak'ah prayers is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school. Forgetting it creates a need for remedy.
Wajib means omission requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw), not nullification of the prayer.
2
Determine the two scenarios based on proximity
The ruling depends on whether the person is closer to sitting (knees still on the ground) or closer to standing (knees lifted). The text uses 'closer to sitting' (aqrab ila al-qu'ud) and 'closer to standing' (aqrab ila al-qiyam).
3
Apply the principle of proximity
If closer to sitting, the person returns to sitting and recites tashahhud because 'something close takes its ruling' – he is treated as if he never stood up. If closer to standing, he does not return because he is like one already standing.
The maxim 'qarib al-shay'i ya'khudh hukmahu' is analogous to the area around a city taking the ruling of the city for Friday prayer.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf regarding sajdah al-sahw in the return case
Some scholars held that sajdah is required due to the delay in performing the wajib. The more correct (asahh) view is no sajdah, because the return effectively nullifies the omission.
The tarjih authority is the text itself, which declares the latter as 'asahh'.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi ruling
Final ruling: If closer to sitting, return and no sajdah. If closer to standing, continue and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
