Whoever forgets the first sitting and then remembers while he is closer to the sitting position, he returns and sits and recites tashahhud because something close to a thing takes its ruling. Then it was said he should perform sajdah for delay, but the more correct is that he does not perform sajdah, just as if he had not stood up. And if he is closer to standing, he does not return because he is like one standing, and he performs sajdah because he left a wajib. [Then Urdu translation and commentary.]
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a person forgets the first sitting (qada'ah ula) in a three- or four-rak'ah prayer and then remembers. The ruling depends on how far he has moved toward standing. If he is still close to sitting (i.e., has not lifted his knees from the ground), he should return to sitting, recite tashahhud, and then continue. In this case, the correct view (as per the text) is that no sajdah al-sahw is required, because the proximity rule gives the action the ruling of the intended action—he is considered as though he never stood up. If he is closer to standing (i.e., has lifted his knees), he should not return to sitting but continue standing for the next rak'ah. Here, sajdah al-sahw is wajib because he has omitted the wajib of the first sitting. The commentary provides an analogy: the area around a city (fina') takes the ruling of the city for Friday and Eid prayers. It also notes a difference of opinion: some say sajdah is needed in the first case due to delay, but the sahih (correct) view is no sajdah.

Key Terms
قعدہ اولی (qada'ah ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in prayers of three or four rak'ahs.
قریب الشیء یأخذ حکمه (qarib al-shay'i ya'khudh hukmahu): The legal principle that something close to a thing takes the ruling of that thing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Forgetting the Last Sitting and Standing for a Fifth Rak'ah
Ruling on forgetting the last sitting and standing for a fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for forgetting the last sitting and returning before prostrating, and identify the condition that determines validity.

Core Idea
If you stand for a fifth rak'ah but return before prostrating, the prayer is saved; the extra rak'ah is cancelled and sajdah al-sahw is required.

This lesson covers a specific error in salah: forgetting the final tashahhud and inadvertently standing for another rak'ah. The Hanafi school provides a clear procedure that preserves the validity of the prayer, provided the mistake is caught before the prostration of the extra rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The worshipper forgets the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in a four-rak'ah prayer and stands for a fifth rak'ah.
This is a common error.
2
Note the condition
The ruling depends on whether the worshipper has prostrated in the fifth rak'ah. The text says 'as long as he has not prostrated'.
Prostration completes a rak'ah.
3
Determine the required action
He must return to the sitting position immediately. This is obligatory to rectify the prayer.
4
Recognize the consequence
The fifth rak'ah is void (ilgha) because he returned before completing it. It is as if it never existed.
The principle: 'what is less than a rak'ah is subject to being void'.
5
Identify the compensation
He must perform sajdah al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) because he delayed the obligatory last sitting.
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib for this delay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ان سهى عن القعده الاخيره حتى قام الى الخامسة رجع الى القعدة مالم يسجد لان فيه اصلاح صلاته و امكنه ذلك لان مادون الركعة بمحل الرفض قال والغى الخامسة لانه رجع الى شنى محله قبلها فيرتفض وسجد للسهو لانه اخرواجبا
And if he forgets the last sitting until he stands for the fifth [rak'ah], he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated, because in it is the rectification of his prayer and it is possible for him, because what is less than a rak'ah is subject to being void. He said: he cancels the fifth because he returned to what was its place before, so it becomes void, and he performs sajdah for forgetfulness because he delayed an obligatory act.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This concise ruling covers a situation in a four-rak'ah prayer where the worshipper forgets the last sitting (tashahhud) and inadvertently stands up for a fifth rak'ah. The key point is that he must return to the sitting position before he performs the prostration of the fifth rak'ah, because he can still rectify his prayer. The fifth rak'ah is automatically void (cancelled) because it was added after the prayer was complete. After sitting and completing the prayer, he must perform sajdah al-sahw due to the delay in performing the obligatory last sitting. The condition is that he has not yet prostrated in the fifth rak'ah; if he has, the prayer becomes invalid.

Key Terms
الغاء (ilgha'): Cancellation of an extra rak'ah that was accidentally added.

Ruling on Forgetting the First Sitting (Qa'dah Ula)
Explains the ruling on forgetting the first sitting using the proximity principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetting the first sitting (qa'dah ula) and determine whether sajdah al-sahw is required based on the worshiper's proximity to sitting or standing.

Core Idea
Forgetting the first sitting requires sajdah only if you are closer to standing.

One of the common challenges in prayer is forgetting an obligatory element. The first sitting (qa'dah ula) is wajib in the Hanafi school. If forgotten, the worshiper must decide whether to return or continue, and whether to perform sajdah al-sahw. This ruling depends on a simple principle: proximity determines the legal status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or more rak'ahs is a wajib (obligatory, but not a rukn) in the Hanafi school.
Other schools may consider it sunnah or fard.
2
Recognize the two scenarios
When the worshiper forgets the first sitting, he may be physically closer to sitting (knees not lifted) or closer to standing (knees lifted or fully standing).
3
Apply the principle of proximity
The text states 'ما يقرب من الشئى يأخذ حكمه' — what is close to a thing takes its ruling. So if closer to sitting, he is legally considered to be still in the sitting position; if closer to standing, he is considered standing.
This principle is used in other areas too, e.g., the outskirts of a city take the ruling of the city for Friday prayer.
4
Determine the ruling for closer to sitting
If the worshiper is closer to sitting, he should return to the sitting and recite tashahhud. The correct view is that he does not need to perform sajdah al-sahw, because he never truly stood, so no delay occurred. Some scholars said sajdah is required, but the sahih opinion is no sajdah.
5
Determine the ruling for closer to standing
If the worshiper is closer to standing (or already standing), he should not return to sitting. He continues the prayer and performs sajdah al-sahw at the end, because he omitted a wajib intentionally (by forgetfulness).
Returning would mean leaving an obligatory (standing for the next rak'ah) for a wajib, which is not allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو

اشرف البدای شیر مار و مداری

يعدلان
ترجمہ اور جو شخص قعدہ اولیٰ کو بھول گیا پھر یاد کیا ایسی حالت میں کہ وہ حالت قعود سے زیادہ قریب ہو تو عود کرے اور قعدہ کرے اور تشہد پڑھے کیونکہ جو شے کسی چیز سے قریب ہو وہ اسی کا حکم لے لیتی ہے۔ پھر کہا گیا کہ تاخیر کی وجہ سے سجدہ سہو کرے۔ اور اصح یہ ہے کہ سجدہ نہ کرے جیسے وہ کھڑا ہی نہیں ہوا اور اگر قیام سے زیادہ قریب ہو تو قعدہ کی طرف عود نہ کرے کیونکہ یہ معنی قائم کے مانند ہے اور سجدہ سہو کرے کیونکہ اس نے واجب ترک کیا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ رباعی یا ثلاثی فرضوں میں اگر کسی نے قعدہ اولیٰ کو فراموش کر دیا اور پھر یاد آیا تو دوصورتیں ہیں یا تو قعود کے زیادہ قریب ہوگا بایں طور کہ اس نے اپنے گھٹنوں کو نہیں اٹھایا ہے اور یا قیام سے زیادہ قریب ہوگا بایں طور کہ اس نے اپنے گھٹنوں کو اٹھا لیا ہے پس اگر اول صورت ہے تو عود کر کے قعدہ کرے اور تشہد پڑھے ۔ کیونکہ قریب الشئی شئی کا حکم لے لیتی ہے۔ جیسے نماز جمعہ اور نماز عیدین کے حق میں فناء شہر کو شہر کا حکم حاصل ہے۔ رہی یہ بات کہ اس صورت میں سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا یا نہیں تو بعض حضرات کی رائے ہے کہ سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا کیونکہ قعدہ اولی جو واجب ہے اس میں تاخیر پائی گئی اور قول صحیح یہ ہے کہ سجدہ واجب نہیں ہوا ہے اس لئے کہ جب قریب اشی کو شے کا حکم دے دیا گیا تو گویا وہ کھڑا ہی نہیں ہوا اور جب قعدہ اولی کو چھوڑ کر قیام متحقق نہیں ہوا تو قعدہ اولیٰ میں تا خیر بھی نہیں پائی گئی اور جب تا خیر نہیں پائی گئی تو سجدہ سہو بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر دوسری صورت ہے تو یہ شخص قعدہ کی طرف نہ لوٹے بلکہ تیسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو جائے کیونکہ ابھی یہ ضابطہ گزرا ہے کہ قریب اللے کو شے کا درجہ دے دیا جاتا ہے پس جب یہ شخص قیام سے قریب تر ہے تو معنی قائم ہی کے مرتبہ میں ہے اور قائم کے لئے قعدہ اولی کے واسطے لوٹنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ تیسری رکعت کا قیام فرض ہے اور قعدہ اولیٰ واجب ہے اور واجب کی وجہ سے فرض کو چھوڑ نا درست نہیں ہے البتہ اس صورت میں سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے واجب یعنی قعدہ اولیٰ کو ترک کر دیا ہے۔ اور اگر کھڑے ہونے کے قریب ہے کھڑا ہو جائے اور سجدہ سہو کرے
Chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. 238. Ashraf al-Biday [book title]. ... He will prostrate with... In the first case opposing the imam becomes necessary, and in the second case inversion of the subject becomes necessary, i.e., the imam who was the follower would become the leader and the muqtadi who was the follower would become the origin. And both these things are not permissible, i.e., opposing the imam and inversion of the subject. So when both these things are not permissible, then sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory upon the muqtadi. He forgot the first sitting then remembered: if he is close to sitting, he should sit and perform sajdah al-sahw or not? And whoever forgets the first sitting, then remembers while he is closer to the state of sitting, he returns and sits and recites tashahhud, because what is close to a thing takes its ruling. Then it is said he prostrates for forgetfulness due to delay, and the correct is that he does not prostrate just as if he had not stood. And if he is closer to standing, he does not return to the meaning? and he prostrates for forgetfulness because he left an obligatory [act]. Translation: And the person who forgot the first sitting, then remembered in a state where he is closer to the state of sitting, then he returns and sits and recites tashahhud, because what is close to a thing takes its ruling. Then it was said that due to delay he should perform sajdah al-sahw. And the correct is that he does not prostrate, just as if he had not stood. And if he is closer to standing, then he should not return to sitting, because this is like one who is standing, and he prostrates for forgetfulness because he left an obligatory [act]. Explanation: The issue is that in four- or three-cycle obligatory prayers, if someone forgets the first sitting and then remembers, there are two cases: either he is closer to sitting, meaning he has not lifted his knees, or he is closer to standing, meaning he has lifted his knees. If the first case, he returns and sits and recites tashahhud, because what is close to a thing takes its ruling, like the open space of a city takes the ruling of the city regarding Friday prayer and Eid prayer. As for whether sajdah al-sahw is obligatory in this case, some scholars hold that sajdah al-sahw is obligatory because there is a delay in the obligatory first sitting. The correct opinion is that sajdah is not obligatory, because when the near thing is given the ruling of the thing, it is as if he never stood. And when leaving the first sitting and standing did not actually occur, there is no delay in the first sitting. And when there is no delay, sajdah al-sahw is not obligatory. And if the second case, this person should not return to sitting but should stand for the third rak'ah, because we have already passed the principle that what is near a thing is given its ruling. So when this person is closer to standing, he is in the status of one standing, and for one standing it is not permissible to return for the first sitting, because standing for the third rak'ah is obligatory and the first sitting is wajib, and it is not correct to leave an obligatory due to a wajib. However, in this case, sajdah al-sahw becomes obligatory because he left a wajib, i.e., the first sitting. And if he is close to standing, he should stand and perform sajdah al-sahw.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the chapter on Sajdah al-Sahw, expanded by the commentator. It begins with a brief note about the muqtadi: if following an imam who makes a mistake, the muqtadi should not perform sajdah al-sahw if doing so would require opposing the imam or inverting the leadership. Then the main issue: forgetting the first sitting (qad'ah ula) in a three- or four-rak'ah prayer. The ruling distinguishes two situations based on proximity to sitting or standing. If the worshiper is closer to sitting (having not lifted his knees from the ground), he should return and perform the sitting and tashahhud. The correct view is that he does not need to perform sajdah al-sahw because, by the principle that what is close to a thing takes its ruling, he is considered as if he never stood, so there was no delay. If he is closer to standing (having lifted his knees), he should not return because his intention is towards standing, and the standing for the next rak'ah is obligatory (fard) while the first sitting is only wajib; one cannot leave an obligatory for a wajib. In this case, he must perform sajdah al-sahw for leaving the wajib. The commentary also explains the analogy: just as the outskirts of a city take the ruling of the city for Friday prayer, so nearness to sitting takes the ruling of sitting. The dispute among scholars is noted: some say sajdah is required in the first case due to delay, but the sahih view is that it is not.

Key Terms
قعدہ اولیٰ (qa'dah ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or more rak'ahs, during which tashahhud is recited.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness, such as delaying or omitting a wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah prayer, a worshiper forgets the first sitting and is about to stand up (has lifted his knees). What should he do?
A) Return to the first sitting and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end.
B) Continue standing and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end.
C) Return to the first sitting without sajdah al-sahw.
D) Continue standing and do not perform sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
The first sitting is wajib; if forgotten, return only if closer to sitting, and no sajdah; if closer to standing, continue and perform sajdah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Forgetting the Last Sitting and Standing for an Extra Rak'ah
Inter-madhhab dispute with ruling details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for forgetting the last sitting (before and after sajdah of the extra rak'ah) and explain the intra- and inter-madhhab disputes.

Core Idea
If you stand for a fifth rak'ah and haven't prostrated, return; if you already prostrated, your fard becomes nafl.

This lesson covers a common scenario of forgetfulness in salah: forgetting the last sitting and standing for an extra rak'ah. The Hanafi school distinguishes between before and after performing the sajdah of that extra rak'ah. Additionally, there is an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, and an inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two branches
The passage divides based on whether the worshiper has performed the sajdah of the extra rak'ah. Note the key moment: before sajdah vs. after sajdah.
The text says 'malam yasjud' (as long as he has not prostrated).
2
Ruling before sajdah of extra rak'ah
State that the worshiper should return to the last sitting, cancel the extra rak'ah (laghw), and then perform sajdah al-sahw for delaying the wajib. Reason: less than a full rak'ah (without sajdah) can be abandoned.
The principle: 'ma dun al-rak'ati bi-mahalli al-rafd' (less than a rak'ah is subject to abandonment).
3
Ruling after sajdah of extra rak'ah
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the fard prayer becomes invalid (batil) and transforms into nafl because the extra rak'ah with a sajdah constitutes a valid unit of prayer, overriding the intention for fard.
Imam Muhammad holds that the prayer remains fard and only sajdah al-sahw is required.
4
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify that Imam Muhammad disagrees: he says the fard remains valid after performing sajdah al-sahw. The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
The text says 'khilafan li-Muhammad' (contrary to Muhammad).
5
Inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the prayer does not become invalid; the extra rak'ah is an error that can be cancelled without affecting the fard. The Hanafi response is that the sajdah establishes the extra unit as a valid prayer, causing the intention to shift to nafl.
The thamarah (practical difference): Hanafis repeat the fard; Shafi'is pray normally with sajdah al-sahw.

مدة
بائل پانچویں رکعت سے پہلے ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو شخص افعال صلوۃ میں سے کسی فعل سے ایسی چیز کی طرف لوٹا جس کا محل اس. پہلے ہے تو وہ فعل مرجوع عنہ (جس سے رجوع کیا گیا) لغو ہو جاتا ہے۔ مثلاً کوئی شخص تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھا پھر یاد آیا کہ نماز کا سجدہ نہیں یا سجدہ تلاوت نہیں کیا پھر اس نے یہ فوت شدہ سجدہ کیا تو سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے کا قعدہ لغو ہو گیا ہے۔ کیو نہک سجدہ کامل قعدہ اخیرہ سے نرم ہے۔ بہر حال جب پانچویں رکعت چھوڑ کر قعدہ اخیرہ کی طرف لوٹ آیا تو سجدہ سہو کرنا واجب ہو گیا کیونکہ اس صورت میں تا خیر فرض گیا ہے اور تا خیر واجب بھی ، تا خیر فرض تو اس لئے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ میں تاخیر ہوگئی ہے اور قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے اور تاخیر واجب اس لئے کہ لفظ
رام واجب ہے وہ مؤخر ہو گیا ہے۔ ہدایہ کی عبارت لانه اخر واجبا میں لفظ واجب سے واجب کے معروف معنی بھی مراد ہو سکتے ہیں اور واجب قطعی یعنی فرض بھی دہو سکتا ہے۔ پہلے معنی مراد لینے کی صورت میں لفظ سلام کی تاخیر مراد ہوگی اور دوسرے معنی مراد لینے میں قعدہ اخیرہ کی تاخیر مراد ہوگی ۔
قعدہ اخیرہ بھول کر پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ بھی کر لیا تو فرض ہو گئے یا باطل ہیں، اقوال فقہاء
ان قيد الخامسة بسجدة بطل فرضه عندنا خلافا للشافعي لانه استحكم شروعه في النافلة قبل اكمال كان المكتوبة ومن ضرورته خروجه عن الفرض وهذا لان الركعة بسجدة واحدة صلوة حقيقة حتى حنت بها في يمينه لا يصلى وتحولت صلاته نفلا عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف خلافا لمحمد على مامر جمہ اور اگر اس نے پانچویں رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کیا تو ہمارے نزدیک اس کا فرض باطل ہو گیا۔ امام شافعی کا اس میں اختلاف اس لئے کہ فرض کے ارکان پورے کرنے سے پہلے اس کا نفل کو شروع کر نا مستحکم ہو گیا اور اس کے لئے فرض سے نکلنا لا زم ہے اور یہ اس ا کہ رکعت تو ایک سجدہ کے ساتھ در حقیقت نماز ہے حتی کہ اگر لا یصلی کی قسم کھائی ہو تو ایک رکعت ایک سجدہ کے ساتھ پڑھنے
And if he forgets the last sitting until he stands for the fifth, he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated, because in that is correction of his prayer and it is possible for him, because less than a rak'ah is subject to abandonment. He said: and he cancels the fifth because he returned to something whose place is before it, so it is invalidated, and he prostrates for forgetfulness because he delayed an obligatory. [Urdu commentary follows, explaining the ruling, the principle that less than a rak'ah is not prayer, the cancellation of the extra rak'ah, and the obligation of sajdah al-sahw for delay. Then the issue of tying the fifth rak'ah with a sajdah: if he ties the fifth with a sajdah, his fard prayer is invalidated according to us (Hanafis), contrary to al-Shafi'i, because his commencement of the supererogatory prayer became established before completing the obligatory, and its necessity is his exit from the fard. This is because a rak'ah with a single sajdah is actually prayer, such that if he swears an oath 'I will not pray', and he prays one rak'ah with one sajdah, he is not guilty of breaking the oath. And his prayer transforms into nafl according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on forgetting the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in a four-rak'ah prayer and standing for a fifth rak'ah. The Hanafi ruling: before performing the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah, the worshiper should return to the last sitting, because less than a full rak'ah (without sajdah) can be abandoned. The extra rak'ah is then cancelled, and sajdah al-sahw is required for delaying the last sitting (or the salam, depending on interpretation). The commentary clarifies that this applies analogously to three- and two-rak'ah prayers. Then a further issue: if the worshiper actually performs the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah (i.e., completes a full rak'ah), according to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the fard prayer becomes invalid (batil) because the intention shifts to nafl. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that the prayer is not invalidated. The Hanafi argument is that once the extra rak'ah is tied with a sajdah, it constitutes a valid prayer unit (rak'ah), and since the intention was for fard, the prayer transforms into nafl, thereby invalidating the original fard. The text also notes that Imam Muhammad disagrees with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on this transformation. The commentator explains the principle that less than a rak'ah is not considered prayer, and gives the example of an oath: if one swears not to pray and performs less than a rak'ah, he is not guilty. The passage also discusses the cancellation of the extra unit when returning to sitting.

Key Terms
قعدہ اخیرہ (qa'dah akhirah): The final sitting after the last rak'ah, during which tashahhud and salawat are recited, and the prayer ends with salam.
لغو (laghw): To cancel or nullify an action, meaning the extra rak'ah is disregarded and treated as if it never occurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah fard prayer, the worshiper forgets the last sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah. He then performs the sajdah of the fifth rak'ah before remembering. According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what is the ruling?
A) He should return to the last sitting and the prayer is valid.
B) The fard prayer becomes invalid (batil) and transforms into nafl.
C) He continues the prayer as fard with an extra rak'ah and performs sajdah al-sahw.
D) He must repeat the entire prayer from the beginning without any action.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on forgetting the last sitting depends on whether you have performed the sajdah of the extra rak'ah: before sajdah, return; after sajdah, the fard becomes nafl according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
